1801 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Lipshutz v. Shantha


Nos. 54807, 54808, 54809, 54810, 54811, 54812, 54813, 54815, 54816, 54979


Court of Appeals of Georgia


144 Ga. App. 196; 240 S.E.2d 738; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2633


November 2, 1977, Argued  
November 10, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for eviction; paying uncontested payments. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Beasley.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nine tenants, sought an interlocutory appeal from the decision of the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which granted appellee landlord writs of possession to rental property in the landlord's dispossessory proceedings pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. §§ 61-301 and 61-302 when the tenants failed to pay past due rent into the trial court as required under Ga. Code Ann. § 304.


OVERVIEW: The tenants had paid into the trial court approximately two-thirds of the rent and the other third was receipts representing repairs made by the tenants. The landlord contended that the receipts were not payment of rent under § 61-304. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the legislative history unequivocally showed that the general assembly in giving the tenants the right to remain in possession during the pendency of a dispossessory proceeding by tendering the payment of rent into the trial court intended "rent" to mean money. The house bill had allowed a tenant to tender money or an accounting of out-of-pocket expenditures due the landlord's alleged failure to make repairs. The senate deleted the provision that allowed an accounting and the house agreed with the change. Thus, the court would not subvert the legislative will by a construction contrary to its express meaning. Whether or not the tenants were required to recoup or set off the amounts they paid for repairs will be determined by a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the landlord in the landlord's dispossessory proceedings against the tenants for failure to pay rent.

 

1802 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Eubanks v. State


No. 53495


Court of Appeals of Georgia


144 Ga. App. 152; 241 S.E.2d 6; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2617


February 16, 1977, Submitted  
November 9, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing December 1, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Theft by conversion. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge Whalen.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Upson Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of theft by conversion, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 28-1808, as charged by the State of Georgia and sentenced him to ten years, to be served on probation with payment of a fine and restitution. The superior court had overruled defendant's motion for a directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant had accepted money from homeowners to build a room on their home within a certain time period. The room was not completed when promised and the homeowners learned that there were materialmen's liens outstanding for building supplies for which defendant had not paid. The State did not present evidence to show how much of the money defendant had actually spent on the construction. On appeal, the court held that the conviction must be reversed because the evidence was insufficient to show how much money defendant had spent on the project and how much, if any, he had converted. The court noted that this impermissibly placed the burden on defendant to show that he had not converted the money. The court held that the probationary portion of defendant's sentence was improper because the evidence was insufficient to support the amount of restitution required. The court rejected defendant's claim that Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1808 was void, or unconstitutional as applied to this case. Further, the court noted that the State's error in listing the applicable statute as Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1803 rather than § 26-1808 had previously been found to be harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the superior court, which had convicted defendant of theft by conversion as charged by the State. The court remanded for a new trial.

 

1803 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. 54486


Court of Appeals of Georgia


144 Ga. App. 130; 240 S.E.2d 890; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2608


September 15, 1977, Submitted  
November 4, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cruelty to children. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Holt.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) of cruelty to children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court admitted testimony of the mother of an intended witness who was eight years old because the child could not appreciate the oath. The trial court admitted the testimony as part of the res gestae. The court found that the statement by the child to her mother, almost two days after the event, was not a spontaneous declaration and because the statements of the child were a narrative of an earlier event, it was inadmissible hearsay. However, the court found that the admission of the statement was not harmful error because the testimony was cumulative of other evidence. Defendant challenged his conviction cruelty to children where the indictment against him charged him with aggravated assault. The court found that the crime of cruelty to children was a lesser included offense to aggravated assault and, thus, the indictment was a sufficient basis for the conviction. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict and affirmed it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of cruelty to children.

 

1804 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Henson v. Columbus Bank & Trust Co.


No. 54482


Court of Appeals of Georgia


144 Ga. App. 80; 240 S.E.2d 284; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2592


September 7, 1977, Argued  
November 2, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 22, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Usury, etc. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Followill.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borrower challenged the order of the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee lender's motion to dismiss his complaint with prejudice. The complaint was based on the Truth in Lending Act, collection of usurious interest, and a breach of contract, and had been previously dismissed without prejudice from a federal court and refiled under the renew statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 3-808.


OVERVIEW: The lender made loans to the borrower, and the borrower paid the prime rate each quarter on the interest without regard to the interest listed on the notes. When the borrower refused to make further interest payments in excess of the interest stated on the note, the lender brought suit, and the borrower paid off the notes without filing an answer. The lender dismissed the suit. The borrower filed suit against the lender in federal court. The federal court dismissed the suit without prejudice, and the borrower refiled the suit in the superior court. The lender's motion to dismiss was granted by the superior court. The borrower appealed. The court affirmed. The court rejected the borrower's assertion of the coercive force of the lender, because it was not raised at the superior court level. The court found that the borrower's voluntary payments prevented recovery. The court found that the expiration of the one-year statute of limitations under Ga. Code Ann. §§ 3-1004, 57-115 and 15 U.S.C.S. § 1640 ran before the action was filed in superior court. The court found the renewal statute was inapplicable because the renewal statute applied only to actions commenced in the state courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which dismissed the borrower's action interest against the lender for violations of the Truth in Lending Act, breach of contract, and collection of usurious.

 

1805 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Baranan v. State Board of Nursing Home Adm'rs


No. 54513


Court of Appeals of Georgia


143 Ga. App. 605; 239 S.E.2d 533; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2427


September 8, 1977, Submitted  
October 5, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: License renewal. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home administrator sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee State Board of Nursing Home Administrators' motion for summary judgment dismissing the nursing home administrator's complaint for a declaration that the Board rules regarding continuing education were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's license was not renewed because he failed to obtain continuing education requirements. The administrator filed a petition in the superior court that sought a declaratory judgment that certain portions of Rule 393-5 of the rules of the Georgia State Board of Nursing Home Administrators were unconstitutional and void. The superior court granted the Board's motion for summary judgment dismissing the administrator's complaint for a declaratory judgment. The superior court's judgment was affirmed. The court held that the state had the inherent police power to place restrictions on a licensee as was necessary for the welfare and safety of society. The court held that the rule requiring mandatory continuing education was reasonable. Further, the administrator was not denied due process and equal protection based on the selections of the Board members where no conflict of interest existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment granting the Board's motion for summary judgment dismissing the nursing home administrator's complaint.

 

1806 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Powers v. Cordele


No. 54416


Court of Appeals of Georgia


143 Ga. App. 363; 238 S.E.2d 721; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2320


September 7, 1977, Argued  
September 20, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge Gregory.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and son, sought review of an order from the Crisp Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their complaint against appellee city seeking to declare void a zoning regulation adopted by the city and an ordinance passed by the city commission purporting to annex certain property owned by the father and son as tenants in common.


OVERVIEW: The father wrote a letter to the city requesting that the property be brought into the city as soon as possible. The city adopted an ordinance annexing the property by expanding the city limits to include the tract. The son learned of the application shortly thereafter but made no objection. The father and son then sought a building permit from the city to construct a building on the unimproved parcel, which was first denied, but subsequently granted. The city attempted to appeal on the ground that the property was improperly annexed. The father and son then filed an action seeking to declare the purported annexation void, which was denied by the trial court. On appeal, the court held that because the father held himself out to represent both himself and the son and the son, through his silence, ratified the request, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying their claim. The annexation of their property to the city was proper and the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court.

 

1807 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. 53998


Court of Appeals of Georgia


143 Ga. App. 88; 237 S.E.2d 533; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2195


May 23, 1977, Argued  
July 15, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 28, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Defiling a flag. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Alexander.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a decision of the State Court of Fulton County (Georgia) that sustained defendant's demurrer to an accusation against him for defiling the flag of the United States.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of defiling the flag by displaying in a shop window a photograph that showed a partially nude male touching a flag of the United States on the rectum area of his nude buttock. Defendant demurred on the grounds that the accusation did not allege an offense; that the charge did not sufficiently inform him of the nature of the offense; and that O.C.G.A. § 26-2803 was unconstitutional. The trial court sustained the demurrer on the basis that the statute was silent as to photographs and the trial court concluded that the statute as written did not cover photographs of flags. The trial court specifically did not rule on the constitutionality of the statute. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court judgment. The court noted that the statute did not define the word defile but it was an ordinary one and had to be given its ordinary signification. Defile was defined by Webster as to sully, to tarnish, to dishonor. The court held that deliberately inserting the national ensign into the anal area of the human anatomy fell within the definition of the term defile and violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

1808 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Storey v. Seffelaar & Looyen, Inc.


No. 54070


Court of Appeals of Georgia


142 Ga. App. 873; 237 S.E.2d 236; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2157


May 24, 1977, Argued  
July 14, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on contract. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Camp.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee appealed a judgment of the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which granted defendant nonresident former employer's motion to dismiss the former employee's action for lack of personal jurisdiction. The former employee filed an action against the nonresident former employer to recover damages for breach of a personal services contract between the parties.


OVERVIEW: The nonresident former employer hired the former employee as a salesman. The former employee sought to recover damages against the nonresident former employer in an action for breach of contract. The nonresident former employer filed a motion to dismiss the former employee's action for lack of personal jurisdiction. The nonresident former employer alleged that the evidence in the record showed that the former employee failed to obtain personal jurisdiction over the nonresident former employer. The lower court held that the parties' alleged employment contract was negotiated and signed in another state. The lower court further held that the exercise of extraterritorial jurisdiction over the nonresident former employer was unconstitutional. The lower court stated that the former employee's purposeful activity within this state in the performance of the parties' contract was so limited that the exercise of extraterritorial jurisdiction over the nonresident former employer offended notions of fair play and justice. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the lower court finding was authorized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the nonresident former employer's motion to dismiss the former employee's action to recover damages for breach of a personal services contract between the parties for lack of personal jurisdiction.

 

1809 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. 53821


Court of Appeals of Georgia


142 Ga. App. 705; 237 S.E.2d 1; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 1720


May 9, 1977, Argued  
June 10, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 1, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to suppress. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Bullard.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence obtained upon execution of a search warrant issued by a Justice of the Peace who was not neutral by virtue of his financial interest in the decision of whether to issue the warrant.


OVERVIEW: Under Ga. Code Ann. § 24-1601, the Justice of the Peace received a $ 5 fee for issuing the search warrant which resulted in the discovery of the evidence at issue. The Justice was not entitled to collect a fee for refusing to issue the warrant. The court agreed that the search warrant was not executed by the required "neutral and detached magistrate" because the Justice of the Peace's financial welfare was enhanced by positive action and would not have been enhanced by negative action. As such, the issuance of the search warrant effected a violation of defendant's Fourth and Fourteenth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress.

 

1810 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bickford v. Nolen


No. 53446


Court of Appeals of Georgia


142 Ga. App. 256; 235 S.E.2d 743; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 1566


February 4, 1977, Argued  
April 27, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 10, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant passenger sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which refused to grant a new trial on the jury's verdict for appellee driver in the passenger's negligence action to recover for injuries sustained when the convertible automobile, in which the parties were riding, went out of control and overturned.


OVERVIEW: At trial on the passenger's claims, the trial judge instructed the jury on the judicially-created guest rule that a driver was not liable to a guest in his vehicle unless the driver was guilty of gross negligence. The jury returned a verdict for the driver. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court agreed with the passenger's constitutional challenge to the guest rule. The court recited the judicial history of the guest rule. The rationale of the promotion of hospitality by insulation of the drivers from lawsuits by guests was no longer applicable because the Georgia Motor Vehicle Accident Reparations Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 56-3401b et seq., required mandatory minimum insurance that protected drivers. The guest rule only served to protect insurance companies. The justification that asserted that the guest rule prevented collusive lawsuits by drivers and guests was without merit because the common law guest rule was overinclusive. However, the court was not authorized to overturn a common law rule sustained by the state supreme court. The court held that the four contested jury instructions were proper and that there was adequate evidence to support the verdict in favor of the driver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the driver in the passenger's action to recover for the driver's negligence that resulted in her injuries.

 

1811 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hamilton Mortg. Corp. v. Bowles


No. 53302


Court of Appeals of Georgia


142 Ga. App. 882; 237 S.E.2d 198; 1977 Ga. App. LEXIS 2163


January 19, 1977, Argued  
April 11, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Judgment Adhered to on Rehearing June 21, 1977. Rehearing Denied July 15, 1977. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Confirmation of sale. Forsyth Superior Court. Before Judge Burtz.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lender sought review of a judgment from the Forsyth Superior Court (Georgia), which denied confirmation of the sale of property after the lender declared the loan to appellee partnership to be in default and sold the property involved pursuant to the secured loan.


OVERVIEW: A loan to the partnership to develop land was secured by a deed. The lender declared the loan to be in default and an undivided 98.77 percent interest in the deed to secure debt was assigned three days later. The property was advertised for sale under a power of sale contained in the deed to secure debt, and the property was sold under power. An application for confirmation of the sale was filed. The partners answered, raising several defenses including estoppel, novation, increase of risk, failure of consideration, failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, failure to sell at the true value and improper venue due to the lender's failure to assert the application for confirmation in their action for equitable relief and damages arising from the same transaction. Confirmation was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the duty of the court was to test the fairness of the technical procedure of the actual sale and to insure that the sale had bought at least the true market value of the property pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 67-1503 et seq. Because there was an issue of whether or not a default had occurred, the trial court had properly denied the confirmation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.

1814 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Zeiger v. State


No. 53077


Court of Appeals of Georgia


140 Ga. App. 610; 231 S.E.2d 494; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 1581


November 2, 1976, Submitted  
November 18, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1976. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ordinance violation. Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Cheeley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Gwinnett State Court (Georgia), which convicted him of a misdemeanor under O.C.G.A. § 68A-507(b) relating to uniform rules of the road.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was selling or giving away newspapers or asking donations from passing motorists. Defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor under O.C.G.A. § 68A-507(b) relating to uniform rules of the road. Defendant argued that the statute, as applied to the facts of the case, unlawfully denied his personal rights, especially freedom of speech, in contravention of the First and Fourteenth Amendment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that even where municipal or state property was open to the public generally, the exercise of First Amendment rights could be regulated so as to prevent interference with the use to which the property was ordinarily put by the State. The court held that defendant's act of choosing the paved area of a highway for a place to stand and transact his business, no matter how laudable the business itself might have been, was certainly a privilege rather than a right, and therefore subject to regulation by the state. The court held that the mere fact that defendant was exercising his First Amendment rights did not shield him from the observance of normal traffic regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for a misdemeanor relating to uniform rules of the road.

 

1815 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


McKenzey v. State


No. 52984


Court of Appeals of Georgia


140 Ga. App. 402; 231 S.E.2d 149; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 1495


October 13, 1976, Submitted  
November 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Escape. Habersham Superior Court. Before Judge Gunter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Habersham Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of escape from a state penitentiary.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had before it records emanating from the director of corrections transferring defendant as a sentenced prisoner from one penal institution to another. It also had copies of sentences imposed as a result of felony convictions. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting a copy of an administrative order showing his transfer as a prisoner without further proof that he was originally committed as the result of a lawful conviction, including a sentence to confinement. He complained that the trial court erred in not directing a verdict of acquittal. The court upheld the conviction. There was ample evidence supporting the trial court's denial of the motion for a directed verdict of acquittal. O.C.G.A. § 77-309(b) provided that persons convicted of a felony and sentenced to serve time in a penal institution were committed to the custody of the director, who was to designate the place of confinement. The director also had the sole authority to transfer prisoners between correctional institutions. Thus, the trial court had before it evidence that defendant was a sentenced prisoner committed to the director for appropriate incarceration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Madsen v. Memorial Sales of Georgia, Inc.

1817 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Watts v. Six Flags Over Georgia, Inc.


No. 52666


Court of Appeals of Georgia


140 Ga. App. 106; 230 S.E.2d 34; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 1363


September 21, 1976, Argued  
September 28, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 22, 1976. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Malicious prosecution. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brothers sought review of a judgment and order of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which directed a verdict in favor of appellee amusement park and which denied the brothers' motion for new trial in the suit that they filed against the park in which they alleged malicious arrest, malicious prosecution, false imprisonment, assault, and battery.


OVERVIEW: Two brothers were denied entrance to the park because they were not wearing shirts. They cursed and then remained near the park entrance. Later, one brother entered the park, claiming that he needed to see the time. A security guard accosted him, and after a scuffle, the brothers left the park but were chased by security guards. They were arrested and charged with battery, trespass, and use of abusive language. Upon their acquittal, they filed suit against the park. The trial court directed a verdict in favor of the park when the brothers failed to produce a transcript of their criminal trial and dismissed the brothers' motion for new trial as abandoned. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by refusing to admit the transcript into evidence, as it was never offered in evidence because the brothers were unable to get a copy of it. The court also held that the motion for new trial was properly dismissed because the brothers' attorney said that he would not argue the motion orally and requested, by letter, that the trial court grant a continuance so that he could obtain the transcript or that the trial court deny his motion so that he could perfect an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the park and affirmed the order denying the brothers' motion for new trial.

1819 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Philyaw v. Fulton Nat'l Bank


No. 52100


Court of Appeals of Georgia


139 Ga. App. 28; 227 S.E.2d 811; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 1665; 20 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 553


April 8, 1976, Argued  
May 17, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tidwell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor filed an action against appellee lender to recover the value of an automobile that he claimed the lender improperly repossessed. The debtor challenged an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of the lender.


OVERVIEW: The debtor defaulted on a loan that was secured by his automobile. The lender informed the debtor of the default. The debtor made a partial payment and the lender repossessed his vehicle. The debtor filed an action for damages. The trial court granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of the lender. The court affirmed. The court refused to certified the debtor's argument that the possession statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 109A-9-503 (1962) was unconstitutional. The court found that the a determination of the issue could be reached a different way. The court held that it would not address the issue because the trial court had not done so. Finally, the court found that the partial payment did not cure the default. There was an acceleration clause in the note allowing the lender to request full payment of the note after the debtor defaulted. The lender requested said payment and the debtor failed to make it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of the lender.

 

1820 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


C.J. v. State


No. 51749


Court of Appeals of Georgia


138 Ga. App. 710; 227 S.E.2d 445; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2295


February 3, 1976, Submitted  
May 10, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Burglary. Fulton Juvenile Court. Before Judge Dillon.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile offender challenged the judgment of the Fulton Juvenile Court (Georgia) adjudicating him a delinquent for committing a burglary.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile offender was adjudicated delinquent for burglarizing a residence. The juvenile was 12 years of age. On appeal, the juvenile offender claimed that the juvenile court's application of O.C.G.A. § 24A-3503, pertaining to fingerprinting, was unconstitutional. The police fingerprinted the juvenile offender after he was arrested on suspicion of another burglary. The juvenile offender claimed that the juvenile court erred in allowing his fingerprints to be admitted into evidence. O.C.G.A. § 24A-3503 required that children 12 years could not be fingerprinted § 24A-3503(a), except in one specific instance under § 24A-3503(e), and even then the fingerprints could not have been filed unless directed by an appropriate court. The court held that the procedure followed in this case clearly constituted a violation of the plain terms of the statute insofar as routine fingerprinting of the 12 year-old juvenile was concerned. The fingerprints were not taken under § 24A-3503(e). The fingerprints in this case were unlawfully taken, filed, and used for comparison purposes but such error did not require a reversal because the juvenile offender confessed to breaking into the house.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court.

 

1821 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Seaboard Coast Line R.R. Co. v. Wroblewski


No. 51638


Court of Appeals of Georgia


138 Ga. App. 793; 227 S.E.2d 438; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2323


January 6, 1976, Argued  
May 7, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Columbia Superior Court. Before Judge Pierce.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad sought review of a decision of the Columbia Superior Court (Georgia), which, after a jury trial, found in favor of appellees, an automobile driver and her husband, in an action for damages resulting from a collision between a train and the automobile.


OVERVIEW: The trial court charged the jury based on O.C.G.A. § 94-1108, making proof of an injury inflicted by the running of locomotives or cars prima facie evidence of the want of reasonable skill and care on the part of the servants of the company in reference to such injury. The court found that this charge was in error and reversed the decision of the trial court. The statute was taken in totidem verbis from a Mississippi statute which had been interpreted to operate only when the facts had not been produced and was intended to compel the railroad to explain how the injury occurred. The Mississippi statute created merely a temporary inference of fact that vanished upon the introduction of opposing evidence. The court held that when a statute had been adopted from another state, the judicial construction already placed thereon by the highest court of that jurisdiction accompanied it, and was treated as incorporated therein. The court found that the railroad had made a full disclosure of the circumstances surrounding the collision, and the evidence adduced was sufficient to tend to dispute each and every allegation of negligence. Therefore, the charge was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

1822 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Godwin v. State


No. 51861


Court of Appeals of Georgia


138 Ga. App. 131; 225 S.E.2d 723; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2080


March 1, 1976, Submitted  
March 15, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for transcript cost. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Frazier.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Floyd County (Georgia) requiring her to pay for the cost of a court reporter requested by defendant in her shoplifting prosecution.


OVERVIEW: In her prosecution for shoplifting, a misdemeanor, defendant requested that a court reporter record the proceedings. Defendant was assessed the costs of the court reporter, and she appealed. The court held that under O.C.G.A. § 6-805(b), the trial court could require the reporting and transcribing of the evidence and proceedings on terms prescribed by it. In addition, any party could as a matter of right have the case reported at her own expense. Thus, it was not an abuse of discretion to require defendant to pay the cost. The court refused to hear defendant's argument that the statutory procedure that allowed for the payment of recording costs in felony cases and not in misdemeanor cases violated due process and equal protection because it did not have jurisdiction where a favorable ruling on such attack would not affect the rights of the party raising the issue. O.C.G.A. § 24-3104 limited compensation to be paid to court reporters for required transcripts, but it did not set payment for court reporters for cases not required to be recorded, such as misdemeanor prosecutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1823 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Swindell v. Georgia State Dep't of Education


No. 51694


Court of Appeals of Georgia


138 Ga. App. 57; 225 S.E.2d 503; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2053


January 13, 1976, Argued  
March 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on notes. Chatham State Court. Before Judge Head.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a debtor and her mother, sought review of the decision of the Chatham State Court (Georgia), which entered summary judgment in favor of plaintiff, the Georgia State Department of Education, in an action by the Department against defendants for payments upon student loans.


OVERVIEW: The Department sought to recover on teacher scholarship loan notes executed by the debtor and her mother as co-maker. The debtor defaulted by discontinuing a course of study for which she was receiving scholarship aid by virtue of her college involuntarily dismissing her. The Department filed a complaint, and the debtor acknowledged receipt of notice. Summary judgment was entered in favor of the Department and fees and costs were awarded. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the minority of the debtor was not defense to the notes. The court further held that her involuntary dismissal from college was not a reason to avoid liability under the note. The court additionally held that fees and costs were properly awarded by virtue of the fact that the debtors acknowledged notice because their allegation that it was not received within 10 days' time was inapposite in light of the fact that two years had passed in which the debtors had the opportunity to pay and avoid the fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of judgment in favor of the Department.

 

1824 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


LaRue v. State


No. 51440


Court of Appeals of Georgia


137 Ga. App. 762; 224 S.E.2d 837; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2597


November 4, 1975, Argued  
February 23, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for unlawful possession of marijuana by the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia). On appeal, defendant principally argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the prosecution failed to show any legal justification for defendant's arrest so the drugs found in defendant's possession and in his car were the fruits of an unlawful arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for violation of a city ordinance prohibiting public drunkenness. At the suppression hearing, the prosecution failed to introduce a certified copy of the city ordinance so it could not serve as a basis for upholding the arrest and subsequent search. The prosecution then argued that the arrest was based on Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2607, the public drunkenness provision of the state's criminal code. The prosecution also argued that admission of the evidence was harmless because, after defendant's motion to suppress was denied, defendant testified to and admitted possession of the marijuana. The court held that: (1) defendant's conduct did not fall within the purview of § 26-2607; (2) the prosecution was able to prove defendant's possession of marijuana solely by the admission of the illegally seized drugs and it was obvious that defendant would not have attempted to justify his possession of the drugs had the state been unable to prove possession in the first place; and (3) a judicial determination of harmless error could only be made in accordance with certain principles so prior case law establishing per se rules of harmless error were overruled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1825 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Porterfield v. State


No. 51626


Court of Appeals of Georgia


137 Ga. App. 449; 224 S.E.2d 94; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2482


January 12, 1976, Argued  
January 30, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Barrow.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court of Clarke County (Georgia), which convicted him of violating the Georgia Controlled Substances Act. Defendant had been indicted with another individual. At trial, out-of-court statements made by the co-indictee were admitted into evidence. Defendant had objected that these statements were inadmissible hearsay because he had not been charged with conspiracy under O.C.G.A. § 26-3201.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also argued that the State had failed to show the co-indictee was unavailable, that the jury should have been instructed that the State was required to prove conspiracy beyond a reasonable doubt before it could consider the co-indictee's statements, and that certain provisions of the Act were unconstitutional. The court rejected defendant's argument's concerning the State's failure to show that the co-indictee was unavailable and that the Act was unconstitutional on the grounds that defendant had not raised these issues below. The court noted that O.C.G.A. § 38-306 provided that, after the fact of a conspiracy was proved, the declarations of any one of the conspirators were admissible against all. The court held that, because this statutory rule of evidence did not condition admissibility on the existence of an indictment for conspiracy, the superior court had properly admitted the co-indictee's statements. The court also held that the jury was required to weigh all the evidence, including the declarations, to determine whether a conspiracy existed and that the trial court had not erred in refusing to charge that the "beyond a reasonable doubt" standard applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

Jackson v. State


No. 51210


Court of Appeals of Georgia


137 Ga. App. 192; 223 S.E.2d 239; 1976 Ga. App. LEXIS 2380


September 29, 1975, Argued  
January 6, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by conversion. Schley Superior Court. Before Judge Blanks.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Schley County (Georgia0, which convicted defendant of theft by conversion in failing to pay for construction materials used to build swimming pools for his customers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contracted to build swimming pools and the customers had paid for their pools. The contracts provided that defendant would pay for the materials and labor. Defendant failed to pay the suppliers and the suppliers placed liens on the customers' real estate. Defendant was convicted of theft by conversion for his failure to pay for the materials. On appeal, the court stated that the Georgia Supreme Court had held the conversion statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 26-1808, constitutional in prior precedent; therefore, defendant's contention that the statute was unconstitutional because it provided for imprisonment for debt was without merit. The court stated that when the State offered the evidence that defendant was paid for the pools and that he in turn failed to pay his suppliers the burden of proof shifted to defendant to account for the funds. The court stated that in light of the evidence that defendant received and spent the money he had received an acquittal was not required. The court stated that the jury had resolved the factual issue of intent and that the verdict was supported by evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of theft by conversion in failing to pay for construction materials used to build swimming pools for his customers.

Trust Co. of Georgia v. Montgomery


No. 50931


Court of Appeals of Georgia


136 Ga. App. 742; 222 S.E.2d 196; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 1478; 18 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1181


September 8, 1975, Submitted  
November 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Balance due after repossession. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant assignee of a conditional sales contract on an automobile appealed from a judgment of the State Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which denied the assignee's claim for the deficiency balance that was owed by the owner of the vehicle after the automobile had been repossessed and sold.


OVERVIEW: The assignee of a conditional sales contract on an automobile filed an action against the owner of the vehicle for the deficiency balance that was owed on the contract after the automobile was repossessed and sold. The trial court found that the owner was 30 days late in making payments, and had fallen behind in his payments on three occasions. However, the trial court entered judgment in favor of the owner because there was no notice from the assignee to the owner that strict compliance with the terms of the original sales contract would be insisted upon. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The mere fact that the assignee had accepted late payments from the owner on five different occasion did not operate as a waiver of the express contract provisions that related to the timeliness of the payments in view of the language set forth in the contract. The court reached its decision in view of the fact that on one occasion the assignee had obtained a written 90-day extension of the due date of the note from the owner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that was entered in favor of the owner of the vehicle in an action that was brought by the assignee of a conditional sales contract on an automobile to collect the balance, which was due under the contract of sale after the vehicle had been repossessed and sold.

1829 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cadle v. State


No. 51020


Court of Appeals of Georgia


136 Ga. App. 232; 221 S.E.2d 59; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 1306


September 16, 1975, Submitted  
October 1, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1975. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Clayton County (Georgia), which convicted him for violations of the Georgia Drug Abuse Act by unlawfully possessing phencyclidine and a small amount of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's motion to suppress the fruits of a search based on an allegedly illegal search warrant, defendant, without attempting to amend his motion, filed an interlocutory appeal. The court dismissed the appeal. Defendant then renewed him motion to suppress, attempting to amend it so as so show the factual basis thereof. The trial court refused to allow defendant to do so. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in refusing to allow defendant to amend his motion to suppress and thereafter consider the motion on its substantive merits because defendant did not intentionally waive any of his rights. The search warrant was improper because if failed to provide all of the required information to ensure its reliability. However, defendant did not improve his position by amending his motion to suppress. By his admission of unlawful possession of marijuana and phencyclidine on the merits of his trial, upon his oath, defendant had reduced the improper consideration of the fruits of the illegal search to nothing more than harmless error. Nevertheless, the possession of phencyclidine conviction had to be reversed because the statute had been declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment with regard to the possession of marijuana conviction and reversed the trial court's judgment with regard to the possession of phencyclidine conviction.

Snell v. McCoy


No. 50679


Court of Appeals of Georgia


135 Ga. App. 832; 219 S.E.2d 482; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 1843


April 30, 1975, Submitted  
September 26, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to recorder. Cherokee Superior Court. Before Judge Pope.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Cherokee Superior Court (Georgia), which reversed the recorder's judgment that defendant was guilty of having been a passenger in a motor vehicle which was engaged in a race or contest of speed as defined in Ga. Code Ann. § 68-1626(f).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car. When the police attempted to stop the car, the driver tried to outrun the police car. The police finally stopped the car by shooting its tires. The driver was charged with fleeing or attempting to elude a police officer. Defendant was found guilty of having been a passenger in a motor vehicle, which was engaged in a race or contest of speed. The superior court reversed the judgment. Affirming, the court and held that absolutely no act of any character was proven against defendant, which showed that he entered into or had any responsibility for the driver's conduct. It was not contended that defendant owned the car or had any control whatever over the driver, or that he directed the driver to engage in a speed contest or to have eluded the policemen, or that there was a conspiracy between defendant and the driver. The court rejected the position of the recorder that any person who was so unfortunate as to have occupied an automobile that was engaged in a racing contest with another car could have been convicted just as if he were the driver. The law required that, to have been convicted of a crime, defendant had to have acted with intention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's reversal of defendant's conviction for having been a passenger in a motor vehicle which was engaged in a race or contest of speed.

Jones v. Southern Home Ins. Co.


No. 50539


Court of Appeals of Georgia


135 Ga. App. 385; 217 S.E.2d 620; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 1677


April 29, 1975, Argued  
June 18, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 10, 1975.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Polk State Court. Before Judge Flournoy.

Wesley Littlefield, owner of an automobile liability policy with uninsured motorist coverage, was killed in a collision with an automobile driven by Ruby Jones. His widow sued Jones seeking recovery of $ 250,000. Jones carried no insurance, and Southern Home Ins. Co. filed defensive pleadings in her name. A trial resulted in a verdict of $ 95,000. Southern Home paid the plaintiff $ 10,000, the amount of its stated policy coverage. An execution was entered against Jones for the balance.

Jones then filed an action against Southern Home, alleging the above facts and in addition urging (1) that in filing defensive pleadings to the action by Littlefield against her in her name the company had acted without her consent, that her interests were disregarded and her privacy invaded, and (2) that she relied upon the company to represent her in the defense of the action and also in settlement negotiations and to secure and accept a settlement which would protect her to the fullest extent possible; however, the insurer, although receiving an offer to settle the case for $ 10,000, refused [***2] the offer without informing or consulting with her, as a result of which a large judgment has been entered against her.

The defendant moved for summary judgment on the ground, among others, that plaintiff stated no claim on which relief could be granted. Meanwhile, it appeared that the action by Jones against Southern Home was in fact filed by the attorneys for Littlefield pursuant to a contract under which Jones assigned any cause of action she might have against the insurer to Littlefield with the exception of $ 1 in compensatory damages, all punitive damages, and attorney fees. The insurer urged that under these facts Jones was not a proper party plaintiff. Littlefield then filed an intervention praying to be made a co-party plaintiff, which contains an order of approval by the trial court. Later, however, another order was entered dismissing the intervention, followed by an entry of summary judgment for the insurer. Jones and Littlefield appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an uninsured motorist, sought review from the Polk State Court (Georgia), which granted appellee insurer's motion for summary judgment in appellant's action that alleged that appellee acted in bad faith toward appellant in its handling of defensive pleadings filed on appellant's behalf by appellee.


OVERVIEW: A motorist was killed in a collision with a car driven by appellant. The widow sued appellant, who carried no insurance. Appellee filed defensive pleadings in appellant's name. A verdict was entered against appellant for $ 95,000. Appellee paid the amount of its policy coverage, $ 10,000. An execution was entered against appellant for the balance. Among other reasons, appellant sued after learning that appellee had received an offer to settle for $ 10,000 but had refused the offer without consulting appellant. The court affirmed. Appellant's due process rights were not violated when appellee made defensive pleadings in appellant's name because that was exactly what Ga. Code Ann. § 56-407.1(d) authorized. Appellant was not an insured and therefore appellee did not owe appellant a duty of good faith in settling the claim. The duty of good faith arose in the context of a contract between an insured and insurer for insurance coverage. Appellant and appellee had no such contract between them. There was no privity of contract between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision, finding that appellant could not recover against appellee on the basis of bad-faith refusal to settle because appellee did not owe appellant any duty of good faith to settle because appellant was not an insured. Appellant and appellee had no contractual relationship between them. The filing of defensive pleadings in appellant's name did not impose on appellee a duty of good faith to settle.

Garner v. Owens-Illinois Glass Container


No. 50445


Court of Appeals of Georgia


134 Ga. App. 917; 216 S.E.2d 709; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2218


April 8, 1975, Argued  
May 30, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Workmen's compensation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wofford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which sustained appellee employer's motion to dismiss the employee's appeal of an order of the State Board of Workmen's Compensation that granted the employer's motion to dismiss the employee's application for review of a deputy director's order continuing a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that she was disabled due to exposure to sulfur fumes at her place of employment. The employer moved for a continuance of the workmen's compensation hearing based on the employee's refusal to submit to a physical examination by an allergy specialist. The superior court dismissed the employee's appeal from the Board's dismissal of her appeal from a deputy director's order granting the employer's motion. On further review, the court determined that the Workmen's Compensation Act did not permit appeals to the superior court from interlocutory orders, but only allowed appeals from final awards. Rejecting the employee's contention that the effect of the Board's dismissal was to terminate her right to pursue her claim, the court noted that the Board's order remanded the employee's claim to the deputy director for a hearing as to the validity of her refusal and thus actually preserved her rights. The court also ruled that the Board's ruling did not unconstitutionally deprive the employee of the opportunity to show why she should not be subjected to the allergy tests because the employee possessed at least two procedures for presenting her objections.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1835 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dixon v. Phillips


No. 50097


Court of Appeals of Georgia


135 Ga. App. 161; 217 S.E.2d 331; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 1602


January 14, 1975, Argued  
May 23, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1975. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Rabun Superior Court. Before Judge Gunter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim sought review after the Rabun Superior Court (Georgia) granted defendant auto owner's motion for summary judgment in an action for damages sustained in a collision.


OVERVIEW: The owner allowed his minor son, a member of his household, to drive the family car. The son allowed another to drive and a collision occurred. The owner testified by affidavit on summary judgment that he had expressly forbidden his son to allow any other person to drive the car. The trial court summary judgment in favor of the owner. The court reversed. The question was not what instructions the owner had given his son as to the way and manner in which the son operated and managed the vehicle; the owner could not limit his liability by such private instructions, to which the injured parties were not privy. The test was whether the car was being operated in the scope of the owner's business. The owner had made it his business to furnish a car for the pleasure and convenience of family members. The law did not allow a principal to insulate and absolve himself of liability by private instructions to his agent. The "family purpose car doctrine" was an extension of the principal-agent relationship. The court overruled Strickland v. Moore, 147 S.E.2d 682, Pritchett v. Williams, 153 S.E.2d 639, and Trust Co. of Ga. v. Howard, 204 S.E.2d 499, insofar as they conflicted with its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in the owner's favor.

Brown v. Georgia State Bd. of Veterinary Medicine


No. 50030


Court of Appeals of Georgia


134 Ga. App. 574; 215 S.E.2d 332; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2087


January 9, 1975, Submitted  
April 18, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suspension of license. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veterinarian brought an action in the Superior Court of Coweta County (Georgia) for judicial review of a final order entered by defendant Board of Veterinary Medicine of the State of Georgia, which concluded that the veterinarian had a professional association with or employed a person practicing veterinary medicine unlawfully. The veterinarian appealed from the judgment that affirmed the Board's final order.


OVERVIEW: The veterinarian's wife, who was not licensed to practice veterinary medicine, administered puppy and worm shots to a basset hound when the veterinarian was not present and had not directed the administration of medication. The veterinarian argued that O.C.G.A. § 84-1502.3 required that all elements set forth in subparagraphs (a), (b), and (c) thereof must concur for any act to constitute the practice of veterinary medicine. The veterinarian accordingly contended that no violation of § 84-1509.7 was proven because there was no evidence that his wife violated § 84-1502.3(c) by employing a title, words, abbreviation or letters in a manner that induced a belief that she was qualified to perform veterinary medicine. The court held that the Board's factual findings and stated principles of law were correct. The court approved the reasoning that the veterinarian's argument transformed the provisions of §§ 84-1502.3(b) and (c) into mere surplusage and rendered the grammatical structure of § 84-1502.3 meaningless. The court declined to revisit the Georgia Supreme Court's decision rejecting the veterinarian's argument that the statute as construed by the Board was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment affirming the final order that the Board of Veterinary Medicine of the State of Georgia entered against the veterinarian.

Brown v. Georgia Power Co.


No. 50186


Court of Appeals of Georgia


134 Ga. App. 784; 216 S.E.2d 613; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2170


February 4, 1975, Argued  
April 18, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1975. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation of land. Burke Superior Court. Before Judge Fleming.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condemnee sought review of an order from the Burke Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee public utility's motion to strike the condemnee's contentions that were not advanced in a hearing before a special master, who made an award based on the value of the land condemned by the utility. The condemnee appealed the denial of his motion for a new trial following a jury's award for the value of its land.


OVERVIEW: The utility instituted condemnation proceedings against the condemnee's land in accordance with O.C.G.A. ch. 36-6A. A hearing was conducted before a special master who made an award to the condemnee. The condemnee filed documents with the trial court, which asserted that the utility lacked the power of eminent domain and that the statutory condemnation procedure violated the condemnee's constitutional rights. The trial court granted the utility's motion to strike the assertions that did not deal with the value of the land. A jury trial was held and the condemnee received a greater award for the value of the land. The trial court denied the condemnee's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court held that the condemnee was not entitled to present new arguments following the hearing because he was given an opportunity to present those arguments before the master and prior to the judgment entry on the master's findings. The condemnee had received notification requisite to his due process rights by service of the utility's complaint. The court reviewed the record and held that the trial judge had not improperly expressed opinions regarding the condemnee's evidence during trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that struck the condemnee's additional assertions. The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied the condemnee's motion for a new trial.

Julian v. State


No. 49955


Court of Appeals of Georgia


134 Ga. App. 592; 215 S.E.2d 496; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2099


January 13, 1975, Argued  
April 9, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 23, 1975. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Peeler.

Julian, after a mistrial on a one-count indictment for possession and sale of heroin, in the Superior Court of DeKalb County, was reindicted in two counts for the same offense. He filed a motion to dismiss the indictment based on the composition of the grand jury pool, which was denied after a hearing, and certain subpoenas, which were quashed on motion. Following trial and conviction a motion for new trial was made and denied, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed for the reasons stated in Divisions 1, 2 and 6 of this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of possession and sale of heroin and denial of his motion for a new trial by the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with and convicted of the possession and sale of heroin. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied by the lower court. The court determined that the jury pool from which potential juror's were called for defendant's trial was in violation of the fair cross section requirement because it consisted largely of older, white, males, which was not representative of community demographics. The court found that the discrepancy was not otherwise justifiable. The court determined that the trial court's denial of the jury array was in error. The court found that the trial court was in error when it limited the time allotted to defendant's character references to two percent of total trial time. The court found that this constituted reversible error. The court found that the trial court erred when it failed to charge on circumstantial evidence when a witness, upon whose direct evidence the state depended, had been impeached. The court reversed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of possession and sale of heroin.

 

1840 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Aycock v. Police Committee of Board of Aldermen


Nos. 49710, 49711, 49712, 49713, 49714


Court of Appeals of Georgia


133 Ga. App. 883; 212 S.E.2d 456; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2322


September 10, 1974, Submitted  
January 22, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 7, 1975. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative appeal. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wofford.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which denied his petition for certiorari on a decision from appellee police board that demoted him from detective to patrolman due to his public statements against his superior officers.


OVERVIEW: The police board had issued a decision that demoted the police officer from detective to patrolman due to his public statements against his superior officers. The police officer had filed a petition for certiorari against the police board, and the trial court denied the petition. The police officer limited his appeal to two basic issues, which were the constitutionality of the police rules that he allegedly violated, and whether he was denied procedural due process of the law. The court found the police rule requiring a reprimand of a police officer who publicly criticized the official action of a superior officer was not overly broad and did not violate the right to free speech. The court found the police rule was reasonable for maintaining good order and discipline within a police department. Next, the court did not find any due process violations just because the police board failed to make findings of fact and conclusions of law. The court held that in the absence of a statute so requiring, the lack thereof did not affect the validity of the police board's decision. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the police officer's petition for certiorari on a decision from the police board that demoted him from detective to patrolman due to his public statements against his superior officers.
