Harper v. First Nat'l Bank


No. 49886


Court of Appeals of Georgia


133 Ga. App. 690; 212 S.E.2d 20; 1975 Ga. App. LEXIS 2241


November 4, 1974, Submitted  
January 7, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Foreclosure. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Bradford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of the judgment of the Fulton Civil Court (Georgia), which entered default judgment in favor of appellee creditor in the creditor's action to foreclose on personal property.


OVERVIEW: The creditor filed a foreclosure of personal property action against the debtor to collect a debt. The debtor filed an answer and asserted a counterclaim. Neither the debtor nor her attorney received any further notice after filing the defensive pleading. On the seventh day after the debtor was served, the creditor made an application for writ of possession and judgment asserting that the debtor had failed to answer. The trial court granted the creditor's application. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the trial court erred in granting a default judgment to the creditor without giving the debtor an opportunity to be heard. The court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 67-704 provided that if the debtor answered a trial was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

1843 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Watts v. Kegler


Nos. 49454, 49455


Court of Appeals of Georgia


133 Ga. App. 231; 211 S.E.2d 177; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1029


July 8, 1974, Argued  
November 7, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Dean.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured parties each sought recovery from defendant injuring party for injuries sustained in a car accident and for loss of consortium due to these injuries. The DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) dismissed the complaints upon a motion by the injuring party's insurer. The injured parties sought review.


OVERVIEW: The injuring party was served as a nonresident motorist under the provisions of Ga. Code Ann. § 68-801 et seq., by service on the Secretary of State, who forwarded the complaints and summons by registered mail at the injuring party's address. Both letters were returned marked "unclaimed." Service was also made upon the injuring party's insurer, which sought dismissal for insufficient service. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court found that strict compliance with the statute was required unless there was a showing of evasion by the non-resident. The court further found that there was a presumption of compliance with the statute but that there also was evidence to overcome this presumption from the fact that the letters were returned and marked "unclaimed." Because there was evidence before the lower court that could be considered sufficient to overcome the presumption of proper service, the court held that a finding of failure of notice of the suit was authorized. Accordingly, the court held that the lower court did not err in dismissing the complaints for lack of proper service.


OUTCOME: In a personal injury action, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment that dismissed the complaints for lack of proper service.

 

1844 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hodges v. Community Loan & Inv. Corp.


No. 49527


Court of Appeals of Georgia


133 Ga. App. 336; 210 S.E.2d 826; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1066


July 1, 1974, Submitted  
October 23, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover loan balance. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Bradford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borrowers sought review of a decision by the Fulton Civil Court (Georgia), which granted plaintiff lender's motion for summary judgment and denied the borrowers' motion for summary judgment in the lenders' action to recover the loan balance from the borrowers.


OVERVIEW: The borrowers denied liability for the loan on the ground that the lender's action was based upon a contract which was null and void because the provisions of the contract violated the Georgia Industrial Loan Act of 1955 (Act), Ga. Ann. Code § 20. The court held that the Industrial Loan Act lender could have recovered from the borrowers the balance of the principal owing from a loan under the theory of assumpsit, or money had and received, when the loan contract between the lender and the borrowers was null and void because terms of the contract violated the provisions of the Act. The court stated that although the contract was rendered void when the contract failed to meet the specifications of the contact's enabling legislation, the transaction made between the parties in the belief that they were in compliance with the Act should not ipso facto have been ruled violative of public policy. The court also held that because the lender initiated its action after the expiration of the one-year limitations period of the Truth-In-Lending Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1601 et seq., the borrowers' counterclaim was untimely. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the lender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant the lender's motion for summary judgment.

 

1845 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Security Management Co. v. King


No. 49538


Court of Appeals of Georgia


132 Ga. App. 618; 208 S.E.2d 576; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1768


July 9, 1974, Argued  
September 4, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 20, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on note. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Wright.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action on promissory notes, appellants, a debtor and its guarantor, sought review of the summary judgment granted by the Civil Court of Fulton County (Georgia) in favor of appellee creditors.


OVERVIEW: The creditors brought suit on separate promissory notes against the debtor company and its president, who had guaranteed the debt. The creditors demonstrated that the debtor and the guarantor were attempting to set off against each note payable to each individual creditor debts due the debtor and the guarantor by a corporation in which each creditor owned an interest. The answers of the debtor and the guarantor and the affidavit of the guarantor submitted by them in opposition to each motion showed affirmatively that the claims sought to be set off were due them by a partnership of which each creditor was a member. The trial court granted the creditors' motions for summary judgment in each case. On appeal the court affirmed. Under either version, whether corporation or partnership, setoff was not available to the debtor and the guarantor. The tender made by them was based upon the calculation of the setoff that was not available to them because a debt due by a partnership could not be set off against a debt due by a third person to one of the firm. The tender was therefore insufficient under O.C.G.A. § 20-1105, so there was no genuine issue as to any material fact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments granted in favor of the creditors.

 

1846 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Page v. Hapeville


No. 48932


Court of Appeals of Georgia


132 Ga. App. 369; 208 S.E.2d 142; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1694


January 8, 1974, Argued  
June 21, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari from city court. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lounge owner sought review of the denial of his petition for certiorari by the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) of a ruling by appellee city to revoke his whiskey- pouring license. The owner claimed that because he had not been convicted of the violation of any city ordinance there could be no revocation of his license, that due cause for revocation was not shown, and other constitutional attacks on varying city ordinances.


OVERVIEW: The owner was served with a notice to show cause why his city whiskey-pouring license should not be revoked. The notice detailed the time and place of the hearing and recited seven grounds on which revocation was sought. After a hearing before the mayor and city council, the owner's license was revoked. The trial court denied the owner's petition for certiorari. The court affirmed. Hapeville, Georgia, City Ordinance 3-35 provided that due cause for the suspension or revocation of a whiskey license consisted of the violation of any laws or ordinances that regulated such business, or violation of regulations made pursuant to the grant of authority to regulate such businesses. If a statute directed the revocation of a license on conviction of such offense, then in the absence of a court conviction there could not be a legal revocation. However, when the cause of revocation was specified as a violation of the laws, the licensing authorities could act on other evidence than a judgment of conviction. Testimony was offered of specific violations and was sufficient to satisfy the due cause requirement. The city acted within its police powers in restricting sales of whiskey.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1847 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


No. 49012


Court of Appeals of Georgia


132 Ga. App. 274; 208 S.E.2d 5; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1673


February 6, 1974, Submitted  
June 14, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 5, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Aggravated assault. Oconee Superior Court. Before Judge Barrow.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Oconee Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault. He shot the victim through a door and wounded him in the hand and arm to the extent that it had to be amputated. On appeal, defendant argued, among other things, the trial court erred in allowing the prosecutor to remain in the courtroom, sequestration having been invoked, and to testify after other witnesses had done so. Defendant contended that it was error to deny his motion for mistrial because of an expression of opinion as to guilt by the district attorney in his opening statement. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that it was within the discretion of the trial court to allow the prosecutor to remain in the courtroom to assist in the presentation of the case. The court held that where the trial judge quickly admonished the jury to disregard the district attorney's statement concerning his opinion on defendant's guilt, denial of defendant's motion for a new trial was not improper. The court held that where defendant testified, the trial judge did not err in charging the jury relating to defendant's testimony because the jury had a right to take into consideration defendant had an interest in the result of the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated assault.

 

1848 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Partain v. Maddox


No. 49152


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 778; 206 S.E.2d 618; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1552


March 5, 1974, Argued  
April 23, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.

On March 7, 1968, the plaintiff, Joseph G. Maddox, was appointed as a member of the State of Georgia Board of Pardons and Paroles to fill an unexpired term. On April 10, 1969, Joseph G. Maddox was appointed to a full seven-year term to the State Board of Pardons and Paroles by the Honorable Lester Maddox, said appointment being confirmed by the Senate on June 12, 1969. On the morning of the swearing in of Joseph G. Maddox for the full term abovementioned, Governor Lester Maddox had Joseph G. Maddox sign an undated resignation to be kept by the Governor. On January 6, 1971, Governor Lester Maddox accepted the resignation of Joseph G. Maddox and sent him a Western Union Telefax signed by the Governor notifying him that he was accepting his resignation. Joseph G. Maddox subsequently told newspaper reporters at a press conference that he intended to continue his duties as a member of the Board of Pardons and Paroles and would disregard the action of the Governor.

Upon learning that the plaintiff, Joseph G. Maddox, intended to disregard the acceptance of his [***2] resignation and to continue to perform his duties as a member of the said board, Governor Maddox instructed Frank Blankenship, Assistant Attorney General assigned to the Governor as legal advisor, to go to the chairman of the Board of Pardons and Paroles to have him change all of the locks on the doors to the board in order to secure the confidentiality of the files of said board. Frank Blankenship conveyed the Governor's instructions to the defendant, J. O. Partain, Chairman of the Board of Pardons and Paroles.

The defendant, J. O. Partain, Chairman of the Board of Pardons and Paroles, then passed on the Governor's instructions to an employee of the Board of Pardons and Paroles, instructing said employee to advise the office manager that Governor Maddox directed that the locks be changed on the offices of the Board of Pardons and Paroles, and the locks were changed. On January 7, 1971, when the plaintiff appeared at the board offices, he was allowed entry only to retrieve his personal effects.

On January 13, 1971, six days after the locks were changed, Joseph G. Maddox filed the instant suit in the Superior Court of Cobb County against J. O. Partain, as Chairman of the Board of [***3] Pardons and Paroles and individually, seeking to enjoin the defendant from interfering with his performance of his duties and from preventing him from entering his office, and seeking actual damages as well as $ 100,000 in punitive damages for the defendant's allegedly interfering with the plaintiff's performance of his duties. At 4:55 p.m., January 13, 1971, the Honorable Luther C. Hames, Jr., Presiding Judge of the Superior Court of Cobb County, signed a temporary restraining order enjoining the defendant from interfering with the plaintiff's right to pursue his duties and ordering the defendant to allow the plaintiff to enter his office for those purposes, and setting the case down for a show-cause hearing on January 19, 1971. Said temporary restraining order was obtained ex parte and was served upon the defendant on January 14, 1971. On January 14, 1971, after newly assuming the office of Governor of the State of Georgia, the Honorable Jimmy Carter declared the office of Joseph G. Maddox vacant, and officially appointed Richard A. Chappel as a member of the Board of Pardons and Paroles, replacing the said Joseph G. Maddox.

On January 19, 1971, Arthur K. Bolton, Attorney General [***4] of the State of Georgia, appeared in behalf of the defendant, and, in addition to denying the claims made by the plaintiff, sought quo warranto, seeking a declaration that the office be declared vacant. On January 20, 1971, the Honorable Luther C. Hames, Jr., entered an order which in essence held that whether or not the resignation of Joseph G. Maddox was valid was an issue to be determined by the jury, and that the restraining order previously entered against the defendant be continued until final adjudication of the issue. On January 29, 1971, the Honorable Luther C. Hames, Jr., granted a certificate of immediate review of the said order. Arthur K. Bolton, Attorney General for the State of Georgia, filed a notice of appeal in the defendant's behalf, and the plaintiff, through his attorney, filed a notice of cross appeal from the said order, all parties being dissatisfied with the ruling of the trial court. In that fashion, the issue of the right to hold the office was submitted to the Supreme Court of Georgia.

On May 20, 1971, the Supreme Court of Georgia issued its order and opinion on the issue of the right to hold the said office. The Supreme Court ruled that the resignation [***5] obtained by Governor Lester Maddox was unconstitutional and void, and concluded that the plaintiff, Joseph G. Maddox, was entitled to hold the said office for the full term of his appointment.

On June 11, 1971, the case having been remanded to the Superior Court of Cobb County, the judgment of the Supreme Court was made the order of the trial court.

On September 3, 1971, the plaintiff filed an amendment to his complaint seeking $ 2,500 attorney fees as damages in the suit against the defendant individually for interference with the plaintiff's right to pursue the duties of his office during the period January 7, 1971, through January 13, 1971. A pre-trial order was entered in the case on April 25, 1972, signed by the Honorable Luther C. Hames, Jr. The jury trial began on May 14, 1973, and on the first day of trial, the plaintiff filed an amendment to his complaint striking all claims for punitive damages and seeking $ 5,000 in attorney fees as damages.

At the conclusion of the plaintiff's evidence, the defendant, J. O. Partain, made a motion for directed verdict on the grounds that: (a) the defendant was clothed with governmental immunity, (b) there had been no evidence indicating [***6] bad faith, wilful or malicious conduct, and (c) the only evidence of damages introduced in the case was that of attorney fees incurred in adjudicating the right of title to the office. The defendant Partain thus argued that he was entitled to the entry of verdict and judgment as a matter of law. The trial judge overruled the defendant's motion for a directed verdict. At the conclusion of the presentation of the defendant's evidence, the defendant again renewed and made a motion for a directed verdict on the same grounds mentioned above. Upon the second day of trial after the evidence was concluded but prior to final arguments to the jury, the plaintiff, over the defendant's objection, filed an additional amendment to the plaintiff's complaint, withdrawing the plaintiff's demand for attorney fees "eo nomine," and seeking damages pursuant to Code § 105-2004 for court costs in the amount of $ 280 and $ 3,000 in attorney fees as expenses, seeking a total judgment in the amount of $ 3,280. The trial court ruled that there was no sufficient showing of the incurring of a $ 280 court cost, but allowed the amendment to be filed instructing the plaintiff's attorney that he would allow [***7] him to argue and to seek attorney fees in the amount of $ 3,000 since that was "the only proof that has been offered."

The case was submitted to the jury and resulted in verdict and judgment for the plaintiff for $ 3,000. Subsequently, the defendant filed his motion for judgment n.o.v. or in the alternative for new trial. The motion for new trial was later amended. The trial judge denied both motions and the defendant appeals.

The thrust of the defendant's appeal is (1) that the defendant was clothed with governmental immunity and (2) that attorney fees are not recoverable as an item of damages in cases of this nature.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, chairman of the board of pardons and paroles, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Cobb County (Georgia) that granted judgment for plaintiff, member of the board of pardon and paroles, and denied his motion for a judgment n.o.v. in an action by plaintiff against defendant for interference with plaintiff's right to pursue the duties of his office.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a member of the state board of pardons and paroles (board), an office created under the Constitution of the State of Georgia and placed within the executive department of government. As chairman of the board, he had the primary responsibility for preserving the confidentiality of its files. He received his information and instructions from the Governor of Georgia. In passing on the governor's instructions to an employee of the board, with instructions to the employee to so advise the office manager, defendant acted within his discretionary authority as chief executive of the board. The court found that the record was devoid of any conduct by defendant that could be construed as being sufficient to lift the shield that protected public officers acting colore officii. The court held that the trial judge erred in failing to grant defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was in favor of plaintiff in an action against defendant for interference with plaintiff's right to pursue the duties of his office.

 

1849 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Walter v. State


No. 49079


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 667; 206 S.E.2d 662; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1512


February 12, 1974, Argued  
April 10, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 24, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Obscene material. Fulton Criminal Court. Before Judge Tucker.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from Fulton Criminal Court (Georgia), where he was found guilty of two of three alleged violations of O.C.G.A. § 26-2101, for distributing obscene material, and received a sentence of 12 months and a fine of $ 1,000 on each count.


OVERVIEW: At a pre-trial hearing, the trial court found that the three films allegedly shown by defendant were "hard-core pornography" and issued a search warrant to seize the films. When the sheriff attempted to do so, defendant was not present at his theater or able to conceal the films from the sheriff's search warrant. However, the sheriff did not search the premises or make any further attempt to seize the films before a hearing on a citation for contempt against defendant was brought for his failure to produce the films. When defendant refused to testify at this pre-trial contempt hearing, based on his rights against self-incrimination, the trial court found him in contempt. Defendant then involuntarily turned the films over and unsuccessfully objected to their use as evidence at trial. The pre-trial contempt hearing evidence fell far short of that necessary to support a contempt adjudication. The trial court had no authority to order defendant to furnish incriminating evidence against himself on pain of contempt. The trial court erred in overruling defendant's objection to the introduction of the films as evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's obscenity convictions.

 

1850 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Collett v. State


No. 48464


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 411; 206 S.E.2d 70; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1435


September 4, 1973, Argued  
March 14, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Hames.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Cobb County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied her motion to dismiss the state's proceeding to revoke her suspended sentence for possession of marijuana, a violation of the Georgia Drug Abuse Act. Defendant's suspended sentence had been conditioned on her leaving the county and not returning to the area, or using the public streets or highways in that area, for a period of 12 months.


OVERVIEW: The sentence required that she leave the county and not return to it, or to any of six surrounding counties, during that period. She was observed in the county using its roads about 10 months later. Defendant argued that the conditions of suspension amounted to an unconstitutional banishment. On appeal, the court held that the superior court had the authority, under Ga. Code Ann. §§ 27-2709, 27-2714, to impose a suspended sentence in this criminal case, since the sentence was in harmony with the verdict. The verdict had indicated the jury's wish that defendant receive probation as if for a misdemeanor. The court noted that Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. VII (1945), Ga. Code Ann. § 2-107, provided that banishment beyond the limits of the state was not a permitted punishment. The court further noted that the fundamental public policy of the state was that one political division was not permitted to dump its undesirable persons upon another. Additionally, the court remarked that the legislature could have chosen to specifically permit banishment to other areas within the state but had not done so. Therefore, the court determined that defendant's motion should have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's order, which had denied defendant's motion to dismiss the proceeding brought by the state to revoke the suspension of her sentence for possession of marijuana, a violation of the Georgia Drug Abuse Act.

Tolbert v. Tolbert


Nos. 48472, 48473


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 388; 206 S.E.2d 63; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1431


September 13, 1973, Argued  
March 14, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for name change. Lee Superior Court. Before Judge Marshall.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision from the Lee Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee children's petition to have their last names changed from that of the father to that of their stepfather.


OVERVIEW: In the divorce decree the father and mother had an agreement that the husband would pay alimony and child support and that the names of the children would not be changed unless the father gave his written consent. The children brought a petition to change their names. The trial court granted the petition. On appeal, the court reversed. The court stated that because the parties elected to submit the appeal on a stipulation of facts instead of submitting the trial transcript it was governed by the stipulation. The court stated that the stipulation did not set forth any evidence that was introduced to support the contention that a change of name was in the children's best interest. The court stated that the stipulation did show that the mother did nothing to live up to the agreement. The court stated that the usual presumption of favor of judgments could not be applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the children's petition that sought to have their last names changed from that of the father to that of their stepfather.

 

1852 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Garber v. American Mut. Fire Ins. Co.


No. 48954


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 366; 206 S.E.2d 86; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1424


January 14, 1974, Argued  
March 7, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on insurance policy. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Camp.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judgment creditor appealed a decision of the Fulton Civil Court (Georgia), granting defendant insurer's motion for summary judgment based upon a finding that debtor's liability insurance policy was not in full force and effect at the time of a collision that resulted in injury to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff judgment creditor brought an action against defendant insurer, alleging it to be the liability insurer of debtor. Defendant contended that debtor's liability policy was canceled prior to the automobile collision that injured plaintiff upon notice by a premium finance company, under a power of attorney, of a request for cancellation due to debtor's default of a premium loan. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's grant of summary judgment on the grounds that the policy was not legally cancelled where defendant did not give proper notice of cancellation. The reviewing court reversed the judgment, holding that Ga. L. 1963, p. 588, Ga. L. 1969, pp. 561, 568, and the contract of insurance required 10 days notice to debtor of defendant's intention to cancel before cancellation became effective. Defendant was not authorized under a power of attorney to ignore the notice requirements. The court explained that the statutes, rather than the policy, controlled. Thus, the policy was in full force and effect at the time of the collision and the trial court erred in granting defendant's motion.


OUTCOME: The trial court reversed the grant of summary judgment for defendant insurer, holding that debtor's liability policy was in full force and effect at the time of the collision that caused injury to plaintiff judgment creditor where power of attorney did not authorize defendant's noncompliance with statutory notice requirements for cancellation of the policy.

Ben O'Callaghan Co. v. Rose, Silverman & Hunt


No. 48797


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 29; 205 S.E.2d 45; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1864

1855 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. David


No. 48927


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 872; 204 S.E.2d 773; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1289


January 16, 1974, Submitted  
February 12, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to suppress. Fulton Criminal Court. Before Judge Duke.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Georgia appealed from a judgment and order of the Criminal Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which sustained defendant's motion to suppress the State's evidence in its airport-search case against defendant, from whom a weapon was confiscated at an airport after an airport metal detector alerted officials to its presence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a search of persons upon the basis of the results shown by a metal detector was unconstitutional whether such persons be passengers or non-passengers, and that written or oral consent was required to legitimize the search. The court disagreed, holding that it was not unreasonable to set up a magnetometer at a concourse entrance to loading ramps to reduce the risk of air piracy, nor was it unreasonable to subject to a magnetometer scan anyone proceeding past that point, whether a ticketed passenger or merely a well-wisher. The court reasoned that airport authorities were not required to conclude that all those who intend to commandeer an airplane, an act which could be committed while the plane stood at the ramp, would purchase tickets. Because there was nothing unreasonable in placement of the magnetometer, or in the airport security officers' stopping defendant when the device gave an alert, seizure of the weapon was justified, and the evidence should not have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Edwards v. Bullard


No. 48872


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 34; 205 S.E.2d 115; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1315


January 16, 1974, Argued  
February 12, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Muscogee State Court. Before Judge Followill.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured passenger sought review of a decision from the Muscogee State Court (Georgia), which granted defendant driver of other car's motion for mistrial in an action for damages for injuries arising out of an auto accident.


OVERVIEW: The passenger in a car was injured when the car was stuck by another car. An action for damages was filed against the driver of the other car. The complaint alleged as negligence per se the violation of a certain municipal traffic ordinance. The trial court, pursuant to a motion by the driver of the other car, struck all portions of the complaint referring to the ordinance because it was found to be unconstitutional. The case went to trial with the complaint recast. When the attorney for the passenger indicated in his opening statement that the driver pled guilty to the ordinance, the driver's motion for mistrial was granted. The passenger appealed. The court held that: (1) the trial court was correct in finding the municipal ordinance unconstitutional, (2) the trial court was correct in striking the ordinance from the pleadings, (3) evidence that the driver entered guilty pleas to the unconstitutional ordinance was admissible as an admission against interest, and (4) the trial court did not commit reversible error in sustaining the driver's motion for a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The order granting a mistrial was affirmed.

 

1857 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


United States Fidelity & Guaranty Co. v. Kelley


Nos. 48773, 48774


Court of Appeals of Georgia


131 Ga. App. 6; 205 S.E.2d 38; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1305


November 5, 1973, Argued  
February 6, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's Compensation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tidwell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction on main appeal; affirmed on cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Workmen's Compensation Board (Georgia) had entered an award to plaintiff claimant pursuant to the Workmen's Compensation Act, O.C.G.A. § 114-709 based on a change in condition. The insurer and the claimant filed cross-appeals from the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which reversed and remanded the case to the Board on the basis that the Board exceeded its powers and followed an erroneous legal theory in making the award.


OVERVIEW: After the claimant received an award for total incapacity, the Board entered an award for partial incapacity from a certain date. The trial court had determined that the action of the Board in making the second award was contrary to O.C.G.A. § 114-709 (1972) and Ga. Bd. Workers' Comp. R.17. In reversing, the court found that the Board followed the authority provided to it by the change in condition section of the Act. The court reasoned that the trial court improperly relied on federal case law that was not binding on it. After the referenced federal case determined that O.C.G.A. § 114-709 (1972) and Ga. Bd. Workers' Comp. R.17 were unconstitutional, the General Assembly the Board amended those provisions. The Board found as a fact that the claimant had an economic change of condition on a certain date and the evidence supported this finding. Retroactively, the claimant lost his entitlement to the compensation previously awarded to him. The court found that the claimant's admission that he returned to work was evidence of a change of condition. The claimant had been properly allowed to testify to the use of his thumb but not his opinion as to his percentage of disability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in regard to the insurer's appeal. The court affirmed the judgment in regard to the claimant's cross-appeal.

 

1858 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Padgett Masonry & Concrete Co. v. Peachtree Bank & Trust Co.


No. 48975


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 886; 204 S.E.2d 807; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1295


January 17, 1974, Argued  
February 1, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 15, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Plea to jurisdiction. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Morgan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff bank against defendants, a masonry corporation and a related individual, the individual was served by second original and the corporation was served as a resident of Bibb County through the Secretary of State of Georgia. Defendants challenged the judgment of the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which, under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 81A-112(h)(1), denied a motion to set aside a default judgment against them.


OVERVIEW: The individual was properly served. Because the sheriff could not locate the corporation in Bibb County, papers were served on the Secretary of State; and a copy of the filed certificate was forwarded to the corporation by registered mail. Neither defendant appeared or answered. Defendants presented affidavits showing the corporation's address and registration as in Jones County. Pursuant to § 81A-112(h)(1), because both defendants were served in an official, legal manner, the defense of lack of jurisdiction over the person and improper venue was waived because not presented to the trial court by motion or by responsive pleading. The court rejected case law relied upon by defendants because it represented the law prior to § 81A-112(h)(1). Defendants then attempted to raise the issue of the constitutionality of § 81A-112(h)(1). The court had no jurisdiction to adjudicate the constitutionality of statutes, and the Secretary's record did not indicate the county of incorporation. Therefore, the court found that the constitutional issue was not before it, and it retained jurisdiction over the action. The trial court was not in error in denying the motion to set aside the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1859 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Southern Bell Tel. & Tel. Co. v. Invenchek, Inc.


No. 48831


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 798; 204 S.E.2d 457; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1268


January 15, 1974, Argued  
January 25, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 7, 1974. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hubert.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant telephone company appealed from an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which granted plaintiff subscriber's motion to strike the telephone company's defenses to his action for damages due to the negligence on the part of the telephone company in curtailing service.


OVERVIEW: The subscriber brought an action for damages against the telephone company due to its negligence in curtailing service. The trial court granted the subscriber's motion to strike the telephone company's defenses based upon § A2.4.4 of the Georgia Commission General Subscriber Services Tariff (tariff), and the telephone company appealed. The court held that the counts based on negligence were subject to the defense pleaded, and as to those counts it was error for the trial court to have granted the subscriber's motion to strike. There was nothing harsh or inequitable in upholding such a limitation of liability when it was thus considered that the rates as fixed by the Georgia Public Service Commission were established with the rule of limitation in mind. Reasonable rates were in part dependent upon such a rule. As to the count alleging that the interruption of the telephone service, delays, and disconnections of the subscriber's telephone were the result of willful misconduct on the part of the telephone company, the court affirmed the order granting the motion to strike. The tariff had no application and constituted no defense against that count.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting the subscriber's motion to strike the telephone company's defense as to the count alleging that the interruptions of telephone service, delays, and disconnections of the subscriber's telephone were the result of willful misconduct on the part of the telephone company. The court reversed the order granting the motion to strike the defense as to the negligence cause of action.

 

1860 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bituminous Casualty Co. v. Renfroe


No. 48699


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 621; 204 S.E.2d 317; 1974 Ga. App. LEXIS 1205


October 4, 1973, Argued  
January 24, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Workmen's compensation. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Henley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant casualty company sought review of an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed an award by the Workmen's Compensation Board that declared that there was coverage, alleging that the policy was cancelled and that the board used unconstitutional procedural rules.


OVERVIEW: The casualty company appealed the Workmen's Compensation Board's ruling that the company was liable under a policy which the company claimed was cancelled. The court affirmed the finding of liability. Ga. Code Ann. § 56-2430 did not require a return receipt certified mailing of cancellation of policies, but the assured employer disclaimed receipt of notice, and the casualty company had the burden of showing that a cancellation notice was sent. Any evidence was sufficient to affirm the Board's determination, and there was evidence to support the Board's finding that the notice was not received. The Board's Rule 5, which required return receipts, was not unconstitutional. Rule 5 complied with the general grant of authority in § 114-703(a), where the general assembly granted extensive control. There was no conflict between the provisions of § 56-2430 and Rule 5, for in this case, Rule 5 did not create any greater duty of proof than existed under general insurance law.


OUTCOME: The superior court order affirming the Workmen's Compensation Board decision was affirmed because there was evidence to support the Board's findings. The Board's Rule 5 was not unconstitutional.

 

1861 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Moorehead v. Counts


No. 48291


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 453; 203 S.E.2d 553; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1346


July 9, 1973, Argued  
December 4, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 18, 1973. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vehicle occupant appealed an order from the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia), which delivered a damage award in his favor against defendants, an automobile driver and owner, on his negligence cause of action to recover for personal injuries and property damages that resulted when the automobile struck the rear of the occupant's vehicle.


OVERVIEW: During defendants' opening argument, their counsel stated that the occupant had made many previous claims and had intentionally caused the accident in order to recover from defendants. The occupant's counsel sought a mistrial on the basis of defendants' improper and prejudicial argument. The trial court denied the motion and instructed the jury to disregard defendants' mention of the occupant's previous claims. The jury delivered an award in favor of the occupant, but the occupant was dissatisfied with the amount of the award and appealed. The court held that the trial court had failed to fulfill its clear obligations under O.C.G.A. § 81-1009 in light of the inflammatory and highly prejudicial nature of defendants' argument. Under § 81-1009, the trial court was required to rebuke defendants' counsel and to endeavor to remove the improper impression from the jury. The trial court failed to rebuke the counsel, and his instruction was inadequate to remove the improper taint from the jury. Both requirements of § 81-1009 were mandatory. The occupant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment award and remanded for a new trial.

 

1862 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Pitts v. General Motors Acceptance Corp.


No. 48177


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 333; 203 S.E.2d 281; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1315


May 3, 1973, Submitted  
November 28, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Foreclosure. Tift Superior Court. Before Judge Gray.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a judgment from the Tift Superior Court (Georgia), which ordered the execution, levy, and sale of a car after appellee corporation filed an action against the debtor seeking to foreclose on an installment sales contract that was in arrears.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was the holder of an installment sales contract on a car and filed a "notice of intention to foreclose" in the trial court, alleging that the debtor was in arrears. The debtor filed a cross-complaint asserting that the corporation had repossessed the car with the assistance of the police without authority of the law. The trial court found the debtor in arrears and ordered the foreclosure and sale of the car. The debtor appealed. Upon review, the court reversed the judgment. The court found that because the trial court treated the action as a notice of intent to foreclose in order to have a notice and hearing as to probable validity before proceeding with a foreclosure under O.C.G.A. § 67-701 et seq., it should merely have entered an order authorizing the corporation to proceed with the foreclosure under the statute. Instead, the trial judge ordered execution, levy, and sale. Essentially the trial judge's order completed the foreclosure when it ordered a sale. Thus, the court ruled that, on remand, the debtor's answer and crossclaim should be treated as an affidavit of illegality with the right to amend and make any attacks upon the execution as desired.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case.

 

1863 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Zachery v. Geiger Finance Co.


No. 48535


Court of Appeals of Georgia


130 Ga. App. 243; 202 S.E.2d 689; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1292


September 14, 1973, Argued  
November 16, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on note. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors sought review of a judgment from the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which found in favor of appellee finance company in the finance company's action seeking the balance due on a contract.


OVERVIEW: The finance company filed an actin against the debtors in an attempt to recover the balance due on a contract. A summons was served upon the debtors, and a default judgment was later entered in favor of the finance company. Subsequently, the debtors moved to vacate the judgment, but the trial court denied their request. On appeal, the debtors contended that the summons was not in the form required by the Civil Practice Act, O.C.G.A. §§ 81A-104, 81A-301 and that it did not amount to a summons at all. The court disagreed and held that, although the debtors were served under the authority of an earlier statute that was subsequently amended, they were allowed more than 30 days to answer. The court determined that the debtors were actually given 38 days after service to answer the complaint, which was more than the 30 days authorized by O.C.G.A. § 81A-112(a). Thus, the debtors could not complain of that which was favorable to them, as they were allowed more time to answer the complaint that under the Civil Practice Act. The court concluded that it was not created to correct errors, no matter how flagrant, that operated to the benefit of the party complaining.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1864 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Estep v. State


No. 48008


Court of Appeals of Georgia


129 Ga. App. 909; 201 S.E.2d 809; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1194


April 4, 1973, Argued  
September 21, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 15, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Burglary. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Coweta Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of burglary.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant presented several enumerations of error. Defendant challenged the local list of the grand jury and petit jury contending there was an unconstitutional, systematic exclusion of blacks, women, and young adults between the ages of 18 and 30. The court followed precedent and overruled his challenges to the jury system. The court found that defendant was not deprived of constitutional rights to a fair trial through denial of his request for personal use of a professional court reporter in addition to the official court reporter. The case was not so complicated that defendant's attorney needed immediate transcripts, and defendant did not point to any factor that would indicate he sustained any harm by the court's denial of his request. The court held that the grand jury was properly impaneled. The court found that portions of the State's closing argument were so prejudicial that the trial court erred in refusing to rebuke him and in overruling motions for mistrial. The remarks objected to were improper as they were comments that had no relevance to the evidence adduced during the trial. The trial court should have granted a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to most of defendant's enumerations of error, but ordered a new trial.

 

1865 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Radcliffe v. Boyd Motor Lines, Inc.


No. 48389


Court of Appeals of Georgia


129 Ga. App. 725; 201 S.E.2d 4; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1127


June 29, 1973, Argued  
September 10, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1973. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Damages, etc. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed as to the dismissal, but affirmed as to the quashing of service.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed a judgment of the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained motions by defendant corporation to dismiss plaintiff's tort action on the ground that the venue and jurisdiction of the action was properly in another county and to quash the service on the ground that there had been no lawful or proper service perfected.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendant, while having its place of business in another county, owned and operated a speedway in the county sued in where, by reason of defendant's negligence, plaintiff's child was killed. Defendant moved to dismiss and to quash service. Both motions were sustained and on plaintiff's appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the action for lack of venue because it was properly brought in the county where the cause of action originated. However, the trial court did not err in sustaining the motion to quash service because there was no valid service. A speedway caretaker who did not meet the statutory status of an officer, cashier, or agent under Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-104(d) accepted service. Nor was the service sufficient by leaving a copy at the place of business because the speedway was no longer in operation. There was no authority under Ga. Code Ann. § 81-215 for issuance or service of a second original because there was only one defendant. Nor did defendant qualify as a "common carrier," subject to service under Ga. Code Ann. § 68-514, because the speedway was not a public highway.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment that dismissed plaintiff's case. The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that quashed service.

 

1866 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Railey v. State Farm Mut. Auto Ins. Co.


No. 48364


Court of Appeals of Georgia


129 Ga. App. 875; 201 S.E.2d 628; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1181


June 29, 1973, Argued  
September 7, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26 and October 11, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Walker State Court. Before Judge Adams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the State Court of Walker County, Georgia, which dismissed plaintiffs' petition seeking damages for a neck and back injury alleged to have been suffered in an automobile collision with defendant driver after process could not be served on defendant within the applicable statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were injured when defendant driver's vehicle collided with plaintiffs' automobile. Thereafter, defendant relocated to another state. Plaintiffs sought to serve process on defendant by publication under the Civil Practice Act § 4(e)(1)(iii), Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-104(e)(1)(iii). Though initially granted, the trial court later revoked its order claiming the request for service by publication was made after the statute of limitation had run on plaintiffs' claim and dismissed the claim. Plaintiffs appealed. The court found that service by publication was not valid and could not authorize an in personam judgment as sought; however, plaintiffs had the benefit of no statutory method or common law method by which lawful service could be effected, and since there had been no waiver, the statute of limitation was tolled under Ga. Code Ann. § 3-805 and therefore had not run.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed; the statute of limitation was tolled under Georgia law because defendant driver moved to another state leaving plaintiffs with no statutory or common law method to effect service of process.

 

1867 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Rautenstrauch v. State


No. 48153


Court of Appeals of Georgia


129 Ga. App. 381; 199 S.E.2d 613; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1015


April 30, 1973, Argued  
June 15, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Fulcher.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which overruled defendants' general demurrers to the indictment charging them with possession of marijuana and overruled defendants' motions to suppress evidence and for discovery.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the trial court erred in overruling their general demurrers to the indictment and in overruling their motions to suppress and for discovery. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court's actions were proper. The court found that defendants were not entitled to pretrial discovery or inspection and possession of evidence and that the State was not required in the indictment to negative any exception, excuse, proviso, or exemption contained in O.C.G.A. tit. 79A, which permitted certain persons to lawfully have in their possession prohibited drugs and narcotics. The court found that in conducting a surveillance of a house, a police officer overheard a conversation involving defendants and others about a package containing "good marijuana." The court determined that the overheard statement, coupled with defendants' flight from the house thereafter, constituted probable cause for police officers to believe that defendants had marijuana then in their possession and were attempting to escape. The court thus concluded that the officers had authority to arrest defendants without warrants and, as incident thereto, to search their persons and their car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1868 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Blackmon


No. 48006


Court of Appeals of Georgia


129 Ga. App. 214; 199 S.E.2d 376; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 949


April 9, 1973, Argued  
May 11, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 15, 1973. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tax appeal. Polk Superior Court. Before Judge Winn.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order and judgment of the Superior Court of Polk County (Georgia), which overruled their motions to set aside the judgment of dismissal and for a new trial, and from the judgment of dismissal of the trial court after appellants rejected a settlement proposal from appellee with respect to their claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed an action in the trial court, which delayed appellee's motion to dismiss pending settlement discussions. Appellee's settlement proposal was rejected, and the trial court signed and delivered an order dismissing the appeal on the same day. The taxpayers did not timely appeal the dismissal order, but then filed motions for a new trial and to set aside the dismissal, alleging that they had failed to receive notice of the entry of the judgment. The trial court overruled the motions. The court affirmed the order and held that only three methods of direct attack on a judgment existed under Georgia law: a motion for new trial, which was predicated upon some extrinsic defect that did not appear upon the face of the record or pleadings; a motion to set aside, which was predicated upon some non-amendable defect which appeared upon the face of the record or pleadings; and a complaint in equity, which required that the judgment had to have been obtained by fraud, accident or mistake, or the acts of the adverse party unmixed with the negligence or fault of the taxpayers. The taxpayers alleged no defects or equitable reason that would have permitted the motions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's overruling of appellants' motions to set aside the judgment of dismissal and for a new trial.

 

1869 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cross v. State


No. 47984


Court of Appeals of Georgia


128 Ga. App. 837; 198 S.E.2d 338; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1637


March 6, 1973, Argued  
April 6, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 19, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Bribery; motion to suppress. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Tillman.

Defendant was indicted for the offense of bribery. This appeal is from the overruling of his motion to suppress tape recordings and the testimony of three police officers on the ground that this amounted to an illegal search and seizure of his conversation because there was no application for or issuance of a warrant authorizing electronic eavesdropping under Ch. 26-30 of the Criminal Code of Georgia.

It appears that an informer known to a police officer told the officer that a certain Johnson wanted to reach him. The officer then called Johnson and they arranged to meet. By agreement of his supervisors, an electronic transmitting device was concealed upon the officer's body for the meeting. No attempt was made to secure a warrant. Two other officers went along to receive and record the upcoming conversations. Shortly after the officer met Johnson, he was taken to another automobile where the defendant was seated. The officer had a conversation with the defendant in which the defendant allegedly offered money to the officer in return for intelligence-type information [***2] on police activities.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction for bribery entered on a jury verdict by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled defendant's motion to suppress tape recordings and the testimony of police officers on the ground that they were the result of an illegal search and seizure of his conversation because there was no application for or issuance of a warrant authorizing electronic eavesdropping under Ga. Code Ann. § 26-3001.


OVERVIEW: After an electronic transmitting device was concealed during an officer's meeting with defendant and no attempt was made to secure a warrant, defendant allegedly offered money to the officer in return for intelligence-type information on police activities. Defendant argued that the evidence was a result of prohibitions found in § 26-3001. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 26-3001 was inapposite because the officer had not intercepted or overheard a conversation that was made directly to him, nor was the officer an eavesdropper, nor did he have the conversation under surveillance. The court ruled that there was no interest legitimately protected by the Fourth Amendment involved when defendant misplaced his belief that the person to whom he voluntarily confided his wrongdoing would not have revealed it. The court determined that no warrant to search and seize was required. The court concluded that § 26-3001 did not apply to a party to the conversation and did not prohibit interception, recording, or divulging of a message when the message constituted the commission of a crime or was directly in furtherance of a crime, provided at least one party thereto consented.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for bribery.

 

1870 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Upton v. State


No. 47961


Court of Appeals of Georgia


128 Ga. App. 547; 197 S.E.2d 478; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1544


March 5, 1973, Argued  
March 16, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Involuntary manslaughter. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Sosebee.

Earl Upton was indicted in the Superior Court of Henry County for the murder of his wife, tried, and convicted of involuntary manslaughter in the commission of an unlawful act. There is some evidence tending toward an inference that Pat Upton, the wife, had been strangled in Clayton County where she was seen by a witness at a distance prior to the incidents occurring in Henry County. The jury had ample grounds to disbelieve this witness, and apparently did so, since Upton was acquitted of both murder and voluntary manslaughter. The case was first appealed to the Supreme Court on the ground, among others, that the present venue statute is unconstitutional. The Supreme Court transferred the case to this court (229 Ga. 834 (195 SE2d 21)) holding that "the verdict was guilty of involuntary manslaughter in the commission of an unlawful act and the evidence was uncontradicted that this crime was committed, if it was in fact committed, in the county where the defendant was tried," that is, in Henry County.

The jury verdict and this holding eliminate from consideration all the testimony which, if believed, would [***2] have led to a verdict of guilty of murder or voluntary manslaughter, and all testimony relating to certain occurrences in Clayton County insofar as the cause of death is involved. This leaves the following evidence:

Shortly after 11:00 p.m. the defendant came to the house of the witness Dodson to get help for his wife. An ambulance was called, and the witness and defendant then went back up the road, where Mrs. Upton was lying unconscious on the right side of the pavement. She was taken to the hospital and pronounced dead on arrival. The defendant made a statement that his wife had fallen out of the car and that at the time he was traveling between 45 and 60 miles per hour. In his statement to the jury he said: "I was going into the curve, and it's quite a variation between 45 and 60 miles an hour, but driving a sports car, I wasn't used to it, so I really don't know. It had two or three gauges on it. I don't know, but I was running at least 45 and not over 60. I went into the curve and got out on the outside." He further stated that he did not know whether his wife jumped or fell from the car, but that she was out before he realized what had happened. From other evidence [***3] as well as other parts of the defendant's statement it appeared that they had been quarrelling, that both had been taking medication, that Mrs. Upton at least had been drinking, and the defendant described his own condition as being "in a state of numbness" but said he knew what he was doing, his coor dination was all right, and he had had to battle with his wife on previous occasions during the trip to keep her from jumping out of the car.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter in the commission of an unlawful act.


OVERVIEW: The only unlawful act on which the trial court charged the jury was the offense of speeding. The court determined that the trial court should have granted defendant's motion for a new trial because his commission of an unlawful act was not proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The court explained that there was no evidence except that defendant's wife was injured when she hit the roadway, that defendant admitted that he was going between 45 and 60, and that the speed limit was 50. The court noted that it was not error to omit from a charge that a defendant's unsworn statement had as much force as the jury chose to give it. The court concluded that defendant could not complain that he was not informed by the State that a certain witness would have testified because the witness had testified at a prior trial, defendant knew what testimony he would have given, and defendant made no further demand for a list of witnesses. The court determined that where defendant had entered a plea of nolo contendere for a previous offense, it was not error to inquire on cross examination of witnesses to his good character whether they were aware that he had been arrested for such offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1871 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Veal v. General Acci. Fire & Life Assurance Corp.


No. 47479


Court of Appeals of Georgia


128 Ga. App. 610; 197 S.E.2d 410; 1973 Ga. App. LEXIS 1558


September 6, 1972, Argued  
March 14, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1973. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge McMurray.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Crisp Superior Court (Georgia) granting summary judgment to defendant insurance company on the ground that the prior judgment against defendant driver was void because the court in which the judgment was rendered could not acquire jurisdiction over defendant by service by publication and then render an in personam judgment against him.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, in a prior personal injury action arising out of a vehicular collision, obtained an in personam judgment against defendant driver. Service upon defendant was attempted by publication under Ga. L. 1966, p. 609, § 4. This suit against defendant insurance company followed. Plaintiff sought to collect her judgment claiming that defendant driver was an insured driver under the terms of an automobile liability policy issued by defendant insurance company. The lower court granted summary judgment for defendant insurance company based on the fact that the prior judgment against defendant driver was void as the court in which the judgment was rendered did not have jurisdiction over his person. The reviewing court affirmed, holding that there was no provision in the state whereby courts may acquire jurisdiction over a defendant by service by publication and then render an in personam judgment against him. Consequently, the judgment that plaintiff sought to enforce against defendant insurance company was void.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for defendant insurance company and held that there was no provision in the state whereby courts may acquire jurisdiction over a defendant by service by publication and then render an in personam judgment against him.

 

1872 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dunaway v. Kaylor


No. 47398


Court of Appeals of Georgia


127 Ga. App. 586; 194 S.E.2d 264; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 963


September 5, 1972, Argued  
November 17, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Fleming.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the victims of an attack by defendant parents' minor child, appealed a judgement of the Richmond Superior Court (Georgia), which granted the parents summary judgment in the victims' action in which they sought recovery for damages against the parents of the minor, for the latter's tortious conduct.


OVERVIEW: The minor attacked the victims with an ice pick. The victims brought an action against the minor's parents to recover damages for their injuries. The trial court granted the parents summary judgment, and the victims appealed. The court affirmed. The court noted that the statute under which the victims sought to hold the parents liable for their son's acts, O.C.G. A. § 105-113, had been held by the Georgia Supreme Court to be unconstitutional. Thus, the court held that the victims could not recover against the parents under this statute. The victims alleged in the alternative that the parents knew at the pertinent time that their son was of a violent temperament and had a propensity to violence and that the parents were negligent in failing to warn the victims of the danger of such violence and in failing to restrain their son. The court held that the allegations of prior knowledge were pierced by the evidence offered in support of the motion for summary judgment whereby the parents denied that their son had ever engaged in combat with anyone or that anyone had complained about the conduct of their son within the past five years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1873 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


North Georgia Finishing, Inc. v. Di-Chem, Inc.


No. 47070


Court of Appeals of Georgia


127 Ga. App. 593; 194 S.E.2d 508; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 967


April 7, 1972, Submitted  
October 26, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1972. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Garnishment. Whitfield Superior Court. Before Judge Vining.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company brought an action in the Whitfield Superior Court (Georgia) against defendant finishing company seeking to garnish defendant's bank account. The trial court overruled defendant's motion to dismiss the garnishment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant posted a bond after the suit was filed and moved to dismiss the garnishment, arguing that the garnishment was unconstitutional as violative of due process. Defendant also claimed that the garnishment procedure was unconstitutional because it violated defendant's due process and equal protection rights guaranteed by the Constitution of the United States and the Constitution of the State of Georgia. The trial court overruled the motion to dissolve the garnishment and certified the case for appeal. Defendant appealed. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that the pleadings failed to disclose a proper constitutional attack upon any statute. Neither the motion nor the certificate of the trial judge showed (1) what statute was involved in the alleged constitutional attack or (2) what specific constitutional provisions, either Federal or State, were involved, nor did they show (3) that the trial judge had ruled that the alleged statute was or was not constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1874 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Blackmon v. Cobb County-Marietta Water Auth.


No. 46996


Court of Appeals of Georgia


126 Ga. App. 459; 191 S.E.2d 128; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 1183


March 7, 1972, Argued  
June 14, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sales tax. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Ravan.

The State Revenue Commissioner made an assessment against Cobb County-Marietta Water Authority for sales and use taxes which had not been paid on its purchases of office supplies, office equipment, automotive equipment, hardware, pipes, valves, paints, chemicals and on electricity and gas purchased from utilities during the taxable periods from April, 1963, through September, 1968.

Both parties moved for summary judgment and the trial court entered a judgment in favor of the taxpayer setting aside the assessment and denied the motion of the Revenue Commissioner. From the judgments on the motions the Commissioner appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction that the appellant's motion for summary judgment be granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Revenue Commissioner filed an action against appellee Cobb County-Marietta Water Authority pursuant to the Sales and Use Tax Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 92-3402a, to recover unpaid taxes. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The Cobb Superior Court (Georgia) granted summary judgment in the water authority's favor. The commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The water authority argued that other water authorities were not subject to the sales and use tax. The court found that the water authority was not exempt under Ga. Code Ann § 92-3403a(C)(2)(d) because it was not part of the federal government, the State of Georgia, or any county or municipality of the state. Further, the court found that other laws that created the Clayton County Water Authority and the Bibb County Water and Sewerage Authority were not assessed sales taxes on their purchases of personal property because those authorities, by laws creating them, were made a division or a part of the county government, making them exempt under § 92-3403a(C)(2)(d). The court held that the disparity did not violate equal protection because uniformity in taxation did not mean universality. In reversing the trial court's judgment, the court held that an amendment to the laws creating the water authority, 1972 Ga. Laws 3208, granted the authority immunity from payment of sales and use taxes but was not retroactive and did not affect its liability for the tax periods in the instant matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and directed the trial court to grant summary judgment in favor of the commissioner.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Attachment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.
