1876 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Coe & Payne Co. v. Wood-Mosaic Corp.


Nos. 46725, 46726, 46740, 46727, 46739


Court of Appeals of Georgia


125 Ga. App. 845; 189 S.E.2d 459; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 1490


November 2, 1971, Argued  
March 10, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 31, 1972. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson.

These cases arise out of the Atlanta Gas Light Tower fire of December 5, 1968, which caused the deaths of four people and extensive property damage.

The principal parties involved in these cases are herein set out. They are C. P. Company (hereinafter referred to as C. P. Company); Coe & Payne Company (hereinafter referred to as Coe & Payne); Overall Paint Company (hereinafter referred to as Overall Paint); Wood-Mosaic Corp. (hereinafter referred to as Wood-Mosaic); Atlanta Flooring Company (hereinafter referred to as Atlanta Flooring); Betty C. Allen (hereinafter referred to as Allen).

The action involving appeals 46725, 46726 and 46727 was brought by C. P. Company, the owner of the building, for property damage. Coe & Payne, one of three named defendants, filed third-party complaints against Atlanta Flooring, Overall Paint, and Wood-Mosaic, as well as several other parties. Atlanta Flooring, in turn, filed cross claims against Wood-Mosaic and Overall Paint.

The action involving appeals 46739 and 46740 was brought by plaintiff Allen for the wrongful [***2] death of her husband, a workman killed in the fire. The defendants included Atlanta Flooring, Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic. Atlanta Flooring filed cross claims against Wood-Mosaic and Overall Paint.

The pleading and evidence of record showed that one theory as to the cause of the fire involves the possible explosion of vapors given off by an adhesive known as "R-65," which is designed to be used in the laying of parquet flooring. Coe & Payne, a flooring contractor, was laying parquet flooring in the Gaslight Tower on the day of the fire, and was using R-65. The adhesive was manufactured by Overall Paint, an Ohio corporation, and distributed by Wood-Mosaic, a Kentucky corporation, for use with its parquet flooring. The adhesive was sold by Wood-Mosaic to Atlanta Flooring, a Fulton County concern, and Atlanta Flooring, in turn, sold the adhesive to Coe & Payne.

Both Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic asserted jurisdictional defenses, claiming that they were not subject to the jurisdiction of Georgia courts under the Georgia Long-Arm Statute, the chosen basis of jurisdiction. After hearing evidence on the motions of those two parties, the trial court sustained their position and dismissed [***3] the various pleadings as to Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic. The appeals are here upon certificates of immediate review.

46726 is the appeal of Atlanta Flooring from the trial court's order dismissing the third-party complaint as to Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic, and consequently dismissing Atlanta Flooring's cross claims against those third-party defendants. C. P. Company and Coe & Payne also appealed from the trial court's order, which appeals bear docket numbers 46727 and 46725 respectively. Those two appeals and the appeal of Atlanta Flooring Company have been consolidated.

46739 is the appeal of Allen from the trial court's order dismissing the complaint as to Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic. 46740 is the appeal of Atlanta Flooring from this order and the consequent dismissal of its cross claim against the defendants Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic.

With these facts in mind, we now consider the pleadings. First with regard to the C. P. Company's appeals and then with regard to the Allen appeals.

The action involved in the C. P. Company's appeals commenced with the filing of a complaint by C. P. Company against Coe & Payne Company and two other defendants. The short form complaint [***4] simply alleged that three defendants negligently caused the fire in question causing plaintiff damage in excess of $ 110,000.

Coe & Payne answered and filed a third-party complaint against Atlanta Flooring, Wood-Mosaic, Overall Paint, and others. The third-party complaint alleged, as to Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic, that those parties were nonresidents of the State of Georgia, but transacted business and had committed tortious acts within the State of Georgia so as to be subject to the jurisdiction of the courts of Georgia under the Georgia Long-Arm Statute (Ga. L. 1966, p. 343; 1968, p. 1419; 1970, p. 443; Code Ann. § 24-113.1 et seq).

The third-party complaint alleged that the fire was caused when fumes or vapors from "R-65 Wood Block Flooring Adhesive" exploded or caught fire; that the adhesive was manufactured by Overall Paint, had been expressly recommended, specified and sold by Wood-Mosaic, manufacturers of the parquet flooring being installed by Coe & Payne and had been sold to Coe & Payne by Atlanta Flooring Company; the third-party complaint then alleged liability based upon both negligence and warranty against Overall Paint, Wood-Mosaic, and Atlanta Flooring, and concluded [***5] with prayers that Coe & Payne have judgment against the third-party defendants for all or part of any sums that might be adjudged against it in favor of plaintiff.

Atlanta Flooring answered the third-party complaint and asserted cross claims against Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic. In its cross claims, Atlanta Flooring alleged that if in fact the "R-65 Wood Block Flooring Adhesive" contributed to this fire and was sold by Atlanta Flooring to Coe & Payne, then Atlanta Flooring had purchased that adhesive from Wood-Mosaic, that the adhesive was manufactured by Overall Paint, that both Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic had impliedly warranted to Atlanta Flooring that the adhesive was merchantable and fit for the use intended, and that if the adhesive was in fact not merchantable and fit for the use intended, then Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic would have breached their warranties as described. The cross claim further asserted negligence on the part of both Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic, and prayed for judgment over against Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic in the event that any judgment is returned against Atlanta Flooring.

Wood-Mosaic filed its answer to the third-party complaint, wherein it [***6] asserted, inter alia, jurisdictional defenses. Wood-Mosaic also filed its motion to dismiss the third-party complaint, asserting insufficiency of process, lack of jurisdiction, and unconstitutionality of the Georgia Long-Arm Statute.

Similarly, Overall Paint filed its answer to the third-party complaint, asserting several jurisdictional defenses. Overall Paint also filed a motion for summary judgment.

Plaintiff C. P. Company then filed an amended complaint wherein it added as parties defendant Atlanta Flooring, Overall Paint, and Wood-Mosaic, as well as certain other parties. Basically, the allegations of the amended complaint repeated the allegations of Coe & Payne's third-party complaint.

Atlanta Flooring filed its answer to plaintiff's amended complaint, asserting cross claims against Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic identical to those contained in its answer to the third-party complaint. Overall Paint filed an answer to plaintiff's amended complaint basically identical with its original answer to the third-party complaint. Similarly, Wood-Mosaic filed an answer to plaintiff's amended complaint paralleling its earlier answer.

Wood-Mosaic subsequently filed, as "third-party [***7] defendant and an additional named defendant," a motion for summary judgment for want of jurisdiction. Overall Paint also filed a motion for summary judgment "as a defendant and a third-party defendant." Overall Paint's second motion was identical to its first, simply referring to its new-found status as a defendant as well as a third-party defendant.

The action involving Allen's appeals commenced with the filing of a complaint by plaintiff against Atlanta Flooring, Wood-Mosaic, Overall Paint, and others. The complaint alleged, as to Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic, that those parties were nonresidents of the State of Georgia, but transacted business and had committed tortious acts within the State of Georgia so as to be subject to the jurisdiction of the courts of Georgia under the Georgia Long-Arm Statute (Ga. L. 1966, p. 343; 1968, p. 1419; 1970, p. 443; Code Ann. § 24-113.1 et seq).

The complaint alleged that the adhesive used in installing floors where plaintiff's husband was working was manufactured by Overall Paint, had been expressly recommended and specified by Wood-Mosaic, manufacturers of the flooring being installed, and had been sold to Coe & Payne (a flooring contractor [***8] and plaintiff's husband's employer) by Atlanta Flooring Company. The complaint then alleged liability based upon the negligence of all defendants.

Atlanta Flooring answered the complaint and asserted cross claims against Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic. In its cross claims, Atlanta Flooring alleged that if in fact the adhesive contributed to this fire and was sold by Atlanta Flooring to Coe & Payne, then Atlanta Flooring had purchased that adhesive from Wood-Mosaic, that the adhesive was manufactured by Overall Paint, that both Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic had impliedly warranted to Atlanta Flooring that the adhesive was merchantable and fit for the use intended, and that if the adhesive was in fact not merchantable and fit for the use intended, then Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic would have breached their warranties as described. The cross claim further asserted negligence on the part of both Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic, and prayed for judgment over against Overall Paint and Wood-Mosaic in the event that any judgment is returned against Atlanta Flooring.

Wood-Mosaic filed its answer to the complaint, wherein it asserted various jurisdictional defenses. Wood-Mosaic also filed [***9] its motion to dismiss the complaint, asserting insufficiency of process, lack of jurisdiction, and unconstitutionality of the Georgia Long-Arm Statute.

Similarly, Overall Paint filed its answer to the complaint, asserting several jurisdictional defenses. Overall Paint also filed a motion for summary judgment. Wood-Mosaic subsequently filed a motion for summary judgment for want of jurisdiction.

In both sets of appeals prior to the hearing of the jurisdictional motions by the court, the parties entered into a stipulation incorporating into the record of this case certain interrogatories and answers filed in Lutz v. Coe & Payne Company et al., Case No. B-50266, Superior Court of Fulton County, which discovery was germane to the jurisdictional question before the court.

The proof considered by the court in both the Allen case and the C. P. Company case consisted of the affidavits of Martin A. Davis and Joseph Mann, interrogatory answers, and interrogatory answers stipulated from the Lutz record.

The affidavit of Martin A. Davis showed that he is Secretary-Treasurer and Chief Executive Officer of Overall Paint, and therefore familiar with the means and methods whereby Overall Paint [***10] conducts its business; that Overall Paint has never had any representatives in the State of Georgia, has never maintained an office or place of doing business in the State of Georgia, has never had an agent or employee located in the State of Georgia, and has never owned any real or personal property located within the State of Georgia; that Overall Paint has never sent a representative into the State of Georgia for the purpose of soliciting business, and does not solicit orders within the State of Georgia; that Overall Paint is an Ohio corporation and is not and has never been authorized to transact business in the State of Georgia; that Overall Paint does not do business within the Stage of Georgia, and has not committed a tortious act within the State of Georgia; that Overall Paint has never produced or manufactured any product in the State of Georgia.

Joseph Mann submitted two affidavits. His affidavit dated January 20, 1971, showed that he is Secretary-Treasurer of Wood-Mosaic and familiar with its business; that Wood-Mosaic never had any representatives or agents in the State of Georgia, has never been domesticated in the State of Georgia, has never maintained a place of doing [***11] business in the State of Georgia, and has never had an agent designated for service of process or an agent upon whom service could be perfected in the State of Georgia; that Wood-Mosaic has never maintained an office or place of doing business in the State of Georgia, has never had an agent or employee located in the State of Georgia, and has never owned any real or personal property in the State of Georgia; that Wood-Mosaic is a Kentucky corporation which has never been authorized to do business in the State of Georgia; that Wood-Mosaic does not do business within the State of Georgia, has not committed a tortious act within the State of Georgia, and has never produced or manufactured any product within the State of Georgia.

With reference to the business of Wood-Mosaic, Mr. Mann testified in his affidavit that Wood-Mosaic manufactures wood flooring, which flooring is sold in Georgia "by order from the customer which orders are accepted and filled by Wood-Mosaic Corporation in Kentucky, and the product is shipped from Kentucky upon invoice to the customer which invoices are paid by remittance paid to Kentucky." The affidavit further shows that the R-65 adhesive was sold to customers [***12] along with orders for wood flooring, and that "this adhesive and the wood flooring was sold in the State of Georgia by orders received from the customer which were accepted and filled by Wood-Mosaic in Kentucky, and the wood flooring and adhesive was shipped F.O.B. our factory in Louisville, Kentucky upon invoice to the customer," which invoices were paid by remittance to Kentucky.

The second affidavit of Joseph Mann, dated January 27, 1971, showed that the "customers" referred to in his prior affidavit did not include Coe & Payne, C. P. Company, James A. Allen, or Billy D. Palmer; that it purchased R-65 Wood Adhesive from Overall Paint Company, and sold its own wood flooring and the R-65 adhesive to Atlanta Flooring in Georgia; that Wood-Mosaic did not at any time sell flooring or R-65 adhesive to Coe & Payne Company, C. P. Company, James A. Allen or Billy D. Palmer, and that Wood-Mosaic had no knowledge of what happened to its wood flooring or the adhesive after they had been received by Atlanta Flooring Company.

Mr. Mann's second affidavit also identified as an exhibit a copy of the installation and maintenance instruction manual supplied by Wood-Mosaic with its flooring. The [***13] manual generally recommended the use of R-65 adhesive or Fastac No. 47. It specified the use of R-65 "only" with the Hadden Hall pattern parquet flooring being laid by Coe & Payne.

Stipulated evidence brought over from the Lutz record included the following:

Wood-Mosaic's answers to Coe & Payne's first interrogatories showed that Wood-Mosaic, during the past five years, had shipped flooring on invoice to various wholesale distributors within the State of Georgia; Wood-Mosaic denied that these invoiced shipments constituted contracts. Wood-Mosaic denied having any records of the value of its products which were ultimately sold to customers in Fulton County or elsewhere in Georgia. It does not prohibit the resale of its product in Fulton County or elsewhere in Georgia. Wood-Mosaic admitted that it shipped or delivered its products, including the flooring and adhesive involved in this fire, to locations within Fulton County and elsewhere in Georgia, but denied that it "distributed" or "recommended" its products. It denied having records showing the volume of deliveries so made. Wood-Mosaic admitted shipping miscellaneous flooring products to Atlanta Flooring during the past five [***14] years in a total dollar amount of approximately $ 40,000, but denied that these shipments constituted agreements or contracts with Atlanta Flooring, and denied knowledge of the ultimate consumer of these products. Wood-Mosaic's flooring is manufactured in Kentucky. Wood-Mosaic does not know the values of the R-65 adhesive it purchased from Overall Paint during the past five years, but does know that the values for the past two years total $ 525.60. Wood-Mosaic has not shipped any R-65 since January 1, 1970.

Wood-Mosaic's answers to Coe & Payne's second interrogatories contained Wood-Mosaic's denial that it sold, distributed, or otherwise marketed R-65 in Fulton County or Georgia, but its admission that it filled orders received from Georgia customers and shipped R-65 F.O.B. in the total amount of 957 gallons and total value of $ 2,288 for the years 1965 through 1968. In answer to a query as to whether Wood-Mosaic recommended the use of R-65 adhesive, Wood-Mosaic referred to its installation manual; that manual requires the use of R-65 with the parquet flooring in question.

Overall Paint's answers to Coe & Payne's first interrogatories showed that Overall Paint sold roof coating [***15] to two Georgia concerns (not parties to this litigation) in 1968 and 1969 resulting in shipments from Overall Paint in Ohio to its customers in Georgia. Nonetheless, Overall Paint denied transacting business in the State of Georgia.

Overall Paint's answers to Coe & Payne's second interrogatories showed that the gross dollar volume of its direct sales to Georgia customers in 1968 and 1969 was $ 14,100. Overall Paint's answers showed that Wood-Mosaic (Louisville, Kentucky) was its sole customer, that some $ 44,000 worth of R-65 had been sold by Overall Paint to Wood-Mosaic during the years 1966-1968, and that Wood-Mosaic Corporation "was the exclusive distributor of R-65 adhesives."

Atlanta Flooring's answers to Coe & Payne's interrogatories showed that during the years 1965 through 1968 it purchased R-65 adhesive from Wood-Mosaic in the amount of 957 gallons and in the dollar value of $ 2,288. In addition, Wood-Mosaic sold in excess of $ 98,000 worth of miscellaneous flooring products to Atlanta Flooring during the years 1965 through 1970.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.

 

1877 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hart v. Columbus


No. 46762


Court of Appeals of Georgia


125 Ga. App. 625; 188 S.E.2d 422; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 1429


January 5, 1972, Argued  
March 3, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens disputed rulings by the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia), which, after overruling the motions by appellees, Columbus, Georgia and others, for directed verdict, reversed itself and entered a declaratory judgment for appellees. The citizens argued that the superior court had no authority to reverse its first decision and ordinances at issue were not reasonable and they were invalid under the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances, which established a new system of ad valorem taxation, were enacted under the charter of Columbus, Georgia, a new body politic. The trial judge denied appellees' motions for directed verdict ruling that there were issues of fact in dispute. On appeal, the court held that, under § 50(b) of the Civil Practice Act, 1966 Ga. Laws 609, 656, as amended, the judge acted within the authority given him by Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-150(b). The reasonableness of the ordinances was a question of law for the trial judge. Further, the court held that the two challenged ordinances complied with the requirements as to the procedures to be followed prior to the creation of urban services districts. After reviewing each of the claims of the citizens, the court held that the ordinances were reasonable and not capricious or arbitrary; the taxation reasonably reflected differences in services. They violated neither the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV nor that of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. II. Nor did they constitute the arbitrary taking of property without compensation in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. III. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court upholding the ordinances.

 

1878 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 46784


Court of Appeals of Georgia


125 Ga. App. 607; 188 S.E.2d 416; 1972 Ga. App. LEXIS 1425


January 3, 1972, Submitted  
March 2, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Driving U. I. Glynn State Court. Before Judge Little.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Glynn State Court (Georgia), which entered a conviction against him for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicants, and from an order denying his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and the denial of his motion for a new trial, and the court reversed his conviction. The court noted that there was sufficient evidence to convict him of the offense and accordingly, the denial of the motion for a new trial on general grounds was proper. Additionally, the fact that the trial court commented to the jury, during defense counsel's closing arguments, with respect to various traffic laws, did not justify the granting of defendant's motion for mistrial. The court found no harmful error for the trial judge's interjection at that time. However, the court held that a new trial was required because it was error for the trial court to have allowed the arresting officer to testify to the fact that defendant was offered the opportunity to take an intoximeter test and refused it. It was noted that defendant had insisted upon his right against self-incrimination both by not taking the test and again at the trial by objecting to the introduction in evidence of the fact that he refused to take the test. Such error required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for driving under the influence of intoxicants and held that a new trial was to be granted.

 

1879 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Corvair Furniture Mfg. Co. v. Bull


Nos. 46429, 46430


Court of Appeals of Georgia


125 Ga. App. 141; 186 S.E.2d 559; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 765


September 16, 1971, Argued  
November 16, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Actions for damages. Long Superior Court. Before Judge Caswell.

These separate suits were tried by separate juries at the September term, 1969, of Long Superior Court. The plaintiff in each of them sought recovery for personal injury, and in one the owner of the car also sought damages for its alleged destruction, because of negligence charged against the defendant's driver in operating a truck on the highway and bringing about a collision with the car in which plaintiffs were riding. There were verdicts for the plaintiffs. Motions for new trial were filed, amended and overruled, and defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a company and one of its truck drivers, sought review of a judgment from the Long Superior Court (Georgia) which, following a jury trial, found in favor of plaintiff injured parties in their actions to recover personal injuries from an automobile accident. The injured parties filed separate suits and each suit was tried by separate juries. The company and the truck driver challenged the method by which the jury panel was selected.


OVERVIEW: The injured party in each of the suits sought recovery for personal injury, and in one the owner of the car also sought damages for its alleged destruction, because of negligence charged against the driver in operating a truck on the highway and bringing about a collision with the car in which the injured parties were riding. There were verdicts for the injured parties. Motions for new trial were filed, amended and overruled, and company and driver appealed. The company and the truck driver contended that method of selecting the jury panel was unconstitutional and that counsel for the plaintiffs was the clerk of the county commissioners and exerted his influence upon them in the selection of names for submission to the judge of the superior courts and from which he was bound to appoint the jury commissioners. The court held that the company and its truck driver failed to file a timely attack on the jury selection process and the constitutionality of the legislation and thereby waived such grounds. The court also concluded that the allegations of conflict of interest against counsel for the injured parties were waived by the failure to file a motion to disqualify counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

1881 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Morton v. Retail Credit Co.


No. 46345


Court of Appeals of Georgia


124 Ga. App. 728; 185 S.E.2d 777; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 1085


June 29, 1971, Argued  
October 7, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1971. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Dismissal of action. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) which, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-137(d), dismissed his claim for libel because of his unexcused delay in serving answers to interrogatories served by defendant company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a complaint against the company that merely alleged jurisdiction, a libel, and resulting damage. The company served interrogatories upon plaintiff in an effort to gain more information as to his claim. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's action because of his unexcused delay in serving answers to the interrogatories. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-137(d), the trial court was authorized to dismiss plaintiff's complaint because he did not submit his answers to the interrogatories within 15 days of receiving them, as required by Ga. Code Ann. §§ 81A-133, 38-2108, nor did plaintiff seek an extension of time in which to serve the answers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing plaintiff's claim for libel because of his unexcused delay in serving answers to interrogatories served by the company.

 

1882 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ansley v. State


Nos. 46215, 46216


Court of Appeals of Georgia


124 Ga. App. 670; 185 S.E.2d 562; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 1065


May 6, 1971, Argued  
September 27, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 22, 1971. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Bribery. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Holt.

Richard A. Petree, Sr., an alderman of the City of Atlanta, and Benjamin Hugh Ansley, as his abettor, were tried together, convicted, and sentenced under Count 2 of an indictment alleging a violation of Code Ann. § 26-2304 (b) on March 5, 1970, in soliciting $ 30,000 for an agreement to procure the passage of zoning legislation by the Board of Aldermen. The same jury simultaneously acquitted the defendants under Count 1 of the indictment, alleging a violation of Code Ann. § 26-2301, in soliciting $ 30,000 for Petree to use his influence and to obtain his vote for the passage of the same zoning legislation described in Count 2. The appeals are substantially identical.



DISPOSITION: We find no error for any reason enumerated and each judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted them of bribery under Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2304(b).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendants of bribery under Ga. Code Ann. § 26-2304(b). The court affirmed those convictions on appeal. The court reasoned that the electronic recordings that were made pursuant to an order that authorized the surveillance of defendants were properly admitted because they were timely returned to the issuing judge under Ga. Code Ann. § 26-3004(c). The court also held that the order that authorized the surveillance was valid because the record clearly showed that the order complied with the applicable federal and state statutes. The court further opined that defendants' constitutional rights were not violated because the surveillance was not interrogation to which a right to counsel attached and defendants were only suspects that were not in custody at that time. The court further found that the convictions were consistent with a not guilty verdict. The verdict purported to allege aspects of the same acts to state two offenses that were based on the same transaction due to a distinction between an accusation of soliciting a sale of a vote of soliciting the sale of influence in procuring favorable legislative action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of bribery.

 

1883 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Thomas


No. 46401


Court of Appeals of Georgia


124 Ga. App. 286; 183 S.E.2d 489; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 899


June 28, 1971, Argued  
July 16, 1971, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.

The City of Atlanta adopted the following ordinance: "It shall be unlawful for any person to exhibit or perform in any hall, house or public place in the city any indecent, immoral or lewd play or dance, or to sing to a public audience any sacrilegious, indecent, vulgar or lewd song. It shall be the duty of the police and officers of the city to arrest every person violating this section in their presence, or on complaint of any citizen of a violation thereof by any person." Shirley Thomas filed an action in the Superior Court of Fulton County stating that she intends to dance topless, that the ordinance which is construed by police to forbid this activity is unenforceably vague and also violates designated First and Fourteenth Amendment standards and is therefore void, and praying a judgment to this effect with incidental injunctive features. Attached as an exhibit to the petition is a letter from H. T. Jenkins, Atlanta Chief of Police, to plaintiff's counsel stating that present ordinances prohibit topless dancing; that persons violating same "would have to take the consequences" and would also place the [***2] night club's permit in jeopardy.

A motion to dismiss the petition was denied and a judgment entered declaring the ordinance to be unconstitutional, which rulings are here enumerated as error.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Atlanta Chief of Police, challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which denied his motion to dismiss a declaratory judgment petition filed by appellee, a woman who wished to dance topless, and entered a judgment declaring an Atlanta ordinance to be unconstitutional. The ordinance at issue prohibited, inter alia, "indecent, immoral, or lewd" plays and dances.


OVERVIEW: The city of Atlanta adopted an ordinance prohibiting "indecent, immoral, or lewd" plays and dances. The woman sought a declaratory judgment that the ordinance, which was construed by police as forbidding topless dancing, was unenforceably vague and also violated designated First and Fourteenth Amendment standards. The trial court denied the police chief's motion to dismiss the woman's petition and entered a judgment declaring the ordinance unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that a decision as to the validity of the ordinance would, by its very nature, be abstract or advisory only. The court noted that topless dancing was not a part of the woman's employment contract, but that her employer had in fact prohibited her from doing so while the ordinance was in effect. Hence, the woman's right to dance was not impaired, and no property right was at stake. The court also noted that, as to the possible infringement of First Amendment freedoms, and the fact that fear of arrest under a possibly unconstitutional ordinance was involved, it was infinitely preferable to try the issues involved after rather than before the fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the police chief's motion to dismiss the woman's complaint and declared Atlanta's indecency ordinance to be unconstitutional.

 

1884 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


West v. Baumgartner


Nos. 45908, 45909, 45910, 45911, 45912, 45913


Court of Appeals of Georgia


124 Ga. App. 318; 184 S.E.2d 213; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 912


January 8, 1971, Argued  
July 7, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1971. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.



DISPOSITION: Judgments in cases numbers 45908, 45910 and 45912 (main appeals) are affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, landowners, trustees, trust beneficiaries, attorney, and corporation, sought review of the judgment from the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their respective motions for summary judgment to dismiss appellee fishermens' claims for malicious prosecution. The fishermen sought review of the dismissal of their false imprisonment claims and denial of their summary judgment motions.


OVERVIEW: The fishermen filed complaints for false imprisonment and malicious prosecution against defendants based on their arrest for fishing in the waters of another. The fishermen had been acquitted. The trial court granted defendants' motions for summary judgment as to the false imprisonment claims but denied the motion as to the malicious prosecution claims. The fishermen's summary judgment motions were denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court but it reversed the denial of the corporation's motion. The court held: (1) that the Act of 1902, 1902 Ga. Laws § 1, only privatized the fishing for fish of the nature of oysters, clams and shell; (2) that, since the fishermen were using hook and line, they were not fishing for such fish, and thus, were violating no private right; (3) that the false imprisonment claims merged into the malicious prosecution claims; (4) that the attorney's request for them to leave the water was not evidence of reasonable fear which would justify a separate claim for false imprisonment; and (5) that the attorney's equivocal discovery responses did not demand a finding that any defendant was not represented by his actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, but it reversed the trial court's denial of the corporation's motion for summary judgment.

 

1885 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Crosby v. Dixie Metal Co.


No. 45755


Court of Appeals of Georgia


124 Ga. App. 169; 183 S.E.2d 59; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 861


November 2, 1970, Submitted  
June 16, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 8, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Complaint. Bibb Civil Court. Before Judge Carlisle.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an individual, appealed the judgment of the Bibb Civil Court (Georgia), which overruled his motion to set aside a civil judgment in favor of plaintiff metal company.


OVERVIEW: The company brought an action against defendant in the trial court. A verdict was directed for the company, and defendant filed a motion to set aside the judgment based on the contention that the Georgia Civil Practice Act (Act) applied to the trial court and that, since he had 30 days in which to file his answer, the case could not be tried nor any judgment rendered against him prior thereto without his consent. The motion was overruled, and defendant appealed. The court noted that it clearly appeared from the passage of the Act that the legislature intended for it to apply to all courts of record. The court held that, because the Act served as an implied repeal of 1955 Ga. Laws pp. 2552, 2560, then no ordinary action could be tried in the trial court prior to the expiration of the 30-day period given for filing an answer to a complaint in O.C.G.A. § 81A-112(a), even though an answer has already been filed prior thereto, unless it was done by consent of the parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1886 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hospital Authority of Emanuel County v. Gray


No. 45804


Court of Appeals of Georgia


123 Ga. App. 415; 181 S.E.2d 299; 1971 Ga. App. LEXIS 1247


January 4, 1971, Submitted  
February 4, 1971, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 5, 1971. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Wheeler Superior Court. Before Judge O'Connor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital sought review of a judgment from the Wheeler Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained cross-defendant physician's motion for a judgment on the pleadings in the hospital's cross-claim seeking judgment against the physician for sums expended.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a malpractice claim against the physician and the hospital, to which the hospital answered setting up various defenses and filed a cross-claim against the physician alleging that any negligence was his because he was not authorized to use the hospital facilities to perform the surgery resulting the injury. The patient subsequently entered into a covenant to forego legal action against the hospital, which resulted in the hospital's dismissal as a party defendant. The following year, the hospital amended its cross-claim and sought judgment against the physician for the sums formerly expended by it to obtain the covenant with the patient. The physician's motion for a judgment on the pleadings was granted and the hospital appealed. The outcome of the matter was rooted in procedural law in that the hospital's cross-claim was no longer pending at the time it was amended because the trial court had filed a consent order reciting that the patient's claims had been settled and the action dismissed with prejudice. As a result, the hospital was not permitted to amend the cross-claim one year later in an effort to convert it into an action for damages against a co-defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the physician's motion for a judgment on the pleadings in the hospital's cross-claim seeking judgment to recover the sums formerly expended by it to obtain a covenant.

 

1887 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Boatner v. State


No. 45847


Court of Appeals of Georgia


122 Ga. App. 736; 178 S.E.2d 699; 1970 Ga. App. LEXIS 1019



November 4, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for bail bond. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following his conviction for possession of marijuana, defendant appealed a judgment from the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his motion for a supersedeas bond pending an appeal of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to two years in jail after he was convicted of a felony drug crime. He appealed his conviction and sentence on the basis that a certain statute was unconstitutional. Defendant moved for a supersedeas bond pending his appeal, and the trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court explained that it did not have jurisdiction to set bonds or bail pending appeals of convictions for crimes. The court noted that defendant's case involved a felony instead of a misdemeanor and held that the issue of whether to grant defendant bail pending his appeal was within the trial court's discretion. The court found that there was nothing in the record that demonstrated that the trial court had abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for a supersedeas bond.

 

1888 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Action Industries, Inc. v. Redisco, Inc.


No. 45619


Court of Appeals of Georgia


122 Ga. App. 754; 178 S.E.2d 735; 1970 Ga. App. LEXIS 1023


September 17, 1970, Submitted  
October 16, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 5, 1970. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to quash. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Mitchell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation brought an action against defendant, a nonresident foreign corporation, effecting personal service on the foreign corporation's president under the Long Arm Statute, O.C.G.A. § 24-113.1 et seq. The State Court of DeKalb County (Georgia) denied the foreign corporation's motion to quash service of process, and the foreign corporation sought review.


OVERVIEW: The foreign corporation's motion to quash contended that the application of O.C.G.A. § 24-115 was unconstitutional because, in light of the rules of the trial court, the foreign corporation was not given a reasonable time to prepare and file its answer. The court noted that 1951 Ga. Laws 2401, 2405 provided that each action was to be filed and summons issued thereon not less than 12 days prior to the first day of the court term and that the summons was to be served not less than nine days prior to the first day of that term, provided that service effected too late for a particular term was good for the next term. The action was filed on February 27 and was thus returnable to the April term, which commenced on April 6. Having been served on March 2, the foreign corporation was allowed more, not less, time than it would have been entitled to under general law. Therefore, the application of the local statutory practice rule was never a denial of due process in the trial court when the action was filed less than 12 days from the commencement of the next succeeding term, and the date for answer stated on the process was more than 30 days from the date of service of process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1889 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Register v. Stone's Indep. Oil Distribs.


No. 44908


Court of Appeals of Georgia


122 Ga. App. 335; 177 S.E.2d 92; 1970 Ga. App. LEXIS 868


January 8, 1970, Argued  
July 13, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 30, 1970. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Dodge Superior Court. Before Judge O'Connor.

Mrs. J. W. Bailey brought suit in the Superior Court of Dodge County for loss of consortium of her husband against James Ross, Jr. and his employer, Stone's Independent Oil Distributors, Inc.; Gerald NeSmith and his employer, Rentz Bus Lines, a partnership consisting of G. P. Register and Burtz V. Register; and Dallas Rodgers. The complaint alleged that one Charlie Mullis collided with the north side of a bridge on an east-west highway in such a manner that his automobile came to rest blocking the west-bound traffic lane. When plaintiff's husband came upon the scene, the automobile in which he was riding was parked, and he ran back to rescue Mullis who was injured and lying helpless in the wreckage. Stone's tanker truck, driven by Ross, drove onto the bridge traveling easterly and stopped in the immediate vicinity of the Mullis wreckage with its headlights on high beam; Rodgers approached from the opposite direction, traveling westerly, collided with the tanker truck and careened into the Mullis wreckage; NeSmith, who was following Rodgers driving [***2] the Rentz bus, collided with the Rodgers vehicle; and these collisions crushed plaintiff's husband against the Mullis vehicle. None of the defendants except Rodgers was a resident of Dodge County, it being alleged that venue was properly in Dodge Superior Court since the action was brought jointly and severally against all the defendants, including the resident Rodgers, for their joint and concurring negligence as set out in the complaint.

The plaintiff then amended her complaint by striking NeSmith and his employer Rentz as defendants, and Ross and his employer Stone filed a third-party complaint against them as third-party defendants after obtaining leave of the court pursuant to CPA § 14 (a) (Code Ann. § 81A-114 (a)). NeSmith and Rentz filed their substantially identical motions to dismiss the third-party complaint, one of the grounds being that it would be in violation of the Constitution of Georgia, Art. VI, Sec. XIV, Pars. IV and VI (Code Ann. §§ 2-4904, 2-4906) to apply CPA § 14 (a) (Code Ann. § 81A-114 (a)) to them since they were residents of counties other than the county where suit was brought. The trial court denied the motions to dismiss, certifying its order for [***3] immediate review, and the appeal was taken to the Supreme Court. That court transferred the case here. Register v. Stone's Independent Oil Distributors, 225 Ga. 490 (168 SE2d 133).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff wife's action for loss of consortium, third-party plaintiffs, driver and employer, filed a complaint against third-party defendants, driver and employer. Third-party defendants filed motions to dismiss on the grounds that venue was improper under Ga. Const. art. VI, § 14, para. 4, 6 and that the complaint was inadequate. The Dodge Superior Court (Georgia) denied the motions to dismiss, and third-party defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife's claim arose out of a multi-vehicle accident. Third-party plaintiffs impleaded third-party defendants under § 14 of the Civil Practice Act (CPA), Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-114. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. It stated that no independent claim had been made by third-party plaintiffs against third-party defendants, but only a claim for contribution in the event third-party plaintiffs were held liable. Thus, the court stated, this claim was an ancillary one contingent upon the outcome of the main case and could not properly be regarded as a "suit" or "case" for venue purposes. The court also rejected third-party defendants' argument that the third-party complaint was deficient because it did not specifically allege that third-party plaintiffs and third-party defendants were joint tortfeasors, stating that the third-party complaint was adequate under the notice-pleading provisions of § 8(a) of the CPA, Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-108(a). Finally, it held that it was not possible at this stage to determine whether third-party plaintiffs and third-party defendants were in fact joint tortfeasors, stating that this was a matter that addressed itself to factual proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision denying third-party defendants' motions to dismiss third-party plaintiffs' complaint in plaintiff's action for loss of consortium.

 

1890 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hawes v. National Service Industries, Inc.


Nos. 45109, 45122


Court of Appeals of Georgia


121 Ga. App. 775; 175 S.E.2d 34; 1970 Ga. App. LEXIS 1353


February 3, 1970, Argued  
April 30, 1970, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1970. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Sales tax. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shaw.

The State Revenue Commissioner appeals and the taxpayer cross appeals from a judgment of the trial court involving the meaning and application of provisions of the Sales and Use Tax Act, the taxpayer having commenced the action in the lower court seeking a refund of taxes paid which were allegedly illegally assessed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Revenue Commissioner and appellee taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which was entered in favor of the taxpayer, in a suit involving the meaning and application of provisions of the Sales and Use Tax Act. The taxpayer had commenced the action in the trial court, seeking a refund of taxes paid, which were allegedly illegally assessed.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner relied on the original language of the Act in respect to transactions before the approval of the amendment on February 19, 1965. On appeal, the court construed § 4 of the Act most strongly in favor of the taxpayer in view of its doubtful meaning. Considering the "in and out" exclusion together with the inclusions with respect to use and consumption of property after it had come to rest in Georgia, and resolving any doubt in favor of the taxpayer, the court concluded that the General Assembly, by the declaration of intent prior to February 19, 1965, did not intend to impose a use tax on the value of property moving "in and out" of Georgia, which merely had other property attached to it while it was in Georgia, and which was at all times intended for use in another state. The trial court properly concluded that the taxes and interest were illegally assessed as to a truck chassis. By cross appeal, the taxpayer contended that all other transactions before February 19, 1965, were exempt under § 4. The court disagreed. No controlling precedent had come to the court's attention to require a holding that the taxes created a multiple taxing situation on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the taxpayer.

 

1891 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Newman v. State


No. 45254


Court of Appeals of Georgia


121 Ga. App. 692; 175 S.E.2d 144; 1970 Ga. App. LEXIS 1315


April 13, 1970, Argued  
April 21, 1970, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Demand for trial. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Emeritus Hicks.

Defendant appeals from the denial of his motion for acquittal and from the order placing his case on the dead docket.

Defendant was indicted in January 1968. The case was called for trial in March and April and on both occasions defendant obtained a continuance. The case was also continued in June, although there is some dispute as to which side made the motion. When called again in September, the State asked for a continuance because the prosecuting witness was in Viet Nam. The same day defendant filed a demand for trial with the clerk. The State requested and received continuances in October, November and December, at which time the court ordered that the demand for trial be spread upon the minutes. In January and February of 1969, continuances were again granted to the State due to the absence of its witness. In February defendant's motion for acquittal was heard and denied, and the State's motion to place the case on the dead docket was granted. The trial court certified the order for immediate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied defendant's motion for acquittal and granted the State's motion to place defendant's case on the dead docket.


OVERVIEW: Defendant obtained several continuances of his criminal trial. The State was granted several continuances when it was learned that the complainant was in Viet Nam. The trial court denied defendant's motion for acquittal on speedy trial grounds, and granted the State's motion to have defendant's case placed on the dead docket. Defendant appealed, contending that his statutory speedy trial rights had been violated. The court held that it was impossible to tell whether the trial court had given defendant special permission pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 27-1901 to make a demand for a speedy trial because the trial court denied defendant's motion for acquittal but also stated erroneously that it did not have the power to grant special permission in accordance with § 27-1901. The court ordered the trial court to construe its order. With regard to the placement of defendant's case on the dead docket, the court held that such was unconstitutional because defendant had not given his permission therefor. However, the State was still entitled to try and make a reasonable showing for a continuance pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 27-2002.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied defendant's motion for acquittal and granted the State's motion to place defendant's case on the dead docket. The court remanded the matter with instructions that the trial court construe the order pertaining to the denial of defendant's motion for acquittal, and consider whether the State was entitled to a continuance in lieu of placement of the case on the dead docket.

 

1892 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Parham v. State


No. 44384


Court of Appeals of Georgia


120 Ga. App. 723; 171 S.E.2d 911; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 911


April 8, 1969, Submitted  
November 26, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Burglary. Chattooga Superior Court. Before Judge Coker.

The defendant appeals from his conviction and sentence of 20 years for burglary, and from the overruling of his motion for new trial, enumerating as error the court's charge to the jury that "Alibi as a defense must be established by the defendant to the reasonable satisfaction of the jury."



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for burglary after a jury trial before the Chattooga Superior Court (Georgia) and sentence of 20 years, and sought review of the overruling of his motion for a new trial. He claimed that it was error for the trial court to charge the jury that alibi as a defense had to be established by him to the reasonable satisfaction of the jury.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's charge was comparable to those approved by Georgia's appellate courts, but on review the court considered the charge in light of the United States Supreme Court's decision in Johnson v. Bennett, rendered five months after defendant's sentence. The court found that Johnson would be controlling if it meant that due process was violated by the jury charge. The court found that the charge impermissibly shifted the burden of proof to defendant and shattered the presumption of innocence. The court noted that alibi was not truly an independent affirmative defense, but rather was evidence in support of a plea of not guilty and should be treated as evidence tending to disprove defendant's presence at the time and place of an alleged crime. The court found that the charge was not harmless error and reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of burglary and sentencing him to 20 years. The court ruled that the trial court had erred in overruling his motion for a new trial.

 

1893 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


National Surety Corp. v. Hernandez


Nos. 44708, 44709


Court of Appeals of Georgia


120 Ga. App. 307; 170 S.E.2d 318; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 754


September 3, 1969, Argued  
September 12, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Savannah City Court. Before Judge Oliver.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor insurer appealed a decision of the Savannah City Court (Georgia), which ordered that service on defendant driver be perfected by publication under the provisions of Ga. L. 1966, p. 609, § 104(e)(1), and denied the insurer's motion to vacate that order, in action brought by plaintiffs, injury victims, against the driver to recover damages for injuries arising from the driver's negligent operation of his truck on a public highway.


OVERVIEW: The injury victims attempted to serve the driver by mailing registered letters to him at two different but similar addresses, which letters were returned marked "Unknown" and "Unclaimed." When attempts were made to serve him with registered mail at a different address, the letters were returned marked "Refused." The victims carried uninsured motorist coverage with the insurer, which intervened in order to contest the trial court's jurisdiction and the victim's right to recover. The victims then sought to perfect service on the driver by publication under the provisions of § 104(e)(1), and the trial court ordered it done. The insurer moved that the order be vacated because § 104(e)(1) did not provide for service by publication. The trial court denied the motion to vacate and the insurer appealed. The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that there was no provision in the Nonresident Motorists' Act, Ga. L. 1957, PP. 649, 650, the "long arm" statute, Ga. L. 1966, p 343, or in the statutes relative to torts for service on a nonresident defendant by publication and, consequently, that method of service was not available in the instant situation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment ordering service on the driver by publication.

 

1894 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Huguley v. State


No. 44506


Court of Appeals of Georgia


120 Ga. App. 332; 170 S.E.2d 450; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 772


May 29, 1969, Submitted  
September 2, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1969. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Public indecency. DeKalb Civil and Criminal Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the DeKalb Civil and Criminal Court (Georgia), which denied his motion that he be examined by a psychiatrist at county expense, denied his motion for a new trial, and convicted him of lewdness and public indecency. The case was before a supreme court on the alleged unconstitutionality of a criminal statute, but the case was transferred to the court after the issue was adversely decided against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion requesting an examination by a psychiatrist at the county's expense, in denying his motion for a new trial, and in charging a jury. The court affirmed his conviction. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying his motion for an examination by a psychiatrist where defendant had not entered a special plea of insanity at the time of trial. The court found that a letter from a psychiatrist, which supported defendant's claim of insanity, had not been submitted to the trial court and was considered newly discovered evidence. Defendant and his counsel had to show that the newly discovered evidence could not have been obtained by the exercise of ordinary diligence prior to trial, which they failed to do. Defendant's counsel caused defendant to be psychiatrically examined 3 days prior to trial and apparently took no affirmative steps to learn by expeditious means the examining psychiatrist's opinion. If defendant and his counsel had been diligent, a plea of insanity could have been asserted under O.C.G.A. §§ 27-1501, 27-1502. The trial court's charge to the jury was a correct statement of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1895 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Noles v. National Engine Rebuilding Co.


No. 44262


Court of Appeals of Georgia


119 Ga. App. 833; 169 S.E.2d 185; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 1270


February 3, 1969, Submitted  
May 16, 1969, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 20, 1969. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's compensation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.

In May, 1966, the claimant received an injury which arose out of and in the course of his employment. A standard form of agreement to pay compensation was approved by the State Board of Workmen's Compensation in July, 1966. The parties then submitted a stipulation to the board which was approved on August 24, 1966. However, on September 23, 1966, the claimant filed an appeal to the superior court where the award was reversed. Upon appeal to this court the judgment of the superior court was affirmed. U. S. Fidel. &c. Co. v. Gibby, 118 Ga. App. 758, 762 (165 SE2d 455). On March 27, 1968, the employer requested the board either to approve the stipulation, with certain portions deleted, or to set the claim down for a hearing to determine a change in condition. The matter then came on for a hearing to determine a change in condition. The award of the deputy director held in part that the claimant had undergone a change in condition in that total disability ceased as of July 18, 1966, and that the employer was authorized to discontinue payments of compensation [***2] as of that date.

The award was affirmed by the full board and the superior court. The claimant appealed and the case is here for review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the judgment of the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which was entered in favor of appellee employer in an action to determine whether the claimant's change in condition authorized discontinuance of workmen's compensation payments.


OVERVIEW: The employer who had been ordered to pay workmen's compensation benefits to a claimant requested the Georgia board of workmen's compensation for a hearing to determine a change in the claimant's condition. The deputy director held in part that the claimant had undergone a change in condition in that total disability ceased and that the employer was authorized to discontinue payments of compensation. The award was affirmed by the board and then by the superior court. On further appeal the court reversed and held that O.C.G.A. § 114-709 (1968) which amended the effective date by which a change of condition was determined and determined the res judicata aspect of an existing award affected the claimant's substantive rights and could not be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1896 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brackett v. Allison


No. 44133


Court of Appeals of Georgia


119 Ga. App. 632; 168 S.E.2d 611; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 1193


January 6, 1969, Submitted  
May 7, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Arbitration. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Kenyon.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment of the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which made an arbitrators' award the judgment of the court in an equitable action for an injunction against trespass.


OVERVIEW: An equitable action against trespass was referred to arbitrators by agreement of the parties. The superior court made the arbitrators' award the judgment of the superior court. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that it could review the judgment of the superior court even though the notice of appeal stated the wrong date for the judgment appealed from. It was an equitable proceeding, and the superior court entered a judgment that was signed by the judge. There was only one judgment and decree in the record. The court concluded that the action came under the Judiciary Act of 1799, O.C.G.A. § 7-224, not the Arbitration Act of 1856, O.C.G.A. §§ 7-201 to 7-223. The Arbitration Act applied only to cases originating out of court. Thus, the superior court did not err in making the award of the arbitrators the judgment of the court, even if the proceedings did not comply literally with the provisions of the Arbitration Act of 1856, because that Act was not applicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

1898 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Star Service & Petroleum Corp.


Nos. 44213, 44214


Court of Appeals of Georgia


119 Ga. App. 171; 166 S.E.2d 593; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 1030


February 4, 1969, Argued  
February 11, 1969, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.

James F. Galbreath was employed by Star Service & Petroleum Corporation as its supervisor in an area including a portion of Georgia, North Carolina and South Carolina. His duties required that he travel in the area and the company furnished him an automobile for that purpose, allowing him to garage it at his home and to use it for personal business or pleasure.

On Sunday, March 10, 1968, Galbreath and his wife went in the car to Roosevelt Baptist Church where he preached at the morning service. After conclusion of the service at about 12:10 p.m., he and his wife started back home and on the way the company car (which he was driving) collided at an intersection with that of Bingham Price, which was being operated by his daughter, Rebecca Ann, and she suffered injury.

Suits were filed by Mr. Price individually, and as next friend for his minor daughter against Mr. Galbreath and Star Service & Petroleum Corp. seeking the recovery of damages. Plaintiffs served interrogatories on Mr. Galbreath seeking to ascertain the nature of his employment, and whether he was acting as agent of his employer in operating the car [***2] at the time of the collision. He answered under oath that the car belonged to the company and that on that date he was generally in its employment, but asserted that his use of the car in going to and returning from the church was purely a personal use, having nothing to do with his duties of employment. He admitted that his use of the vehicle was with the consent and permission of his employer, that he had the discretion of garaging it at his home and that he had done so the night before. When he used it for personal purposes he paid for the gasoline and oil used. On this occasion he had gone directly from his home to the church, and was returning to his home without deviation and without any intention of going or stopping elsewhere. There had been no stops between the church and the intersection where the collision occurred save when required by traffic signs or signals.

Star Service & Petroleum Corp. moved for a summary judgment, submitting in support of its motion the interrogatories and Mr. Galbreath's answers. Plaintiffs sought to call him for oral examination at the hearing on the motion, but were denied the privilege of doing so.

The motion for summary judgment was [***3] sustained, and plaintiffs appeal, enumerating as error the sustaining of the motion and granting of a judgment dismissing Star Service & Petroleum as a defendant in the cases, and the refusal of the court to permit the calling of Galbreath for oral examination at the hearing on the motion.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, victim and her parent, appealed from the order of the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to defendant employer in an action for damages against defendant employee from an accident that occurred while he drove a company car on a personal trip. The trial court declined to allow plaintiffs to call the employee as a witness at the summary judgment hearing.


OVERVIEW: The employer furnished a car for the employee but allowed the employee to use it for personal matters. The employee filed an affidavit that stated that the accident occurred while he was on his way home from church and that he was not on the business of the employer. On appeal, the court held that the affidavit was not self-serving hearsay because it was contrary to the interests of the employee, it was under oath, and any benefit to the employer was incidental. The court found that the affidavit negated the allegations of respondeat superior and shifted the burden back to the plaintiffs on a motion for summary judgment under Ga. Code Ann. § 81A-156(c) to show that there was no material issue of fact. The court held that the statute did not require or favor oral testimony since such testimony would open the door to trial-like proceedings. The court rejected the argument that the garaging of the car at the home of the employee was for the convenience of the employer and made it liable. The court noted that statutes that had attempted to assign liability on mere ownership without fault had been held to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the employer and the denial of a request for oral testimony at the summary judgment hearing.

 

1899 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Freeman v. Valdosta


No. 44135


Court of Appeals of Georgia


119 Ga. App. 345; 167 S.E.2d 170; 1969 Ga. App. LEXIS 1292



January 31, 1969; March 11, 1969


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at: 119 Ga. App. 345 at 346.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of January 21, 1969, Reported at: 119 Ga. App. 345.



DISPOSITION: Judgment adhered to.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant made a second motion for rehearing of a decision of the superior court (Georgia), which refused to rule on the constitutionality of a statute because the issue was raised for the first time in a certiorari to the superior court from a judgment in a municipal court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought to have a certain statute declared unconstitutional. The superior court refused to rule on the issue, holding that the issue was brought up for the first time on appeal. The court affirmed the superior court. Appellant did not contend that he had made a proper attack on the constitutionality of the statute in the recorder's court. Appellant contended this was unnecessary because the recorder orally stated he knew the case was to determine certain constitutional issues. The court held that a mere statement by the judge trying the case that he understood constitutional issues might be determined in the case did not relieve appellant from making a proper constitutional attack for the trial judge to rule upon. Where it did not appear from the record that issues were made in the trial court, they could not be raised by certiorari in the superior court, and reviewed in the court. The court was a court alone for the trial and correction of such errors of law as appeared from the record as made in the trial court. The same principle applied to the superior court upon petition for certiorari to an inferior court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

1904 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dinkler v. Jenkins


No. 43392


Court of Appeals of Georgia


118 Ga. App. 239; 163 S.E.2d 443; 1968 Ga. App. LEXIS 1279



July 31, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at: 118 Ga. App. 239 at 256.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of June 26, 1968, Reported at: 118 Ga. App. 239.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a motion for rehearing in an action against respondents concerning the sale of liquor.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that the court's original opinion held by implication that certain prohibitions contained in a 1938 act, such as the sale of liquor to minors, the operation of liquor businesses in close proximity to schools and churches, or the limitation as to the amount of license fees and taxes that might be imposed, did not apply to those selling mixed drinks. The court held that such an argument assumed that the local government failed to act in accordance with its power and authority to promulgate reasonable rules and regulations governing the conduct of any licensee, including hours of business, types of employees, and other matters that might fall within the police powers of such municipalities and counties. The court further held that the evidence demonstrated that the city adopted a comprehensive ordinance providing for hours of sale, sales to minors, and sales on election days.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's motion for rehearing.

 

1905 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dinkler v. Jenkins


No. 43392


Court of Appeals of Georgia


118 Ga. App. 239; 163 S.E.2d 443; 1968 Ga. App. LEXIS 1363


January 11, 1968, Argued  
June 26, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 31, 1968. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Dyer.

Carling L. Dinkler, Jr., d/b/a Dinkler Plaza Hotel, and fourteen other plaintiffs brought suit against Herbert T. Jenkins, Chief of Police of the City of Atlanta, and various law enforcement officials of Fulton County and the Atlanta Judicial Circuit, seeking a temporary restraining order, interlocutory injunction, and declaratory judgment based upon the contention that plaintiffs are entitled to pursue their businesses of selling distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises until 2 a.m. following midnight on Saturdays.

Omitting allegations pertaining to the propriety of the remedies sought, the petition alleges in substance as follows:

By virtue of Ga. L. 1964, p. 771, any municipality lying within a county having a population of 40,000 or more in which the sale of alcoholic beverages is permitted by law is authorized to conduct a special referendum for the purpose of determining whether or not the sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises should be permitted. Among other things, the 1964 Act provides [***2] that cities holding a favorable referendum shall have the full power and authority to adopt all reasonable rules and regulations governing the qualifications and criteria for issuance of licenses to sell distilled spirits or alcoholic beverages for beverage purposes by the drink for consumption only on the premises and to promulgate reasonable rules and regulations governing the conduct of the licensees, including the regulation of hours of business. Pursuant to this Act the City of Atlanta conducted a favorable referendum and adopted an ordinance providing for the licensing of establishments to engage in the business of selling distilled spirits by the drink. The ordinance, attached to the petition as an exhibit, provides in Section 30 (d) that licensees for the sale of spirituous liquors by the drink shall not engage in the sale or permit the consumption of spirituous liquors between the hours of 2 a.m. Sunday and 9 a.m. Monday. It is alleged that the plaintiffs are licensed owners and operators of establishments in the City of Atlanta engaged in the business of selling distilled spirits and alcohol by the drink for consumption on the premises, and that defendants seek to close [***3] the establishments at 12 midnight on Saturdays.

The State Revenue Commissioner was allowed to intervene as a party defendant, and all defendants, with the exception of Police Chief Jenkins, filed general demurrers to the petition. From the sustaining of the demurrers and the dismissal of the petition, plaintiffs appealed to the Supreme Court. That court held that the case was not one within its jurisdiction and transferred it to this court. Dinkler v. Jenkins, 223 Ga. 807 (158 SE2d 381).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bar operators appealed from a judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained the demurrer of defendant officials to the operators' petition for injunctive and declaratory relief to prevent the officials from prohibiting the sale of liquor by the drink after midnight on Saturdays.


OVERVIEW: The officials contended that the operators were prohibited from selling liquor after midnight by the "tippling house statute", Ga. Code Ann. § 26-6105, which prohibited keeping a bar open "on the Sabbath day or Sabbath night", and by two provisions of the 1938 Act, Ga. Code Ann. §§ 1079, 1060, which re-authorized the sale of liquor for off-premises consumption after repealing a general prohibition, and prohibited sale from midnight Saturday to midnight Sunday night. The operators asserted that the sale until 2:00AM Sunday morning was allowed under a local ordinance passed pursuant to the 1964 Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 1083. On appeal, the court reversed the superior court order sustaining the officials' demurrer. The court interpreted "Sabbath" under the "tippling house statute" as precluding sale from dawn Sunday until midnight, thus inapplicable. The court held that the 1938 Act pertained only to sales for off-premise consumption, thus did not conflict with the "1964 Act" which specifically authorized municipalities to regulate sales by the drink, thus the local ordinance permitting the operators to remain open until 2:00 AM was a valid exercise of the authority conferred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court judgment which had sustained a demurrer by the officials to the operators' petition for injunctive and declaratory relief to prevent the officials from prohibiting the sale of liquor by the drink after midnight on Saturdays.

Britt v. Gainesville


No. 43638


Court of Appeals of Georgia


118 Ga. App. 40; 162 S.E.2d 740; 1968 Ga. App. LEXIS 1298


May 8, 1968, Submitted  
June 5, 1968, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1968. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari from city court. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Kenyon.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained the action of a trial court that found defendant guilty of violating the City's ordinance that prohibited the blocking of a public crossing by a railroad train, or car, or locomotive.


OVERVIEW: After he was found guilty of violating the City's ordinance that prohibited the blocking of a public crossing by a railroad train, or car, or locomotive, the superior court sustained the trial court's judgment, and defendant sought further review. On appeal, defendant contended that he was not liable under O.C.G.A. § 94-517. The court found that the evidence showed that it was possible that an engineer, or a brakeman, or a flagman might have halted the railroad car without the knowledge of, or instructions of, defendant. Therefore the court ruled that the City failed to carry the burden of proving defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Based on the determination that the conviction was unauthorized by the evidence, the court held that it was unnecessary to determine whether the constitutionality of § 94-517 was properly raised in the trial court by the prosecution. The court held that it was also unnecessary to determine whether the trial court erred when it held that the statute was unconstitutional or whether a "defense" under the statute was proven. The court ruled that the trial court erred when it overruled defendant's petition for certiorari.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction.
