Thompson v. Metro. Life Ins. Co.


No. 42726


Court of Appeals of Georgia


115 Ga. App. 724; 155 S.E.2d 728; 1967 Ga. App. LEXIS 1225


April 4, 1967, Submitted  
May 16, 1967, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on insurance policy. Fulton Civil Court. Before Judge Webb.

John P. Thompson commenced this action in the Civil Court of Fulton County, on May 26, 1966, against the Metropolitan Life Insurance Company, to recover weekly sickness and accident benefits allegedly due under a group insurance policy issued to General Motors Corporation by the insurer, under which the insurer had issued the plaintiff a certificate of coverage effective October 1, 1961. The claim is for an injury which the plaintiff allegedly incurred on May 14, 1963. Under the terms of the group policy as shown by the certificate of coverage attached to the petition, the plaintiff had two years from the time within which proof of claim was required to commence an action. He commenced the action after the expiration of this period, but within three years. The trial judge sustained a general demurrer to the petition and the plaintiff appeals from this judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.

 

1915 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Blackburn v. Hall


No. 42585


Court of Appeals of Georgia


115 Ga. App. 235; 154 S.E.2d 392; 1967 Ga. App. LEXIS 1074


January 3, 1967, Argued  
January 25, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 17, 1967. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Election contest. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Banke from Clayton Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a congressional candidate opposing an election contest (opponent) brought by appellee contestant pursuant to the Georgia Election Code of 1964 (Election Code), § 34-1701 et seq., sought review of an order of the Dekalb Superior Court (Georgia) that denied the opponent's motion for a demurrer.


OVERVIEW: Along with other alleged tabulation errors, the contestant challenged the rejection of "over-votes," which resulted when a voter punched a hole in the "votermatic" card for every candidate from a particular party, but for the congressional race only, also punched a hole for the candidate for the opposite party. The superior court denied the opponent's motion for demurrer. On appeal, the court held that the alleged "over-votes" were not a basis for relief, but that demurrer was properly denied, based on the other issues. The court held that the superior court had jurisdiction under the Election Code, despite the fact that Congress had authority to decide not to seat either candidate, and that the election contest, while a special proceeding, was a civil case, thus was included within the provisions of the Appellate Practice Act of 1965, 1965 Ga. Laws p. 18. The court held that the 1965 amendment to the Election Code was intended to invalidate over-votes and prevent their counting and tabulation, because that kind of ballot was ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which denied the opponent's motion for a demurrer in the contestant's proceeding under the Election Code.

 

1916 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brissette v. Munday


Nos. 42432, 42473


Court of Appeals of Georgia


115 Ga. App. 131; 153 S.E.2d 606; 1967 Ga. App. LEXIS 1038


November 9, 1966, Argued  
January 20, 1967, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 3, 1967. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Pye.

This appeal and cross appeal originated as an action in Fulton Superior Court by Suzanne E. Brissette against B. C. Munday, Jr. and John L. Brissette, seeking recovery for personal injuries she sustained on February 12, 1962, when an automobile in which she was riding on the right front seat, driven by John L. Brissette, her brother, collided with an automobile driven by Munday. The collision occurred on Lake Forrest Drive in Fulton County in the middle of the street at the intersection of the street and the driveway to Munday's home on the west side of the street. Munday was proceeding out of the driveway into the street, and John L. Brissette was proceeding north on Lake Forrest Drive. The left front of the Munday vehicle collided with the left front of the Brissette vehicle, and the Brissette vehicle veered to the right off the street into a tree. The case was tried before a jury, and on October 5, 1964, the jury returned a verdict for plaintiff against B. C. Munday, Jr. only, for $ 15,000. Munday appealed on August 24, 1965, from the overruling [***2] of his motion for a new trial on July 30, 1965. This court on January 28, 1966, held that John L. Brissette was a proper party appellee, and that a new trial should have been granted as to both defendants. Munday v. Brissette, 113 Ga. App. 147 (148 SE2d 55). The Supreme Court granted certiorari, and on May 26, 1966, held that Munday had no right to object to the verdict of the jury discharging his co-defendant Brissette. Brissette v. Munday, 222 Ga. 162 (149 SE2d 110). On June 21, 1966, this court conformed its opinion to the mandate of the Supreme Court, and amended its judgment to show that "the court did not err in denying a new trial as to the co-defendant, John L. Brissette." Munday v. Brissette, 113 Ga. App. 849 (149 SE2d 829). Thereafter, by order entered on August 31, 1966, the trial court overruled plaintiff's amended motion for a new trial as against the defendant John L. Brissette, action on her motion having been previously suspended during litigation in this court and the Supreme Court on the issue of whether Munday was entitled to a new trial as against the plaintiff, or both the plaintiff and defendant Brissette. The plaintiff Brissette now appeals from the overruling [***3] of her motion for new trial, as against the defendant Brissette, and the defendant Brissette cross appeals seeking a reversal of the trial court's ruling on his demurrers, a motion for a directed verdict, and an order of the trial court striking a portion of the remittitur of the Court of Appeals from the files of the trial court. Additionally the defendant Brissette moves to dismiss the plaintiff Brissette's appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on appeal; affirmed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger and defendant driver sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which, on remand, overruled the passenger's motion for a new trial as against the driver and overruled the driver's demurrers. The driver also filed motions for a directed verdict, for an order striking a remittitur, and to dismiss the passenger's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The driver struck another vehicle as it was exiting from a driveway. The passenger filed a personal injury action and a verdict for the passenger against the other vehicle's owner only was returned. On the first appeal, the court held that the driver was a proper party appellee and that a new trial should have been granted to both defendants. The state supreme court granted certiorari, and held that the other vehicle's owner had no right to object to the verdict of the jury discharging the driver. On remand, the trial court overruled the passenger's amended motion for a new trial as against the driver and the driver's demurrer. On appeal, the court held that under § 2(a) of the Appellate Practice Act of 1965, 1966 Ga. Laws 494, the passenger had the right to appeal the adverse determination of her motion for a new trial. The court determined that the passenger's allegations against the driver were clearly sufficient to have placed him on notice of the duty of care owed and that the trial court did not err in overruling the driver's demurrers. The court found that the trial court's raising of constitutional issues in denying the passenger's motion for a new trial was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order from the trial court as to the passenger's appeal of the denial of the motion for new trial, but affirmed as to the driver's cross-appeal.

 

1917 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Brown


Nos. 42399, 42400


Court of Appeals of Georgia


114 Ga. App. 650; 152 S.E.2d 641; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 885


November 9, 1966, Argued  
November 21, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Intervention. Catoosa Superior Court. Before Judge Coker.

Brown brought suit against Blakely, "as defendant," and State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company, "as nominal defendant," for damages arising out of an automobile collision allegedly attributable to the negligence of Blakely.

In the petition as amended State Farm was named "as nominal defendant" under Code § 56-407A (Code Ann. § 56-407.1), and it was alleged that State Farm had an agent in Catoosa County "upon whom service of process can be perfected; therefore, said nominal defendant is subject to the jurisdiction of this court."

The petition as amended further alleged: "That the defendant, David Charles Blakely, owner and operator of the vehicle causing injury and damage to the plaintiff, was not covered by a policy of property damage or bodily injury liability insurance; therefore, same was an 'uninsured motor vehicle.' That the nominal defendant, State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company, issued a policy of automobile liability insurance to the plaintiff, which insurance policy provides for coverage to him for damage caused by an uninsured motorist, and said policy was in full force and effect [***2] at all times herein mentioned. Said insurance company is named herein as a nominal defendant in order that a copy of the petition and process can be served upon it, as prescribed by law, as though said insurance company was a party defendant."

The prayer was for process requiring "said defendants" to answer the complaint and for judgment against "defendant, David Charles Blakely." Process was issued against Blakely and State Farm, and a copy of the petition and process was served upon State Farm's agent.

State Farm, as "one of the defendants in the above-stated case," filed a general demurrer, an answer, and a motion to purge the petition of prejudicial matter by striking its name as a party defendant. It also filed an application for leave to intervene, alleging that the application was filed before any party was in default and that it was necessary that it be allowed to file defensive pleadings as an intervenor, as distinguished from a defendant, in order to protect its rights. Defendant Blakely also filed an answer.

Plaintiff filed motions to dismiss the demurrer and the answer of "the nominal defendant, State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company," upon the grounds that [***3] the nominal defendant was not a real party to the action and that there was no provision of law authorizing the filing of a demurrer and answer by the "nominal defendant." Plaintiff also moved to dismiss the application for leave to intervene upon similar grounds.

The lower court denied plaintiff's motions to dismiss the general demurrer, answer, and application for leave to intervene. It also overruled the general demurrer and denied the motion to purge filed by State Farm "as one of the defendants." The application for leave to intervene was allowed, the order reciting that State Farm was permitted to plead and to protect all of its rights in the litigation.

State Farm appealed from the orders overruling its general demurrer and denying its motion to purge; in the cross appeal plaintiff assigns as error the order allowing the application for leave to intervene and the orders denying its motions to dismiss the general demurrer, answer and application for leave to intervene.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on the main appeal; affirmed on the cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged orders of the Catoosa Superior Court (Georgia) overruling its general demurrer and motion to purge while plaintiff appealed the allowance of defendant's application for leave to intervene in uninsured motorist action.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged orders of lower court overruling its general demurrer and motion to purge while plaintiff appealed the approval of the application for leave to intervene in the lawsuit against the known uninsured motorist. The court reversed the denial of the general demurrer and motion to purge, but affirmed the application for leave to intervene. The court looked at the plain language of Ga. Code § 56-407(A) and found while it precluded defendant from being named as a party defendant, it provided that defendant should be served with notice of the lawsuit because of its potential liability under the uninsured motorist policy. The court found defendant had a due process right to intervene regarding the issuance of the judgment against the uninsured motorist and to insure the jurisdiction of the court in order to protect the interest of its insured and any interests that would be effected by the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed orders overruling defendant's general demurrer and motion to purge, but affirmed the order allowing the application for leave to intervene since its interests and the interests of its insured would be effected by the judgment.

 

1918 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Fid. & Casualty Co. v. Whitehead


Nos. 42199, 42200


Court of Appeals of Georgia


114 Ga. App. 630; 152 S.E.2d 706; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 879


September 6, 1966, Argued  
October 26, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 16, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's compensation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.

William E. Whitehead, an employee of Whitehead Die Casting Company, suffered a hernia arising out of and in the course of his employment November 1, 1960, from which disability began January 18, 1961. An agreement for the payment of compensation was entered into February 1, filed with the compensation board and approved by it February 6. Payment for total disability was made for 13 weeks and then terminated because the employee refused to submit to surgery for a correction of the hernia. His counsel directed a letter to the board on April 19 asserting that, although the employee continued to be disabled, the insurer had discontinued the compensation payments, and asked that the matter be assigned for hearing.

The employer's insurer notified the board on April 26 that it was represented by counsel, who would appear for it at the hearing to be scheduled.

A hearing was set for June 1, and on May 29, employee's counsel requested that it be postponed because of the physical inability of the employee to attend. The hearing was postponed and no request [***2] was made by either party for a rescheduling of the matter until June 19, 1963, some two years later, when the insurer's counsel asked that it be reassigned and that a determination of whether there had been a change in the employee's condition be made. A hearing was scheduled for August 2 and all parties were notified. Upon the opening of the hearing, counsel for the employee moved that his original request for a hearing be withdrawn and dismissed. The motion was denied, and the hearing proceeded.

The deputy director made his findings of a change in condition and entered an award December 19, 1963, by which compensation was terminated as of April 19, 1961, the date of the original request for hearing by the employee after the employer had ceased making compensation payments. The award was appealed to the full board and after argument a majority, being of the opinion that there was ample evidence to support the findings made by the deputy director, adopted them and made his award that of the full board. An appeal was entered to Fulton Superior Court and on April 12, 1965, an order was entered sustaining the appeal, remanding the matter to the board with direction that it hold [***3] its award in abeyance pending the outcome of a proceeding which the employee had filed in Fulton Superior Court July 31, 1963, seeking a judgment for unpaid compensation alleged to have been due during the period from April 19, 1961, to June 27, 1963. The order provided that it was without prejudice as to the merits of the claim, leaving the board free to reissue its award after determination of the pending proceeding in the superior court. There was no appeal from that order.

On September 3, 1965, the board gave notice to all parties of a hearing scheduled for September 27 for the purpose of determining on what date a cessation of payments of compensation by the insurer may have been authorized.

On February 28, 1966, a judgment was rendered in the superior court for the amount claimed to have been due as payments not made during the period from April 19, 1961, to June 27, 1963, with interest, from which this appeal was entered.

The employee cross appeals, enumerating as error the denial of his motion to dismiss his original request for a hearing after the cessation of payments, and the admission of certain pleadings as evidence in the hearing on the proceeding in the superior [***4] court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in both the main and cross appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and its workmen's compensation carrier, challenged a judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) awarding certain compensation to appellee, an injured worker. The worker cross-appealed, claiming that it was error for a state workmen's compensation board to deny his motion to dismiss his original request for a hearing following the employer's cessation of payments.


OVERVIEW: After suffering a work-related hernia, the worker received disability pay for 13 weeks. It ceased when the worker refused to undergo surgery. The worker sought a hearing on the cessation of payments, but later moved to withdraw the request, which motion was denied. In the interim, he suffered a mental breakdown, and when the case was heard two years later, an administrative finding of change of condition was made, and compensation was terminated. Meanwhile, the worker filed suit in the superior court for unpaid compensation and won an award. The employer and its carrier appealed, and the worker appealed the denial of his motion to withdraw his hearing request. The court affirmed both judgments. After rejecting jurisdictional claims based on competing interpretations of a repealed law, the court held that the administrative finding of change of condition was unauthorized because the worker's hernia, not his mental illness, was the condition at issue. But a finding as to the timing of the offer of surgical correction had to be made in order to determine the date on which payments were properly terminated. The court also gave directions for further administrative proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments below.

 

1919 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State Highway Dep't v. Calhoun


No. 42329


Court of Appeals of Georgia


114 Ga. App. 501; 151 S.E.2d 806; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 818


September 7, 1966, Argued  
September 28, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 24, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation of land. McDuffie Superior Court. Before Judge Stevens.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condemnees sought review of an order of the Superior Court of McDuffie County (Georgia), which entered judgment in favor of appellee state highway department in its action to condemn land.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment in favor of the state highway department in its condemnation action against the condemnees. On appeal, the condemnees alleged that the trial court erred in refusing to exclude the testimony of a witness because he did not relate his estimate of value to the time of taking. The court found that while the witness did not specifically state that his opinion was as to the value of the land on the date of the taking, it appeared that the plat made by the condemnor for the purpose of the proceeding was tendered to him in identifying the tract and he was then asked if he was familiar with the market value of the property. But the court determined that while the trial court's charge to the jury on estimated values and the condemnees right to actual market value was a correct statement of the law at the time the case was tried, it was in direct conflict with the provisions of 1966 Ga. Laws 320, 327, which stated that consideration was not to be given to any increase or decrease in the value of property actually taken resulting from the improvements in connection with which the right of eminent domain was being exercised.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

 

1920 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Darlington Corp. v. Finch


No. 41963


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 825; 149 S.E.2d 861; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 1216


May 4, 1966, Argued  
May 26, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tanksley.

In her petition plaintiff alleged that on January 7, 1963, she was the tenant of an apartment on the 12th floor of the Darlington Apartments, and that she and her sister got on one of the automatic elevators and descended to the ground floor, where they were to get off, and, as she attempted to leave the elevator the doors closed against her, causing her to fall and sustain certain injuries. She alleged that the door to the left was equipped with a rubber bumper which, when touched, would cause that door to open, while the door to the right was not so equipped, and that the defendant was negligent in failing to have both doors so equipped and in failing to provide her with a safe means of ingress and egress.

Upon trial of the case plaintiff testified that she lived in the apartment from shortly after the building opened for tenants in 1951, until after this occasion when she was injured in 1963, and that she had used and operated the elevators practically every day during that time except when she was out of town. She knew how they operated -- one [***2] just pushed the signal button and when the elevator came and opened its doors, one got on and pushed the button indicating the level at which she wished to get off. There is a button on the panel having "hold" on it, which will hold the door open if pushed, but she did not use that; if she had wanted to hold the door open she could just put up her hand and touch the rubber cushion on the left door, and she had done so many times, though she did not on this occasion. The elevator is of regulation size, well lighted, and on the occasion when she fell it was lighted as usual and operated just as it usually did. There were no foreign objects or anything of the kind causing her to trip or to slip and fall. The elevator door just struck her and she fell. Her sister, who was with her when she fell, testified to the same effect.

Westinghouse had made and installed the elevators and its electrical engineer, testifying as an expert for the defendant, asserted that he inspected the elevator shortly after the accident and also at a later time and found it to be in proper working condition. It had been installed in accord with the American Standard and Safety Code, sponsored by the American [***3] Institute of Architects, the National Bureau of Standards, and the American Society of Mechanical Engineers. The equipment in 1963 was that which had been installed in 1951.

The Superintendent of Electrical Affairs for the City of Atlanta asserted that he had made annual inspections of the elevator from 1957 through 1964 and on each occasion found it to be in proper working condition and meeting all requirements of the city elevator ordinance.

There was no proof of any defect in the mechanism of the elevator, or of its automatic doors, or of any malfunctioning of them. There was no proof of any knowledge on the part of the defendant that there had been any lack of proper functioning in the elevator or its doors, or of any malfunctioning of them. There was no evidence that it had given trouble or that it had caused others to fall on any previous occasion.

The jury returned a verdict for plaintiff, and to the overruling of a motion for new trial and of a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with direction that a judgment be entered for the defendant in accordance with its motion for judgment n.o.v..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlord sought review of a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which entered judgment on a jury's verdict in favor of plaintiff tenant in her personal injury action for damages sustained in a fall caused by an elevator door hitting her as she exited the elevator. The trial court overruled defendant's motions for a new trial and judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: The tenant alleged that the landlord was negligent in its failure to equip both elevator doors of an elevator in her building with rubber bumpers that would cause the door to open when touched. Only one of the elevator doors was equipped with a bumper, and the tenant alleged that one of the elevator doors hit her as she attempted to leave the elevator and knocked her down. On appeal, the court reversed and directed the trial court to enter judgment notwithstanding the verdict in favor of the landlord. There was no basis to support a finding of negligence by the landlord or a failure by the landlord in its duty to exercise extraordinary care in the maintenance and operation of the elevator. The doctrine of res ipsa loquitur was inapplicable because mechanical devices, such as the elevator, get out of working order and become dangerous without negligence. The tenant testified that the elevator was operating normally. The landlord was not required to install bumpers on both elevator doors, the elevator was properly installed and had been in proper working order at the time of the accident, and was reasonably safe for all persons who operated it with ordinary care and diligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, entered on the jury's verdict in favor of the tenant in her personal injury action against the landlord and directed the trial court to enter judgment notwithstanding the verdict in favor of the landlord.

 

1921 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Glover


No. 41867


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 815; 149 S.E.2d 852; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 1214


March 7, 1966, Argued  
May 16, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 13, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on insurance policy. Sylvester City Court. Before Judge Monk.

This is an appeal from the City Court of Sylvester by State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company, which had filed defensive pleadings as intervenor (as allowed by order of the trial judge) in an automobile damage suit pending in the City Court of Sylvester. Appellant had issued its policy of automobile liability insurance containing "uninsured motorist" coverage which applied to the collision being sued on. Certain orders and rulings of the trial judge adverse to appellant are appealed to this court as being in error. For convenience, appellant is sometimes referred to herein as "State Farm" and/or "Intervenor," and Arthur Guarnieri is sometimes referred to herein as "plaintiff," the position he occupied in the trial court. On May 13, 1965, Arthur Guarnieri, by next friend, filed his suit for personal injuries in the City Court of Sylvester, against Junior Lee Jordan, alleged therein to be a resident of Colquitt County, and against William Glover, alleged therein to be a resident of Worth County. The petition alleged that the plaintiff sustained [***2] personal injuries and property damage for which the action was brought, allegedly caused by the negligence of the defendant, Junior Lee Jordan, while operating an automobile belonging to defendant William Glover which was involved in a collision with the motorcycle being operated by plaintiff. This petition was served on Junior Lee Jordan but was never served on William Glover. Plaintiff caused a copy of the petition in this matter to be served on State Farm as provided by Ga. L. 1964, pp. 306-309, which Act relates to uninsured motorists. No defensive pleadings or appearance has ever been made in the case by either Junior Lee Jordan or William Glover. State Farm filed its petition in the trial court for leave to intervene in the cause, alleging that it had issued an automobile liability insurance policy providing coverage to plaintiff for damages caused by an "uninsured motorist" under provisions of such insurance policy; that it had been served with a copy of the petition filed by the plaintiff; that it was necessary to protect State Farm's rights that it be given leave to intervene, made a party to the cause, and allowed to file an answer and other defensive pleadings to the [***3] plaintiff's petition; and that State Farm should be given an opportunity to resist the rendition of a judgment operating to its prejudice in the case. On June 19, 1965, at a time when no party was in default, the trial judge entered an order extending the time within which the insurance company might file "an answer, demurrers, pleas or any other pleadings" in the case for an additional period of time after the entry of the final order of the court granting or denying the petition for leave to intervene. This order was consented to in writing by the plaintiff's counsel. The trial court ordered the petition for leave to intervene filed and set a date for hearing thereon. The trial court entered an order on July 10, 1965, reciting that the petition to intervene having come on regularly to be heard on July 9, 1965, the court ordered that the petition for leave to intervene by State Farm be granted, and ordered that State Farm be made a party intervenor "authorized to make such appearances and to file such answer and other pleadings as it deems appropriate." Thereafter, State Farm filed a timely plea to the jurisdiction of the court on July 21, 1965, before filing its answers or demurrers [***4] to the petition. In this plea State Farm alleged that (1) Junior Lee Jordan is a resident of Colquitt County, Ga., is not a resident of Worth County, Ga., and that the Superior Court of Colquitt County has jurisdiction of this case and the City Court of Sylvester has not; (2) that at the time of filing of the plea to the jurisdiction by State Farm, Junior Lee Jordan has failed to file a plea to the jurisdiction or other defensive pleadings, though more than thirty days have elapsed since the time he was served with process and suit; (3) that intervenor has not waived jurisdiction as to the parties herein and any waiver by Junior Lee Jordan of jurisdiction would be prejudicial to this intervenor; and (4) that as of the date of the filing of the plea the codefendant, William Glover, has not been served with process or copy of the petition herein. Appellant filed demurrers to the petition and an answer. Appellant renewed its demurrers after the petition was amended by plaintiff. In its answer, appellant denied the material allegations of negligence contained in the petition. On August 12, 1965, appellant propounded interrogatories to plaintiff. On August 13, 1965, plaintiff propounded [***5] interrogatories to appellant. On August 21, 1965, appellant filed objections to the interrogatories propounded by plaintiff. On August 23, 1965, plaintiff filed objections to appellant's interrogatories. The attorney for plaintiff, H. P. Burt, filed an affidavit relating to the interrogatories on August 27, 1965. The attorney for appellant, Mr. George D. Busbee, filed an affidavit relating to the interrogatories on August 27, 1965. On August 28, 1965, the plaintiff filed an amendment striking paragraph 1 of the original petition, wherein plaintiff had alleged that Junior Lee Jordan was a resident of Colquitt County and inserting in lieu thereof a new paragraph 1 alleging that Junior Lee Jordan was a resident of Worth County. On September 11, 1965, plaintiff filed three motions in the case. They are as follows: "1. Comes now plaintiff and moves the court to dismiss intervenor's (State Farm Mutual Insurance Company) answer with respect to contesting the alleged negligence charged against defendant, Junior Lee Jordan, on the ground that said case is in default as to Junior Lee Jordan and the only issue remaining is the question of damages. Plaintiff moves the court to strike the [***6] following paragraphs to defendant's answers: 1, 2, 3, 4, that portion of paragraph 7 denying paragraph 9 of plaintiff's petition and paragraph 8." "2. Comes now plaintiff, and moves the court to dismiss intervenor's (State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company) demurrers on the ground; (I) There is no provision of law authorizing intervenor to file said demurrers." "3. Comes now plaintiff, and moves the court to dismiss intervenor's (State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company) plea to the jurisdiction on the ground: (I) A plea to the jurisdiction is a personal plea, which can only be filed by the defendant, Junior Lee Jordan. (II) Said action is in default as to defendant, Junior Lee Jordan, who was served personally in said State and county. (III) There is no provision of law authorizing intervenor to file said plea." Appellant filed a motion to dismiss the plaintiff's petition because plaintiff had wilfully failed and refused to respond to interrogatories to which no objections were filed by plaintiff, and that plaintiff had wilfully failed to answer interrogatories or cause any hearing to be held on his objections. On December 11, 1965, the court entered two orders. The [***7] first order reads as follows: "The plaintiff's motion to dismiss intervenor's answer with respect to the alleged negligence charged against defendant, Junior Lee Jordan, coming on for a hearing, and after due consideration of same, it is ordered that said motion be sustained and that the case be marked in default as to defendant, Junior Lee Jordan." The second order of December 11, 1965, reads as follows: "The plaintiff's motion to dismiss intervenor's plea to the jurisdiction, coming on for a hearing, after due consideration of same, it is ordered that said motion be sustained, and the said plea be dismissed." On January 3, 1966, the court entered an order overruling the demurrers of appellant as renewed. On January 3, 1966, the trial judge also entered the following order in this case: "With respect to the pending motions as filed in court in the above stated case, by the plaintiff in said case, and also by the intervenor in said case, pertaining to the interrogatories as filed in court by each of said respective parties hereto and more specifically pertaining to the admissibility and execution of certain numbered questions as propounded and contained in interrogatories as filed [***8] with the clerk of the court by each of said parties hereto, and, it now appearing to the court that said case is, in default as to the defendant in said case, no answer having been filed. And it further appearing, that the question involved in this cause of action is one of unliquidated damages, which of course is incumbent on the part of the plaintiff to prove. Accordingly, all motions and objections as made by each of the parties hereto, plaintiff and intervenor, with respect to interrogatories, are hereby overruled and denied, excepting such evidence only as may be applicable and admissible in establishing the amount of unliquidated damages in said case, and/or in mitigation thereof and which evidence when so submitted, the intervenor herein is not precluded from contesting the same in mitigation of the amount of such damages claimed by due cross examination as he may deem proper."

The insurance company appeals from the order of the court, dated January 3, 1966, overruling the general demurrers of Intervenor to plaintiff's petition as amended; the order of December 11, 1965, sustaining plaintiff's motion to dismiss Intervenor's answer; and from the order of December 11, 1965,  [***9] sustaining plaintiff's motion to dismiss Intervenor's plea to the jurisdiction.

Appellant's enumeration of errors is as follows: "1. The court erred in sustaining plaintiff's motion to dismiss appellant's plea to the jurisdiction by order dated December 11, 1965. 2. The court erred in sustaining plaintiff's motion to dismiss appellant's answer with respect to the alleged negligence charged against Junior Lee Jordan and marking this case in default as to defendant Junior Lee Jordan by order dated December 11, 1965. 3. The court erred in overruling appellant's demurrers and renewed demurrers on each and every ground thereof by an order dated January 3, 1966. 4. The court erred in overruling appellant's motion and objections and in sustaining plaintiff's motion and objections with respect to certain interrogatories in an order dated January 3, 1966. 5. The court erred in its order dated January 3, 1966, which order, in effect, held that intervenor could not contest the question of defendant's negligence but could only introduce evidence on the question of the amount of damages plaintiff is entitled to recover."



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed in part; affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor insurer challenged the decision of the Sylvester City Court (Georgia), which granted plaintiff insured's motion to dismiss the insurer's answer with respect to the alleged negligence charged against defendant uninsured tortfeasor and granted the insured's motion to dismiss the insurer's plea to the jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The insured serve notice of a lawsuit against the uninsured motorist pursuant to the Georgia uninsured motorist law, Ga. Code Ann. § 56-407.1. The insurer filed a motion that challenged the jurisdiction of the trial court and filed an answer that contested the issue of negligence. The trial court granted the insured's motion to dismiss the insurer's answer and the insured's motion to dismiss the insurer's challenge to jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the insurer could challenge jurisdiction and could contest liability because the uninsured motorist law allowed a first-party insurer to defend an uninsured motorist claim. The court also held that the insurer's general demurrer was properly overruled because the objection to the addition of a new cause of action by amendment was not properly raised where it was not to the amendment alone and did not specifically point out that it added a new cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision of the trial court, which had granted the insurer's motion to dismiss the insurer's answer and motion to dismiss the insurer's challenge to jurisdiction.

 

1922 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Trice v. Wilson


No. 41798


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 715; 149 S.E.2d 530; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 1185


February 9, 1966, Argued  
May 6, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 25, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge McGehee.

Mrs. Katherine Jones Wilson brought suit against Edward Trice, administrator of the estate of Jessie L. Long, to recover damages in the amount of $ 50,000 for the wrongful death of her husband, Morris M. Jones. Briefly stated, the plaintiff's petition alleged that her husband received fatal injuries in a collision which occurred on January 8, 1964, in Upson County, when the defendant's intestate negligently drove his truck across the center line of State Highway 74 and into the path of her husband's oncoming vehicle.

To this action the defendant filed a plea in bar in which it was alleged that the plaintiff had received the sum of $ 14,956.50 from the State of Georgia as compensation for the same damages which she was seeking to recover in the present action; and it was asserted that the acceptance of such compensation extinguished the plaintiff's cause of action, released the defendant from liability thereon and constituted a bar to the prosecution of this suit. Attached as an exhibit to the plea was a copy of Resolution Act No. 241 of the General Assembly,  [***2] approved by the Governor on March 26, 1964, which provided in part as follows: "Whereas, on January 8, 1964, at about 4:15 p.m., Morris M. Jones, a resident of Upson County, Georgia, was operating a certain 1954 Ford pick-up truck owned by him on State Route No. 74 traveling in a westward direction and was at a point about five (5) miles west of thomaston, Georgia, when he met a truck belonging to the State Highway Department and operated by an employee of said State Highway Department; and

"Whereas, the driver of the State-owned vehicle negligently turned said vehicle to the left and onto the left-hand side of said highway while driving in an eastwardly direction directly into the path of the vehicle driven by Morris M. Jones; and

"Whereas, William R. Oxford was a passenger in the vehicle operated by Morris M. Jones, the said William R. Oxford was fatally injured in said collision; and

"Whereas, Mrs. Katherine Landers Jones incurred $ 275.00 doctor bill, $ 266.20 hospital bill, $ 25.00 ambulance fee and $ 1,035.30 funeral expenses; and

"Whereas, the vehicle owned and operated by Morris M. Jones was damaged beyond repair and was rendered worthless and the fair market value of said [***3] vehicle immediately prior to said collision was $ 855.00; and

"Whereas, Morris M. Jones was 35 years of age at the time of his death and was employed by Thomaston Cotton Mills, Thomaston, Georgia, with an average weekly earning in excess of $ 60.00 per week; and

"Whereas, the Carlisle Mortality Table shows a life expectancy for a person 35 years of age to be 31.00 years; and

"Whereas, based on said Mortality Table the full value of said life would be $ 96,720.00 and reducing said sum to its present cash value, the cash value of said life would be $ 39,227.00; and

"Whereas, the said Morris M. Jones was critically injured and died from said injuries sustained in said collision on the 13th day of January, 1964, which collision occurred through no fault of the said Morris M. Jones, and it is only fit and proper that his widow be compensated for his death and expenses relative thereto.

"Now, therefore, be it resolved by the General Assembly of Georgia that the State Highway Department be and is hereby authorized and directed to pay to Mrs. Katherine Landers Jones, widow of Morris M. Jones, deceased, the sum of $ 12,500.00 for the cash value of the life of Morris M. Jones, plus the [***4] amount of $ 855.00 for damage to said truck, plus the amount of $ 566.20 for hospital, doctor and ambulance expenses and fees, plus the amount of $ 1,035.30 for funeral expenses. Said payment shall be in full and final satisfaction for any claim against the State arising as a result of the collision described and set forth in this Resolution. The payment of said sums shall be from the funds appropriated to or available to the State Highway Department."

Evidence adduced on the hearing of the defendant's plea disclosed that the plaintiff had authorized her attorney to seek compensation from the State of Georgia for the death of her husband and other damages arising out of the collision between his vehicle and that of the State Highway Department; that the damages for which she received compensation from the State as enumerated in Resolution Act No. 241 arose out of the same act upon which her right of recovery against the defendant in the present action was based; and that she had received and cashed a check from the State Highway Department in the amount of $ 14,956.50.

The trial court who by agreement of the parties heard the plea in bar without the intervention of a jury entered [***5] an order overruling the plea and the appeal is from that judgment as one which would have been final if entered as contended for by the appellant.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tortfeasor challenged an order of the Upson Superior Court (Georgia), which denied its plea in bar, which sought dismissal of plaintiff wife's wrongful death action, on the basis that the wife's acceptance of a settlement from the tortfeasor's employer acted a release to the tortfeasor.


OVERVIEW: The tortfeasor's employer was the state. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the state's payment of compensation to the wife did not bar the wife's action against the tortfeasor. In so ruling, the court noted that, generally, the release of one of several joint tort-feasors extinguished a plaintiff's cause of action and relieved all jointly liable thereon. However, the tortfeasor's employer, the state, had no legal liability to the wife, as it was immune. As such, it did not share joint liability with the tortfeasor. Unlike other states, the state had not established any statutory guidelines to insure that parties in the position of the wife received fair and adequate compensation for their injuries, and as such, the award was purely discretionary. However, because the law prohibited the double recovery of damages, the tortfeasor was permitted to plead the settlement in reduction or avoidance of the wife's right of recovery but not as an absolute bar to her right of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which held that the wife's acceptance of a settlement from the tortfeasor's employer was not a bar to the wife's wrongful death action against the tortfeasor.

 

1923 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ga. Power Co. v. Fletcher


No. 41919


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 559; 148 S.E.2d 915; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 1135


April 4, 1966, Submitted  
April 29, 1966, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Breach of lease contract. Troup Superior Court. Before Judge Knight.

W. J. Fletcher leased from Georgia Power Company 164 acres in Troup County for a term of four years beginning January 1, 1963, and ending December 31, 1966, for a rental of $ 400 payable $ 100 each September 1, beginning September 1, 1963. A portion of the land was woodland and the rest of it tillable farm land. The lease provided, inter alia, that the land was to be used "for farming only and in such manner as will not violate any local, State or National laws," and that upon failure of the tenant to pay rent promptly when due or "to do and perform any of the other obligations and covenants hereof, the owner has the right, after giving 30 days notice of its intention to do so, to cancel this lease and take possession of said property."

Lessor learned that the lessee had discontinued planting corn, cotton, and the like on some 24 acres of the land and placed it, along with adjoining lands owned by the lessee, in what is commonly known as the Cropland Adjustment Program of the Agricultural Stabilization and Conservation Service of the U. S. Department of Agriculture, which, while permitting the planting of [***2] legumes or pasturage grasses on the land, prohibits any harvesting thereof or grazing between May 1 and November 1 of the year involved. Taking the position that the lessee had violated his obligation under the lease to "farm" the land, lessor notified him that the lease was being canceled, and demanded possession. There is no contention that the rentals were not paid or tendered promptly when due. Lessee declined to surrender possession, and a dispossessory warrant was sued out. The issue was tried before a jury, which returned a verdict for the defendant, and plaintifflessor a jury, which returned a verdict for the defendant, and plaintifflessor appeals, with enumerations of error amounting to the general grounds of a motion for new trial.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lessor sought review of a decision from the Superior Court, Troup County (Georgia), which entered a judgment for appellee lessee in a an action by the lessor to cancel a rural land ease and obtain possession of the leased land.


OVERVIEW: The lessor rented mixed open and wooded land to the lessee. The lease provided that the land had to be used for farming purposes. When the lessee placed 24 acres into a conservation program sponsored by the federal government, the lessor declared that the conditions of the lease had been broken and demanded possession. The trial court entered a judgment for the lessee. On appeal, the court affirmed because the expression "farming purposes" was not limited to the cultivation of the soil and growing of crops; it included stock raising and maintaining pasturage. Furthermore, the character of the use caused by the diversion into the conservation program was not changed because that fell within the meaning of the farming purpose clause of the lease. Finally, the conservation program was not a prohibited sublease because the federal government acquired no interest in the land that was put into the program.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the lessee.

 

1924 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Sanders Truck Transp. Co. v. Beverly


No. 41668


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 271; 147 S.E.2d 855; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 1035


January 3, 1966, Argued  
February 18, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1966. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Killebrew.

This is an appeal from the order of the Superior Court of Richmond County denying the motion of the defendant Sanders Truck Transportation Co., Inc. to strike and dismiss the plaintiff's petition, and from certain other rulings of the trial court respecting the defensive pleadings of the transportation company. The allegations of the petition show substantially the following facts: The defendant Sammons was driving a truck of the defendant transportation company which was towing another truck and trailer also owned by the defendant transportation company and driven by the other defendant Jeffers. The drivers had stopped the vehicles on the Sand Bar Ferry bridge in Richmond County at a point about 450 feet west of the Georgia-South Carolina Line, at about 9:30 p.m. They failed to provide any lights on their vehicles visible to one approaching from the rear thereof and violated other statutory provisions, which acts were charged against the defendants as negligence and which were alleged to have proximately caused the plaintiff's automobile to collide [***2] with the rear vehicle resulting in the injuries to the plaintiff for which she sued. The errors enumerated by the appellant, and such other facts as may be necessary to an understanding of the issues presented by this appeal will be set forth in the opinion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant transportation corporation appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Richmond County (Georgia), which denied the corporation's motion to strike and dismiss plaintiff motorist's personal injury action brought against the corporation and defendant drivers.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was injured after her vehicle collided with the transportation corporation's truck which was towing another truck and trailer. At the time of the collision, both trucks were stopped on the road without lights visible to vehicles approaching from the rear. On appeal, the corporation argued that the trial court erred in allowing the petition to be amended because the petition did not contain enough to amend by, and because the amendment added a new and distinct cause of action. The court affirmed, concluding that (1) the petition was not so devoid of substance as to be incapable of amendment; (2) the amendment did not change the parties in any way; (3) the corporation's officers knew, or should have been able to ascertain, which of its drivers was driving which truck, and while it was entitled to have this information correctly alleged, the confusion engendered by the original petition was not such as to materially hinder its defense; and (4) service of the petition on the clerk rather than an officer was not so defective as to be void but was merely irregular and was subject to amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision which denied the corporation's motion to strike and dismiss the motorist's personal injury action.

 

1925 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Redd v. Brisbon


No. 41595


Court of Appeals of Georgia


113 Ga. App. 23; 147 S.E.2d 15; 1966 Ga. App. LEXIS 949


October 6, 1965, Submitted  
January 5, 1966, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 21, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Richmond City Court. Before Judge Chambers.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorist appealed a decision of the Richmond City Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant service station owner on the motorist's action against the station owner and defendant customers.


OVERVIEW: One of the customers went into the service station to have his car washed. When the owner said he didn't have time, he asked a second customer to drop the first customer off and bring his car back. On the return trip, the second customer collided with the motorist. On appeal from summary judgment in favor of the station owner, the court affirmed, holding that the relationship of master and servant did not exist between the station owner and the second customer. The mere fact that the second customer was driving the automobile with the direction of or with the knowledge and consent of the station owner was not, standing alone, sufficient to impose liability upon the station owner for the second customer's negligence. No general employment by the station owner of the second customer existed; no payment of compensation for the services to be performed was contemplated. Conceding that the second customer accompanied the first customer at the direction of the station owner for the purpose of returning the automobile to the service station, he was, in doing so, nothing more than a mere volunteer.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant station owner on the motorist's action was affirmed.

 

1926 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. J. D. Jewell, Inc.


No. 41100


Court of Appeals of Georgia


111 Ga. App. 242; 141 S.E.2d 326; 1965 Ga. App. LEXIS 934



February 25, 1965, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for inspection taxes. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commissioner of Agriculture of the State of Georgia challenged a judgment from the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained a demurrer by defendant poultry farmer, a corporation, and dismissed an action to collect inspection taxes on feed used by the poultry farmer to grow its own poultry.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner of Agriculture filed suit against poultry farmer to recover inspection taxes allegedly due on poultry feed. The poultry farmer raised poultry under lease agreements with lessors under which the poultry farmer supplied the lessors with everything that they needed to raise baby chicks to the broiler stage, including the baby chicks. The lessors were paid a portion of the proceeds of the sale of the broilers. The trial court expressly declined to invalidate the 1956 amendment to O.C.G.A. § 42-205 on constitutional grounds, but it sustained the demurrer and dismissed the action on the ground that the provisions imposing the tax on feed furnished, supplied, or used for the growing of the poultry farmer's own poultry under contracts, leases, or agreements were too vague, indefinite, and uncertain to be enforced. The trial court found that the language of the proviso insofar as it refers to any ''person, firm, or corporation'' granted an exemption was void for uncertainty. The court disagreed and reversed the judgment because the language was inclusive enough to impose a tax on poultry feed mixed by the poultry farmer and fed to his or its own poultry.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.
