Sparks Specialty Co. v. Moss


No. 40979


Court of Appeals of Georgia


110 Ga. App. 585; 139 S.E.2d 345; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 707



November 3, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Dismissal of interrogatories. Lamar Superior Court. Before Judge Brown.

Sparks Specialty Company, after having obtained a common law judgment against B. J. Moss and caused execution to be issued thereon, addressed interrogatories to the defendant seeking information through which it could collect the amount of the judgment and execution. The interrogatories signed by the plaintiff's attorney, were prefaced by the following statement: "Pursuant to the provisions of Sections 38-2108 and 38-1201 of the Code of Georgia Annotated, I herewith submit to you for answer under oath and the service of a copy thereof on me within 15 days after the service hereof, the following interrogatories, to wit:" The court on motion of the defendant dismissed the interrogatories on the ground that they were purportedly propounded on the basis of Code sections which had not been officially codified by the General Assembly. The plaintiff excepts to that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.

 

1928 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Atlanta


No. 40766


Court of Appeals of Georgia


110 Ga. App. 114; 137 S.E.2d 668; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 558



June 30, 1964, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 22, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning, etc.; constitutionality of ordinance. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.

Rogers, Pipkin and Scouffas, as Trustees for the Peachtree Congregation of Jehovah's Witnesses, sought a "special use permit" to construct a church on West Wieuca Road in Atlanta. 1 The trustees made an elaborate presentation at a public hearing in August, 1962, before the Planning and Zoning Committee of Atlanta's Board of Aldermen. The committee denied the application without making any findings of fact. In September, 1962, the Board of Aldermen of the City of Atlanta adopted the adverse report of the Planning and Zoning Committee, again without any findings of fact. The trustees then filed their petition for certiorari, which was sanctioned by the superior court judge in October, 1962. The city filed its answer to the certiorari petition in February, 1963, after the trustees moved for a contempt citation for failure to answer. After amendments by petitioners, the superior court overruled the application for certiorari in December, 1963.


1 In 1948 this Congregation purchased two lots on Juniper Street, N. E. and applied for a special use permit, which was denied; in 1950 they were denied a permit for property on Gordon Street, S. W.; in 1959 they were granted a permit on Moore's Mill Road, N. W., but after construction was started the permit was revoked. The lot here involved was purchased in May, 1960, and the permit application was filed in June, 1961.

 [***2] The case was originally appealed to the Supreme Court, but was transferred to us because the Court of Appeals "has jurisdiction in cases involving the constitutionality of municipal ordinances." Rogers v. Mayor &c. of Atlanta, 219 Ga. 799 (136 SE2d 342).



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustees challenged the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled an application for certiorari to challenge the denial, by respondent city, of a special use permit that the trustees sought on behalf of a church.


OVERVIEW: The trustees argued that a city zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The court found that a city zoning ordinance provided reasonable standards and was constitutional for any of the reasons urged. The court also found that the application for the permit was approved as to form by the planning commission, that it otherwise complied with the requirements of buildings in the district, and the parking space provisions. The remaining objective standard under the denial could have been based on the desire to not create a traffic hazard or congestion. The evidence, without dispute, showed that the location of the church would increase the daily traffic flow by a very small percentage no more than three time a week. Because the application met all of the objective criteria pertaining to special use permits, there was no evidentiary support for the denial. The applicants having met all of the objective standards of the zoning ordinance pertaining to special use permits, the court reversed, directing the superior court to sustain their application for certiorari and make a final decision in their behalf.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the trustees a writ of certiorari to review the denial of a zoning application was reversed with a direction that the application should be granted.

 

1929 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dukes v. State


No. 40581


Court of Appeals of Georgia


109 Ga. App. 825; 137 S.E.2d 532; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 1010



June 15, 1964, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Voluntary manslaughter. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Bell.

Loree Dukes was indicted for murder and convicted of manslaughter in the Superior Court of Bibb County. The defendant pled not guilty, but did not deny the shooting, and in her statement to the jury contended that she did not remember what happened. The facts showed in brief that the defendant agreed to meet her divorced husband after working hours in a parking lot, her purpose in doing so being to obtain funds with which he was in arrears in payment of support money for their three children, and his purpose according to her, being that he wished to renew cohabitation with her. Following an argument the defendant shot the deceased with a pistol which she normally carried in the glove compartment of her automobile, inflicting a wound from which he died some days later. After conviction her motion for a new trial was overruled, and she brings error.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled her motion for new trial and convicted her of voluntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: After an argument, defendant shot the deceased, her ex-husband. Defendant claimed that her statements, obtained at a time that she did not have counsel, should have been suppressed because she was illegally detained at the time it was made. Specifically, she claimed that she was booked on some inconsequential misdemeanor or ordinance violation merely as a colorable device in connection with investigative procedure. However, defendant's statements were not made after prolonged detention but were made coincident with her arrest. As such, the statements were admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1930 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Law v. State


No. 40634


Court of Appeals of Georgia


109 Ga. App. 733; 137 S.E.2d 364; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 971



May 6, 1964, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Larceny of automobile. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson.

The defendant and five others were indicted for larceny of an automobile in count 1 of a two-count indictment, and for receiving stolen goods, stolen by persons unknown, in count 2. On the trial the defendant was acquitted of the larceny charge but was convicted on the count which charged him and the others with receiving stolen goods. Prior to the trial the defendant demurred to the second count of the indictment because the indictment shows on its face that the principal thief is known, having been indicted in the first count of the indictment. The trial court overruled such demurrer and sustained a motion to quash a subpoena duces tecum wherein the defendant sought to obtain a copy of testimony or notes pertaining to testimony adduced before the grand jury in such case. After the verdict the defendant's amended motion for new trial was overruled and the defendant assigned error on the above judgments adverse to him in a writ of error to the Supreme Court. The writ of error was transferred to this court by the Supreme Court, Law v. State, 219 Ga. 583 (134 SE2d 776), [***2] when it was determined that no question as to the constitutionality of a statute was raised in the trial court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled defendant's demurrer to an indictment that charged him with receiving stolen goods, which sustained the prosecution's motion to quash a subpoena duces tecum, and which convicted defendant of receiving stolen goods.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with receiving stolen goods. The trial court overruled defendant's demurrer to the indictment, sustained the prosecution's motion to quash a subpoena duces tecum whereby defendant sought to obtain a copy of testimony or notes pertaining to testimony adduced before the grand jury, and convicted defendant of receiving stolen property. The court held that: (1) the demurrer attacking the indictment was without merit; (2) the trial court's order quashing the subpoena duces tecum was not error; (3) the trial court's charge to the jury that knowledge of the alleged theft of the property in question had to be proven beyond a reasonable doubt but that knowledge could be inferred from surrounding facts and circumstances was not erroneous; (4) a complaint about the overruling by the trial court of an objection to a question asked could not be considered because the complaint did not set forth the answer given to the question; and (5) the evidence authorized the verdict that convicted defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1931 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hilderbrand v. Housing Authority of Atlanta


Nos. 40551, 40552


Court of Appeals of Georgia


109 Ga. App. 297; 136 S.E.2d 24; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 858



February 28, 1964, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 11, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation of land. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Whitman.

The Housing Authority of the City of Atlanta filed two separate proceedings in rem under the provisions of Ch. 36-11 of the Code of 1933, as amended by an Act approved January 13, 1938 (Ga. L. 1937-38, Ex. Sess., p. 251), to acquire by condemnation fee simple title to two certain described tracts of land in the City of Atlanta, Fulton County, Georgia, for use in carrying out an urban redevelopment project. Assessors were duly appointed in both proceedings, took the oath required by them, and thereafter made and filed awards for the land described in the petitions. Orders of condemnation were rendered by the superior court and the awards were paid into the registry of the court. Thereafter the condemnor, defendant in error in both cases, filed its appeal from the assessors' awards with the Clerk of the Superior Court of Fulton County. Plaintiffs in error in both cases filed motions to dismiss the condemnor's appeals on the ground that the condemnor had failed to pay the assessors' fees and costs prior to or at the time of filing its appeals, nor at the time of the filing [***2] of plaintiffs in errors' motions to dismiss (which was 24 days after the filing of the condemnor's appeal in one case and 98 days in the other), and on the further ground that such failure to so pay assessors' fees and costs constituted an unreasonable and flagrant departure from the appeal procedure set out in Code Ann. § 36-605. The motions to dismiss came on for hearing under written stipulations of facts and, after it was orally stipulated that the assessors' fees had been paid at some undesignated time since the filing of the motions to dismiss and after argument was heard thereon, the court overruled said motions. To the judgments of the court overruling the motions to dismiss the condemnees except.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in error condemnees sought review of judgments of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) overruling their motions to dismiss the appeal of defendant in error, the Housing Authority of the City of Atlanta, of the assessors' award in a condemnation proceeding because the Authority had not paid the assessors' fees and costs, which allegedly was an unreasonable and flagrant departure from the appeal procedure set out in O.C.G.A. § 36-605.


OVERVIEW: Under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-1110, a condemnor's right of appeal from the assessors' awards was subject to the same terms and conditions as were provided in O.C.G.A. ch. 36-6, and O.C.G.A. § 36-605 required the condemnor to pay the assessors' fees and authorized the court to award such other costs as provided by law in civil cases in the superior court. However, the court held that the Authority's failure to pay the assessors' fees and costs within 10 days of the filing of its appeals did not vitiate the appeals because: (1) if the Authority was a political subdivision of the State, it was exempt from payment of such fees and costs by O.C.G.A. § 36-605; (2) even if the Authority was not a political subdivision of the State, neither O.C.G.A. § 36-605 nor any other section of O.C.G.A. chs. 36-6 or 36-11 made the payment of these costs and fees a condition precedent to the filing of appeals from the assessors' awards; and (3) if the Clerk received an appeal without exacting the costs, the appeal was good and the Clerk was estopped as to all persons except the appellant from saying that the costs had not been paid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

 

1932 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Employees Ret. Sys. v. Lewis


No. 40531


Court of Appeals of Georgia


109 Ga. App. 476; 136 S.E.2d 518; 1964 Ga. App. LEXIS 894



February 27, 1964, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 19 and April 2, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment, etc. Laurens Superior Court. Before Judge Ward.

This declaratory judgment action was brought by the State Employees Retirement System against Laurens County, and seeks to adjudicate the county's liability for Social Security payments on behalf of the deputies and others employed in the sheriff's office of that county for the three-year period of September, 1957 to January, 1960.

The allegations of the petition essentially are: In 1956 the Retirement System and the county amended their previous contract to bring sheriff's deputies and employees under Social Security, and the county began making payments on these individuals, continuing until September, 1957, when the Supreme Court of Georgia determined that the 1952 Act placing the sheriff on a salary rather than a fee basis of compensation and making the sheriff's employees employees of the county was unconstitutional and void because it had been improperly advertised. Gay v. Laurens County, 213 Ga. 518 (100 SE2d 271). From the time of this decision until the end of 1960 the county did not report and pay Social Security for these persons. 1


1 The Act of 1952 placing the sheriff on a salary was substantially re-enacted in 1960, Ga. L. 1960, p. 2072, and the county resumed payments after the effective date of the new Act.

 [***2] The Retirement System seeks a declaration that it is entitled to recover the Social Security payments for this period. The System's contract with Federal Social Security Administration requires it to make payments for all employees covered whether or not the System has collected for them on penalty of deduction from any Social Security money due the State. It is alleged that the System will be put in a position of having to pay Federal Social Security Administration for the deputies and other employees before their status as to Social Security coverage is determined.

The trial court, after overruling general and special demurrers, held that the persons involved were not employees of the county during the period in dispute. To this adverse ruling the System excepts.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retirement system challenged a judgment of the Laurens County Superior Court (Georgia), which held that various employees of the sheriff's office were not employees of the county during the three-year period for which the system sought contributions from defendant county for social security payments the system was required to make on behalf of the employees.


OVERVIEW: The system filed an action seeking contributions from the county for contributions the system was required to make to Social Security on behalf of employees for whom the county had been making contributions but had discontinued payments after a law making sheriff's employees employees of the county was declared unconstitutional and void. The court affirmed the determination that the county was not liable for the Social Security contributions. Because the contract was invalid during the period in which the system sought contribution, the fact that the contract may have been entered into in good faith and payments may have been made thereunder could not have had the effect of estopping the county, requiring it to make further payments under the contract. Moreover, during the period involved the county paid no wages to the employees. They were paid by the sheriff. The employees did not work for the county; rather they worked for the sheriff. Absent any payment of wages to them by the county there was neither any obligation on its part to make any deductions or payments, nor any intention on the parties to the contract that it be done.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the system contributions.

 

1933 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Morman v. Pritchard


No. 40053


Court of Appeals of Georgia


108 Ga. App. 247; 132 S.E.2d 561; 1963 Ga. App. LEXIS 596



July 11, 1963, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 30, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari; Judgment of County Board of Education. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Anderson.

The plaintiff in error, following her discharge as a teacher in the Richmond County School System, brought certiorari directly to the Superior Court of Richmond County without first appealing the judgment of the local Board of Education of Richmond County to the State Board of Education. The record of the hearing before the county board was duly transmitted to the superior court with the petition in certiorari. The petition for the writ was sanctioned by the superior court on September 21, 1962.

The respondent filed a motion to dismiss the petition for certiorari in November 1962, and on December 21, 1962, the trial judge, the Hon. G. C. Anderson, after hearing on the motion, entered an order sustaining the motion to dismiss the petition for certiorari "on each and every ground thereof" and dismissed the petition.

The grounds of the motion to dismiss sustained by the trial judge and upon which the dismissal of the petition is based are as follows:

"1. That the above stated petition for certiorari is void and should be dismissed as the said [***2] petition does not set forth any sufficient, legal, or proper assignment of error upon the judgment of the County Board of Education of Richmond County, in discharging the petitioner as a teacher.

"2. That the above stated petition for certiorari is void and should be dismissed as the said petition does not plainly and distinctly set forth the errors complained of and contains no sufficient, proper, or legal assignment of error.

"3. That the assignments of error in the petition for certiorari set forth as (a), (b), (c), (d), (e), and (f) do not plainly and distinctly set forth the errors complained of and are not sufficient, proper, or legal assignments of error and should not be considered by this Honorable Court.

"4. That the said petition for certiorari should be dismissed as it is directed to F. J. Pritchard, Chairman of the Board of Education of Richmond County, when no such office exists as F. J. Pritchard, Chairman of the Board of Education of Richmond County; and under the laws of Georgia, it should have been directed to the County Board of Education of Richmond County, as the law provides that the County Board of Education of Richmond County constitutes the tribunal for [***3] hearing and determining any matters of local controversy in reference to the construction or administration of school law, and the president of said board is not the tribunal.

"5. That the said petition for certiorari should be dismissed as it purports to appeal from a decision of the Board of Education of Richmond County, when the same should have been an appeal from the County Board of Education of Richmond County, and the laws of Georgia specifically provide that when the County Board of Education of Richmond County has made a decision, it shall be binding on the parties and that an appeal from any decision of the County Board of Education of Richmond County is to the State Board of Education; therefore, the writ of certiorari does not and cannot lie directly to the Superior Court of Richmond County from said decision of the County Board of Education of Richmond County.

"6. That the said petition for certiorari should be dismissed as certiorari cannot lie from the judgment of the County Board of Education of Richmond County in discharging the petitioner as a teacher, as under the law the same is not an exercise of judicial power or authority but is an exercise of administrative [***4] authority only."

Error is assigned on the order and judgment of the trial judge in sustaining the motion to dismiss the petition in certiorari and in dismissing it.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher sought review of an order and judgment from the Richmond Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained respondent chairman of the county board of education to dismiss the teacher's petition for a writ of certiorari. Following her discharge from employment in the county school system, the teacher had brought certiorari directly to the trial court.


OVERVIEW: After she was discharged from her position with the county school system, the teacher brought certiorari directly to the trial court without first appealing the judgment of the county board of education to the state board of education. The trial court sustained the chairman's motion to dismiss the teacher's petition in certiorari. On appeal, the chairman contended that the petition should have been dismissed because it was directed to the chairman and not to the tribunal itself, which was the county board of education. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) ordinarily neither the faulty prayer seeking issuance of the writ directed to the wrong party nor the subsequent erroneous direction of the writ would necessarily be fatally defective before final judgment; (2) the petition could have been amended to correct the defect before final judgment; and (3) the record did not show that a request was made by the teacher for additional time within which to amend nor did it show that an amendment was offered prior to the time of the trial judge's final order of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained the chairman's motion to dismiss the petition.

 

1934 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Baggett Transp. Co. v. Barnes


No. 40183


Court of Appeals of Georgia


108 Ga. App. 68; 132 S.E.2d 229; 1963 Ga. App. LEXIS 546



June 4, 1963, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's compensation -- direct appeal to appellate court.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 1963 Ga. Laws 156, appellant employer and appellee claimant each sought review of the order of the Georgia State Board of Workmen's Compensation that affirmed a deputy director's award of compensation to the claimant.


OVERVIEW: The direct appeal from the board was brought under the Act of 1963 that purported to repeal the former O.C.G.A. § 114-710, which required that appeals from the board be taken first to the superior court, with writ of error from the superior court to the court of appeals. Although neither party raised the issue of jurisdiction, the court sua sponte examined the issue and determined that a direct appeal from the board under 1963 Ga. Laws 156 violated Ga. Const. art. VI, § 2, para. 8, which limited its jurisdiction to the correction of errors of law from superior courts, certain city courts, and "such other like courts." The board was not a "like court," but an administrative body, and, under the constitution, the court of appeals had no power to entertain a direct appeal from the board. Thus, that provision of 1963 Ga. Laws 156 was unconstitutionally void and O.C.G.A. § 114-710 remained in full force and effect.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1935 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Shoffeitt v. State


No. 39718


Court of Appeals of Georgia


107 Ga. App. 217; 129 S.E.2d 572; 1963 Ga. App. LEXIS 784



January 16, 1963, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Abandonment. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley.

J. H. Shoffeitt was convicted of abandonment. His motion for new trial consisting of the usual general grounds and two special grounds was overruled. He excepted.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Superior Court of Hall County (Georgia) for the offense of abandonment. He contended that his motion for a new trial should have been sustained because the trial court erred when it permitted counsel for the State to cross-examine him, without his consent, after he made an unsworn statement to the court and jury in his own defense pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 38-415.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that prior to a decision by the United States Supreme Court, it was within the trial court's discretion whether to allow counsel for a criminal defendant to ask the accused questions or make suggestions to him relating to his unsworn statement while he was making such statement in his defense or after he had concluded that. However, the Supreme Court's decision held that as a matter of right, the accused was entitled to be questioned by his counsel to elicit his unsworn statement. The trial court erred when it stated that if defendant was permitted to be questioned by his counsel, the State had a right to cross-examine him even if he objected. The court relied on the Supreme Court of Georgia's ruling that while the statute provided that a defendant who made a statement could be cross-examined, it was a matter of right to him that he could not be examined unless he desired. His willingness to submit to the examination must be expressed by him, after he had completed his statement. Without his consent, neither the court or counsel could legally propound a question to him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that denied defendant's motion for a new trial.

Holland v. College Park


No. 39248


Court of Appeals of Georgia


105 Ga. App. 427; 124 S.E.2d 693; 1962 Ga. App. LEXIS 944



February 28, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affidavit of illegality, etc. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Banke.

Plaintiff in error filed an alleged affidavit of illegality in the Clayton Superior Court which charged that the defendant had issued a fi. fa. pursuant to an ordinance of the City of College Park which provided for paving and curbing of Lee Street and assessing the property owners whose real estate abutted on either side with the cost. This ordinance assessed one-half of the cost against real estate abutting on the north side of the street and one-half on the south side. The plaintiff in error contended that the ordinance was never legally adopted; that it was never spread upon the minutes of the governing authority, in violation of the city charter, and that it was adopted without proper hearing; that it was being discriminatorily administered; that the street paving assessment was being arbitrarily and discriminatorily assessed against the plaintiff in error the entire length of the side street as plaintiff in error had previously paid a street paving assessment for the front of his property; and that the resolution was unconstitutional and in violation of the Constitution of the United States and [***2] of the State of Georgia.

To the alleged affidavit of illegality the city filed a general demurrer and an answer and traverse to it admitting the issuance of the fi. fa. and denying the other paragraphs. The defendant's general demurrer was overruled, a jury trial was waived, and after hearing, the trial court issued an order dismissing the affidavit of illegality. To this order the plaintiff in error excepted.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error city resident sought review of a decision of the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed his alleged affidavit of illegality that charged that defendant city had issued a writ of execution against his property pursuant to an ordinance that the resident claimed the city had never legally adopted under the authority of City of College Park, Ga., Charter Amendments, 1951 Ga. Laws 2797, § 13, and 1951 Ga. Laws 2804-5.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an ordinance adopted under the City of College Park, Ga., Charter Amendments (Amendments), 1951 Ga. Laws 2797, § 13, and 1951 Ga. Laws 2804-5, the city issued a writ of execution against the resident's property after assessing the property with a portion of the cost of paving an abutting city street. The resident filed an alleged affidavit of illegality, claiming that the city had never legally adopted the ordinance. The trial court dismissed his affidavit, and the resident sought review of the trial court's decision, claiming that the execution was void because the assessment on his property was excessive. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the city was authorized under the Amendments to execute upon the property and that because could do so the amount of its assessment was not relevant. The court also ruled that the assessment was not arbitrary because the city assessed all property at the same rate and that the city could assess against the resident's property for each street it abutted. The court found further that the resident's claim that the city had not legally adopted the ordinance was contradicted by the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that had dismissed the resident's alleged affidavit of illegality.

No. 39273


Court of Appeals of Georgia


105 Ga. App. 408; 124 S.E.2d 655; 1962 Ga. App. LEXIS 1077

Williams v. State


No. 39243


Court of Appeals of Georgia


105 Ga. App. 226; 124 S.E.2d 448; 1962 Ga. App. LEXIS 891



January 23, 1962, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Possessing indecent and obscene photographs. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for possessing indecent and obscene photographs by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant sought review of her indictment. Defendant filed special and general demurrers to the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to have the act under which she was indicted declared unconstitutional. Defendant contended that the indictment failed to allege that she knowingly possessed the obscene photographs. On appeal, the court determined that the Georgia Supreme Court had disposed of defendant's constitutional arguments. The court stated that the language in the indictment was sufficient to allege possession of the obscene photographs and not mere custody of the obscene photographs. The court held that the indictment was not subject to defendant's general demurrer because it described photographs in the defendant's possession and under her control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1940 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. De Jarnette


Nos. 39089, 39090


Court of Appeals of Georgia


104 Ga. App. 664; 123 S.E.2d 16; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 766



September 29, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 18, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Whitman.

These are companion cases representing the actions of Mrs. Alma D. Cox for her own injuries and Mr. T. C. Cox, her husband, bringing his action for loss of his wife's services and for expenses incurred as a result of her injuries. Throughout the opinion the references are to the pleadings and demurrers in Case No. 39090, T. C. Cox v. N. M. DeJarnette et al., Trustees, and the rulings apply equally to the corresponding demurrers in Case No. 39089. Counsel has stated that the questions are identical in the two cases, and the court so treats them.

Plaintiff T. C. Cox brought this action to recover for the loss of his wife's services and expenses in connection with her injuries against N. M. DeJarnette, et al., as Trustees of the Inman Park Methodist Church. The petition charged that the named trustees held the legal title to the church and educational building of the Inman Park Methodist Church and the real estate upon which they were located; that these buildings and real estate were held by the defendant trustees for the church and the charitable purposes of the Methodist [***2] Church; that the educational building was constructed for the church during 1954, 1955, and 1956, and was accepted by the defendant trustees of the church from the building contractor on September 17, 1956; that from that date, and particularly on July 15, 1957, the date of the injury to petitioner's wife, the possession of the educational building, its steps and approaches, for the purpose of exercising supervision, oversight and care of the building, was in the defendant trustees as trustees of the church; that the pastor of the church was authorized to extend an invitation to all persons, including members of the church, to use the physical facilities of the church for religious purposes, including use of the prayer room; that petitioner's wife at the time of the injury was a member of the Board of Stewards and of the Committee of Membership and Evangelism of the church, and was secretary of the Christian Missionary Education of the church; that she performed the duties without salary or compensation; that she and the petitioner made regular monthly contributions to the church; that at the entrance of the educational building were front steps and a landing constructed by the defendants [***3] through the contractor; that such steps were constructed without a non-skid tread, but were troweled with a steel trowel so as to have a slippery surface; that, when the steps or landing were wet or damp with rain water, the steps and landing were slippery like glass; that they were a nuisance by which third parties would be injured when walking on them; that they were certain to cause persons to slip and fall, were inherently and intrinsically dangerous to third persons, were so negligently defective as to be imminently dangerous to third persons; that the steps and landing were accepted by the trustees without actual knowledge of the dangerous condition, but if they had exercised ordinary care, they would have discovered the dangerous condition of the steps and landing; that petitioner's wife on the day of the injury entered the educational building at a time when the steps and landing were dry in order to use the prayer room of the church; that a sprinkling of rain fell upon the steps and landing and wet and dampened them while she was in the building; that in leaving the building, not knowing the steps were slippery and unsafe, her feet slipped and slid out from under her causing [***4] her to catapult down the steps, causing serious and permanent injuries.

The petition set forth ordinances of the City of Atlanta, providing as follows: ". . . Exterior stairways shall conform to requirements of interior stairs in Section 604 . . . (c) Treads and landings shall be constructed in a manner to prevent persons from slipping thereon." and, "(1) Conditions Constituting Nuisance. Any building structure, enclosure, place or premises is a nuisance where it is perilous to life or property by reason of its construction . . ."

The petition charged the defendant trustees were negligent in causing the steps and landing to be constructed and maintained in such a manner as to be dangerous to life and limb of third persons when walking on them in damp or wet weather; in causing the steps and landing to be constructed contrary to and in violation of the alleged city ordinances; in failing to roughen the steps and landing so as to make them safe for persons walking on them in damp or wet weather, or applying an abrasive tread for the same purpose; in failing to correct the slippery surface of the steps and landing and thereby eliminate the condition which the petition charges was a [***5] nuisance.

The petition urges that the negligence alleged was administrative negligence of the trustees, chargeable to them in their capacity as trustees, and not chargeable to any subordinate employees of the trustees. The petition set forth the injuries to the petitioner's wife and the medical expense incurred for her, and prayed for these items as damages. The petition alleged that the defendant trustees held the title to the various properties for the benefit of the Inman Park Methodist Church, most of the property being dedicated and devoted to the charitable purposes of the church, but some of the property being held for noncharitable purposes, and "that among the non-charitable assets to which title is held by defendant trustees on July 26, 1957, was and is an owner's public liability policy, issued by Dixie Fire and Casualty Company of the City of Greer, South Carolina, insuring defendant trustees for bodily injury liability to third persons for which the insured trustees shall become legally obligated to pay to third persons, such as your petitioners, arising out of the ownership, maintenance or use of the Church premises, and all operations necessary or incidental thereto."

 [***6] The final paragraph of the petition prayed for judgment against the defendant trustees as trustees to compensate for the full extent of the injuries, ". . . said judgment to be recoverable against all of the assets held in trust by the defendants, whether said assets be used for charitable or noncharitable purposes, to the extent as may be provided by law. Petitioner does not seek to subject any personal or individual assets owned by any of defendant trustees in their personal or individual capacities . . ."

The defendants filed general demurrers to the petition and sixteen special demurrers, which are discussed in the opinion. The trial court sustained the defendants' general demurrers and dismissed the petition. All, or parts of all, of nine of the special demurrers were sustained, and all or parts of five special demurrers were overruled. Paragraph 10 of the special demurrer was overruled on the ground that paragraph 27 (a) by incorporation of paragraph 17 of the plaintiff's petition was partly good and partly bad, and paragraph 10 being to the entire paragraph 27 (a) with paragraph 17 incorporated, was bad in form. Paragraph 15 was overruled on the ground that paragraph [***7] 27 (g) was partly good and partly bad, and paragraph 15 of the demurrers being to the entire paragraph 27 (g) was bad in form. A portion of paragraph 18 of the special demurrers, as amended, was sustained as to the second unnumbered paragraph. No ruling was made upon the first paragraph of special demurrer 18.

To the judgment of the trial court sustaining the general and special demurrers, and to the judgment failing to overrule the first unnumbered paragraph of special demurrer 18, the plaintiff excepted.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, sought review of a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained general and special demurrers of appellee church trustees in a personal injury action, and dismissed the claim of the husband and wife.


OVERVIEW: A husband and wife brought an action in negligence against the trustees of their church after the wife was injured in a fall on the church steps. The husband and wife alleged that the trustees did not exercise ordinary care to discover that the steps became very slippery when wet and that the trustees were negligent in allowing the construction of such steps. The trustees filed general and special demurrers to the action. The lower court sustained the general demurrers, and certain of the special demurrers, and dismissed the action of the husband and wife. On review, the court affirmed the decision of the lower court sustaining certain of the special demurrers. The court found, however, that the lower court erred in sustaining a demurrer which raised the doctrine of charitable immunity as a bar to the cause of action. The court found that the cause of action could be stated to the extent of any liability coverage held by the church. The court also found that the petition of the husband and wife stated a cause of action in negligence and that the lower court erred in sustaining the general demurrers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court sustaining certain of the special demurrers, but it reversed that part of the decision sustaining the general demurrers. The petition of the husband and wife stated a cause of action in negligence and was not subject to general demurrer.

 

1941 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Hansel v. State


No. 38895


Court of Appeals of Georgia


104 Ga. App. 318; 121 S.E.2d 696; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 669



September 6, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 15, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Voluntary manslaughter. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Harrison.

Donald C. Hansel was indicted by a grand jury in Chatham County for the offense of murder. Upon trial in Chatham Superior Court he was convicted of voluntary manslaughter. From an order overruling his amended motion for a new trial, the defendant excepted, bringing the case to this court for review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia), which convicted him of voluntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that after going down a dirt road, defendant and the victim got out of their cars. Defendant stated that when the victim approached him with a knife, he reached into his car, got his gun, loaded it, and told the victim to stop. Defendant then stated that the victim surprised him by lunging at him and that the gun went off. Defendant concluded his statement by stating that he shot the victim to keep the victim from cutting him. The State produced a witness who heard a voice just before the shot was fired say please don't shoot. In addition, a knife was found near the victim's body and testimony was introduced that the victim was shot from a distance of 15 feet or less. The court held that it appeared that defendant and the victim voluntarily entered into a duel with deadly weapons with knowledge that injury or death might result therefrom. As a result, the trial court did not err in refusing to charge the jury on the law of accidental killing. Finally, defendant could not argue that the provisions of O.C.G.A. §38-415, relating to the unsworn statement of defendants in criminal trials, were unconstitutional because he failed to raise the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1942 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wolfe v. Albany


No. 38906


Court of Appeals of Georgia


104 Ga. App. 264; 121 S.E.2d 331; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 656; 49 L.R.R.M. 2140; 43 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,328



July 14, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 28, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for certiorari; violation of city ordinance. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Crow.

The defendant was tried and convicted in the Recorder's Court of the City of Albany for violation of a city ordinance containing the following provisions:

"Section I. Every person who, within the City of Albany, shall solicit memberships in any club, association or union, where there is any charge for membership therein, shall prior to any solicitation for members thereof, apply to and obtain from the City Clerk a certificate and license authorizing such activities upon his or her part.

"Section II. Be it further ordained by the authority aforesaid, that a prerequisite for the obtaining of any such license shall be: (a) a showing that the applicant is of good moral character and that he or she has never been convicted of any offense against the laws of any state or of the United States; (b) That the applicant is not, nor has ever been affiliated with or a member of any organization or group having Communistic beliefs; and (c) a payment of the sum of $ 25.00 as a license fee." Punishment for violation is by fine and/or imprisonment.

The defendant,  [***2] a labor union organizer, filed a plea in abatement challenging the validity of the ordinance on a number of Constitutional and statutory Federal grounds. Evidence was offered in support of the plea which revealed that the defendant was employed for the purpose of meeting with employees of A. & M. Karagheusian, Inc. to discuss the feasibility of becoming organized, to talk with them directly in and around the plant gates and at their homes, and to request them to join the Textile Workers Union, and that he also held meetings for the purpose of talking with and soliciting such employees. The application form required before the issuance of the license contains the following language: "The undersigned submits, in connection with the foregoing application (a) a certificate from --- attesting to the fact that I am a person of good moral character, and I state that I have never been convicted of any offense against the laws of any State, or of the United States; and (b) that I am not now and have never been affiliated with or a member of any organization or group having communist beliefs. The license fee of $ 25 is tendered herewith." It was admitted that the defendant failed to make [***3] such application, tender the license fee, or obtain a permit before soliciting persons to join the labor union. The recorder overruled the plea in abatement and found the defendant guilty of the violation charged. A petition for writ of certiorari to the Superior Court of Dougherty County was dismissed and error is assigned on that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him for violation of a city ordinance against soliciting memberships in a club, association, or union.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a labor union organizer who was employed to meet with employees of a corporation to discuss the feasibility of becoming organized and requesting them to join a union. He was charged with violating a city ordinance that prohibited solicitation of memberships in clubs, associations, or unions where there was a charge for membership without a license. He filed a plea in abatement challenging the validity of the ordinance, but was convicted. He appealed. The court reversed the conviction, holding that Congress had no power to intrude in the field of purely intrastate commerce. The ordinance denied to all citizens of the city the right to request their friends join any dues-paying association unless they first obtained a license for that purpose, and the grant of the license was conditioned upon payment of a fee and the furnishing of statements that the applicant was of good moral character, never violated any law, and never joined any organization having "Communistic" beliefs. The court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional because there was no reasonable relationship between the restraints imposed on freedom of speech and the general welfare of the community.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for violation of a city ordinance that prohibited solicitation of memberships in clubs, associations, or unions where there was a charge for membership without a license.

 

1943 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Carpenter v. Forshee


No. 38792


Court of Appeals of Georgia


103 Ga. App. 758; 120 S.E.2d 786; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 1055



May 31, 1961, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Adoption of child, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Moore.

The defendant in error filed a petition in the Superior Court of Fulton County for the adoption of a child. The petition, to which was attached the written consent of the child's mother, alleged that the petitioner was a resident of Fulton County; that the mother of the child was the petitioner's wife; that the petitioner and his wife did not know the whereabouts of the child's father; that the father for more than twelve months had wantonly and wilfully failed to comply with a decree of the Superior Court of Cobb County, ordering him to make weekly payments for the support of the child, and that therefore his consent was not required. Upon presentation of the petition the court entered an order for interlocutory hearing, setting a date for hearing and directing that "service be perfected upon the party or parties whose written consent to the adoption is required, unless service of said petition and notice has been or will be duly waived in writing." The record does not show any service (personal, by registered mail or by publication) upon the father. On the date set for hearing the court entered a temporary [***2] order, reciting that after the examination of the parties interested, in chambers, under oath, and after giving consideration to the investigation and report made by the State Department of Public Welfare, it appeared that the adoption was for the best interest of the child; ordering that the prayers of petitioner be granted and that temporary custody of the child be awarded petitioner; and that the matter be set down for final hearing after the expiration of six months. Before the final hearing, the plaintiff in error, the natural father of the child, filed the following: (1) a plea to the jurisdiction on the grounds (a) that the courts of Colorado, where the father resided, and not the courts of Georgia had jurisdiction of the subject matter of the adoption, because the child's residence follows that of his father; and (b) that the father had not consented to nor been served or received notice as required by Georgia law; (2) a general demurrer on the grounds that the petition did not show (a) facts constituting abandonment or the father's consent; (b) that the child was a resident of Fulton County; (c) that service was made as provided by law, or; (d) that the father was a resident [***3] of Fulton County or had forfeited his parental rights and thereby that the court had jurisdiction; (3) an answer and objection praying that the adoption be denied and the interlocutory order be revoked, in which he denied and sought to refute the contention that he had wilfully and wantonly failed to comply with the court order for support of the child and that his consent was not necessary, and showed that he never received a conformed copy of the adoption petition and order for interlocutory hearing. The evidence adduced on the plea to the jurisdiction related to the domicile and residence of the natural father, the residence of the natural mother, the child, and the petitioner; support furnished by the natural father, his visits to Georgia and efforts to see the child. In this pleading the father appears to have followed the procedure provided by Code Ann. § 74-415 permitting the court, at any time before entry of a final decree, to revoke its interlocutory order for good cause shown. From the wording of the father's answer and the evidence presented in its support his position appears to be based on his contention that he had not wilfully and wantonly failed to comply with [***4] the support decree; and he contends therefore that his consent to the adoption was required; and that therefore the provisions of the statute for service, either on nonresidents (mailing a conformed copy), or on persons whose residence is unknown (by publication) should have been followed. After hearings on each the court took all of these matters under advisement, and thereafter overruled the father's plea to the jurisdiction and general demurrer. The court entered an "Order on Application for Adoption" reciting that "after hearing evidence the court is of the opinion that . . . the natural father of said minor has wantonly and wilfully failed to comply with the order of the Superior Court of Cobb County, Georgia, . . . to make weekly payments for the support of said child, for a period of more than twelve months, therefore the consent of said party is not necessary in order that the adoption be consummated . . . the objection of . . . the natural father . . . is overruled and denied and it is ordered that adoption proceedings proceed as the law provides." To the three orders, overruling the plea to the jurisdiction and the general demurrer and denying the objections to the adoption,  [***5] the father excepts.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error father challenged an order from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which granted the petition of defendant in error stepfather for adoption of the father's child, overruled the father's plea to the jurisdiction and demurrer, and denied his objections to the adoption in finding that he had wantonly and wilfully failed to comply with a child support order and that his consent to the adoption was unnecessary.


OVERVIEW: The stepfather filed a petition for adoption of the child, and the mother's written consent alleged that the father's whereabouts were unknown and that his consent was not required because, for more than 12 months, he had wantonly and wilfully failed to comply with a support decree. No service was made on the father, and the trial court entered a temporary order granting the petition and held that the adoption was in the child's best interest. The father then filed a plea to the jurisdiction on the grounds of improper venue and lack of consent, and a demurrer. The trial court overruled the plea to the jurisdiction and the general demurrer and denied the objections to the adoption. On appeal, the court held that: (1) under Ga. Code Ann. § 74-401, venue was proper in the county where the stepfather resided; and (2) the consent of both parents prior to the adoption was required, and the exception thereto did not apply because the father had not been adjudicated for wilful and wanton nonsupport; however (3) the failure to effect service on the father was harmless error because he did not seek a continuance or decline to participate in the trial of his objections to the adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had granted the stepfather's petition for adoption, overruled the father's plea to the jurisdiction and general demurrer, denied his objections to the adoption of his child, and found that the father had wantonly and wilfully failed to comply with a support order and that his consent to the adoption was not required.

 

1944 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Revlon, Inc. v. Murdock


No. 38670


Court of Appeals of Georgia


103 Ga. App. 842; 120 S.E.2d 912; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 1073



May 31, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Kennedy.

Mrs. Irene Murdock filed her petition in Richmond County Superior Court against Revlon, Inc., for damages allegedly caused by injuries she received while using the product of the defendant, a manufacturer of cosmetics.

The petition alleged that the plaintiff was employed as a beautician in a beauty salon to give manicures, facials and shampoos to the patrons of the salon; that in said employment she used and applied the defendant's products on the salon's patrons; that her employer purchased from a wholesale distributor and promoter of the defendant's products some bottles of the defendant's nail polish together with a smaller empty table service bottle; that such bottle was manufactured by the defendant for the purpose of having the polish from the larger bottles poured into it for use at the manicure table, which was a necessary and integral step in the use and application of the polish on the salon's patrons; that just after the package containing three bottles of polish and the empty bottle were opened prior to the plaintiff's use of it as hereinafter described, she picked [***2] up the service bottle and, following the written directions furnished by the defendant and included in the purchase, shook the bottle to mix the polish and make it suitable for application; that while thus shaking the bottle in a normal and mild manner, the bottom blew out and the bottle exploded and violently propelled all of the glass in the bottom of the bottle to her left hand, inflicting described injuries and resulting in various damages to the plaintiff; that the plaintiff's injuries would not have occurred if said bottle had not been defective and had had sufficient strength to withstand the mild shaking given by the plaintiff as directed by the defendant.

The petition further alleged that the defendant knew its wholesaler would resell the product to beauty salons and that it would be used by the various beauticians employed therein throughout the United States; that the defendant put the bottle on the market generally to be distributed and then used by the plaintiff and persons similarly situated with the implication and warranty that the use of the bottle was safe.

To this petition the defendant filed a general demurrer, which the trial court overruled. To that judgment [***3] the defendant excepts, bringing the case to this court for review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cosmetics manufacturer filed exceptions to a judgment of the Richmond Superior Court (Georgia), overruling the manufacturer's general demurrer to the petition of plaintiff beautician, which sought damages allegedly caused by injuries the beautician sustained while using the product of the manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The beautician was employed in a beauty salon. In her position, the beautician used the manufacturer's products on the salon's patrons, which her employer purchased from a wholesale distributor of the manufacturer's product. Although she followed the manufacturer's written directions in working with the manufacturer's nail polish, while shaking the polish bottle as directed, the beautician was injured when the bottle exploded. She filed her action against the manufacturer, who filed a general demurrer, which was overruled. The manufacturer appealed the trial court's decision. Upon review, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that in view of the language used in Ga. Code Ann. § 96-307, the court could not conclude that it was the legislature's intent to extend implied warranties to every consumer or user of a product, unless such individual was also a purchaser. The court stated that because the beautician was not a purchaser, or even the ultimate consumer, of the product causing her injury, she could not rely upon the implied warranties mentioned in § 96-307, and, as such, her petition was subject to the general demurrer, which should have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the trial court erred in overruling the general demurrer of the manufacturer to the beautician's petition.

 

1945 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Allied Finance Co. v. Prosser


No. 38698


Court of Appeals of Georgia


103 Ga. App. 538; 119 S.E.2d 813; 1961 Ga. App. LEXIS 994



April 4, 1961, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on foreign judgment; plea of nul tiel record. Bulloch Superior Court. Before Judge Renfroe.

The plaintiff brought action against the defendant in the Superior Court of Bulloch County, Ga., to recover on a judgment it obtained against the defendant in the State of Texas. To the plaintiff's petition the defendant filed his answer, demurrer and special plea of nul tiel record, alleging that the judgment obtained in Texas is void for want of jurisdiction of the defendant by the Texas court. The record discloses that the plaintiff obtained a judgment for the unpaid balance of a note against the defendant, maker of the note, in the State of Texas. The petition in the action brought in the State of Texas against the defendant alleges that he is a resident of Statesboro, Ga. In that action service of process was made upon the defendant pursuant to an act of the legislature of the State of Texas which provides: "Any . . . nonresident natural person that engages in business in this State . . . shall be deemed equivalent to an appointment . . . of the Secretary of State of Texas as agent upon whom service of process may be made in any action,  [***2] suit or proceedings arising out of such business done in this State, wherein such . . . nonresident natural person is a party or is to be made a party . . . For the purpose of this act . . . any nonresident natural person shall be deemed doing business in this State by entering into contract by mail or otherwise with a resident of Texas . . ." Service was made upon the Secretary of State of Texas, and notice to that effect was mailed to and received by the defendant. Thereafter, judgment by default was taken against the defendant. The defendant signed the note and conditional-sale contract on which the action was founded in connection with the trading of an automobile. It does not appear from the plea whether the defendant signed the note in Texas or mailed it to Texas from Georgia. The court entered its order sustaining the defendant's plea of nul tiel record, and it is to this ruling that the plaintiff excepts.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor sought review of a judgment of the Bulloch Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained a plea of nul tiel record by defendant debtor in an action by the creditor to enforce a foreign judgment entered against the debtor in the State of Texas.


OVERVIEW: The debtor was a resident of Georgia. The creditor obtained a default judgment against the debtor in the State of Texas to recover on a note that secured an automobile. Personal jurisdiction over the debtor in the Texas court was based upon Texas' statutory authority to service of process through the Texas Secretary of State upon nonresidents that did business in Texas. The debtor did not conduct any business in Texas. The debtor's only connection with Texas was to mail the note to the creditor in Texas. The creditor then filed an action to enforce the Texas judgment against the debtor. The debtor filed a special plea of nul tiel record on the ground that the Texas court did not have personal jurisdiction to enter the default judgment. The trial court sustained the plea of nul tiel record. The creditor claimed on appeal that the Texas court had jurisdiction over the debtor. The court rejected the creditor's claim. The court found that the debtor's single contact with the State of Texas by mailing the note did not establish that the debtor was doing business in Texas for purposes of establishing personal jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sustained the debtor's plea of nul tiel record on the creditor's claim.
