1947 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Fields v. Albert


No. 38515


Court of Appeals of Georgia


102 Ga. App. 632; 117 S.E.2d 221; 1960 Ga. App. LEXIS 703



October 25, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson. May 31, 1960.

Y. Albert & Son sued Mrs. Eula Fields in the Civil Court of Fulton County upon contract seeking payment of $ 167.20 principal plus $ 16.40 interest and cost, the same constituting an unpaid balance on the purchase of a carpet. The judge, after hearing evidence in the case, rendered judgment for the plaintiff, whereupon the defendant tendered an appeal to the Appellate Division of the Civil Court of Fulton County. Thereafter, the appellant dismissed her own petition and then petitioned for writ of certiorari to the Superior Court of Fulton County, which was sanctioned on March 10, 1960, returnable to the May term. The plaintiff moved for dismissal on the grounds that certiorari would not lie to the superior court from the judgment of the civil court, where the amount of the suit is less than $ 300, unless the judgment is first appealed to the appellate division of said court, and because the plaintiff failed to give notice as provided for in Code § 19-212. It appears from the record that notice of sanction, time and place of hearing was given on April 28th, hearing scheduled for May 24th, petition dismissed [***2] on May 31st, and that the term of court commenced on May 2, 1960.

On motion the court dismissed the writ of certiorari and it is to this ruling that the defendant excepts.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant buyer sought review of a judgment from Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed her writ of certiorari for review of the trial court's judgment in favor of appellee seller. The seller's suit was to recover the unpaid balance on the buyer's purchase of a carpet. The buyer dismissed her first petition for review to another court and then petitioned for writ of certiorari to the superior court.


OVERVIEW: The seller challenged the buyer's writ on ground that, under O.C.G.A. § 19-212, notice for a writ of certiorari must be given within 10 days before the sitting of the court to which the certiorari is returnable. The buyer's counsel argued that sufficient notice was given in a letter written by him to the seller's counsel and informing him that the original judgment was superseded by the petition and writ of certiorari. The court agreed with the seller and held that the buyer's failure to give 10 days written notice of the sanction of writ of certiorari and also the time and place of hearing was fatal because it was not waived or prevented by unavoidable cause. The court noted that the mere putting of counsel on notice that the writ of certiorari has been sanctioned could not suffice as a substitute for the notice required concerning the time and place of hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment dismissing the buyer's writ of certiorari.

 

1948 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Perry v. Md. Casualty Co.


No. 38415


Court of Appeals of Georgia


102 Ga. App. 475; 116 S.E.2d 620; 1960 Ga. App. LEXIS 657



September 29, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Kelley. November 30, 1959.

Mrs. Ivylyn O. Perry sued Marell Farms, Inc., Maryland Casualty Company, and Clarence Dunagan to recover attorney's fees allegedly due the plaintiff for representing the defendant Dunagan in a workmen's compensation case. The petition was in two counts. The defendants, Marell Farms, Inc., and Maryland Casualty Company, filed general and special demurrers to the plaintiff's petition as well as an answer. The case was placed on the trial court's calendar "for disposition," and on the date such case was set the defendants were not present and were not represented by counsel and upon their failure to announce ready for trial the plaintiff's motion to strike their answer was sustained and the case proceeded to trial at such term before a jury, and a verdict was returned for the plaintiff. Thereafter, the defendants Marell Farms, Inc., and Maryland Casualty Company, at the same term but more than 30 days after the verdict and judgment, filed a motion which as amended prayed for a rule nisi to issue, that the judgment and verdict be vacated and set aside, that the judgment be arrested as provided by Code § [***2] 110-702, and that the motion be considered and entertained as an extraordinary motion for new trial under the provisions of Code § 70-303, and a new trial be granted the defendants. Thereafter, the plaintiff's demurrers to the defendants' foregoing motion were overruled and the former verdict and judgment, as well as the judgment striking the defendants' answer were vacated and set aside. The plaintiff assigned error on the judgments adverse to her in a writ of error addressed to this court. This court transferred the writ of error to the Supreme Court inasmuch as the verdict rendered against the defendants was on a count of the plaintiff's petition which had attacked certain statutes as being unconstitutional and which relied on the allegations that such statutes were unconstitutional in order to authorize a recovery. The Supreme Court ( Perry v. Maryland Casualty Co., 216 Ga. 93, 115 S. E. 2d 102), returned the writ of error to this court because it did not appear that any judgment had been rendered by the trial court as to the constitutionality of a State law.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney appealed a judgment from Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which set aside a verdict and granted a new trial to defendants, client and others, in an action to recover legal fees.


OVERVIEW: One count of the petition attacked certain statutes as unconstitutional. General and special demurrers were filed. The case was placed on the trial court's calendar for disposition and was brought to trial in the absence of the client and the other defendants. The attorney's motion to strike the answer was sustained, and the jury rendered a verdict in favor of the attorney. A motion for new trial was filed. The trial court vacated and set aside the verdict and judgment, as well as the striking of the answer. The court held that no brief of the evidence was necessary under O.C.G.A. § 70-301.1 (1947) in the motion for new trial because the question to be considered did not require a brief of the evidence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in construing its local rules to find that the case had not been properly set for trial. The trial court erred, however, in failing to pass upon a demurrer to the allegation of unconstitutionality, which was not an issue that could be resolved by the appellate court. Moreover, the absence of a defendant was not a proper ground to dismiss a valid plea or answer. A new trial was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that vacated and set aside the verdict and judgment in favor of the attorney.

 

1949 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Studstill v. Aetna Casualty & Sur. Co.


No. 38168


Court of Appeals of Georgia


101 Ga. App. 766; 115 S.E.2d 374; 1960 Ga. App. LEXIS 1004



June 6, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Summary judgment, etc. Sumter Superior Court. Before Judge Rees. October 12, 1959.

On February 20, 1959, Aetna Casualty & Surety Company filed suit to recover the balance due on a promissory note, as transferee, in the amount of $ 8,942.27, against J. T. Studstill, d/b/a Americus Provision Company. On February 24, 1959, the defendant filed his answer denying said indebtedness and the plaintiff filed a garnishment, affidavit and bond naming J. T. Studstill, d/b/a Americus Provision Company as defendant and Citizens Bank of Americus as garnishee. The defendant then filed a garnishment dissolution bond in the amount of $ 8,942.27. On April 23, 1959, the plaintiff filed its motion for summary judgment based on its petition, its and the defendant's depositions and affidavits and other documentary evidence. On May 12, 1959, the plaintiff offered an amendment to its petition which was allowed by the court and subsequently filed in the clerk of the superior court's office on May 14, 1959. On June 6, 1959, the defendant offered and filed with the approval of the court, subject to demurrer, an amendment, and on the same date a hearing was had on the plaintiff's motion for summary [***2] judgment and evidence by affidavits and depositions was offered by both parties in support of and in opposition to said motion. On October 8, 1959, after having heard evidence in the form of affidavits and depositions by both plaintiff and defendant, as well as arguments of counsel for all parties, the trial court did enter an order granting summary judgment in favor of the plaintiff in the amount sued for on the note.

To said order and judgment of the trial court defendant excepts, assigns error on same and brings the case here for review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant alleged debtor sought review of an order of the Sumter Superior Court (Georgia), which granted plaintiff transferee's motion for summary judgment in the amount sued for on a promissory note. The transferee had filed an action against the debtor to recover the balance due on the note.


OVERVIEW: The debtor answered the suit, denying his alleged indebtedness. The transferee responded by filing a garnishment, affidavit, and bond. The debtor then filed a garnishment dissolution bond. Thereafter, the transferee filed its motion for summary judgment based on its petition, its and the debtor's depositions and affidavits, and other documentary evidence. The court affirmed the judgment. In his brief, the debtor argued that there were genuine issues of fact between the parties that should have been submitted to a jury. The court held that the debtor's contention was without merit for the reason that if, at the time of the hearing on the motion for summary judgment, he had any valid defenses, it was his duty under the Georgia Summary Judgment Act to present same at that time. The summary judgment granted placed the debtor in no different position from where a verdict by a jury or a directed verdict by the trial court would have placed him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1950 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brantley v. Heller


Nos. 37988, 37998


Court of Appeals of Georgia


101 Ga. App. 16; 112 S.E.2d 685; 1960 Ga. App. LEXIS 772



January 14, 1960, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Libel. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Anderson. August 15, 1959.

Ray D. Brantley sued George H. Heller, John H. Davis and the Insurance Company of North America for libel. The alleged publication was contained in a separation notice, the original of which was delivered to the Employment Security Agency, Georgia Department of Labor. Such publication is the only alleged publication alleged in the petition although it is alleged that the plaintiff has been unable to obtain employment "without obtaining good reference from his last employer, and without revealing to person, firms or corporations, where he seeks employment, the reasons given by his former employer, for his leaving his employment, the false statements shown in exhibit 'A'" attached to the petition. Demurrers, both general and special, were filed to the petition as well as a motion for a summary judgment by the defendants, which motion was supported by an affidavit. The plaintiff's motion to dismiss such motion for summary judgment was denied and a judgment granting such summary judgment was rendered. The plaintiff assigns error on the judgments adverse to him which dealt with the summary judgment. On the [***2] same date that the summary judgment was granted and in a simultaneous judgment the trial court overruled the general and several special demurrers and sustained other grounds of special demurrer and dismissed the petition. This judgment stated that the part thereof which sustained the special demurrers and dismissed the petition was not then effective and would be effective only if the appellate court reversed the judgments dealing with motion for summary judgment. The defendants, in a cross-bill of exceptions, assign error on the judgments overruling their demurrers.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed on main bill of exceptions. Cross-bill of exceptions dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee appealed the decision of the Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the former employee's motion to dismiss the motion for summary judgment of defendants, employer and others, in the former employee's action for libel, and which granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The former employee brought an action for libel based on a separation notice filed by defendants, and delivered to the Employment Security Agency. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss and grant of the motion for summary judgment. The court held that (1) the former employee's claim that the affidavit attached to the summary judgment motion contained some inadmissible evidence was insufficient because he did not specify the portion which was objectionable; therefore he could not move to exclude the document in its entirety; (2) the former employee failed to establish a constitutional question because he did not show its unconstitutionality with fair precision, show what was violated, or show how the statute violated the constitution; and (3) the summary judgment was properly granted because the alleged publication was absolutely privileged pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 54-642.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the former employee's motion to dismiss defendants' motion for summary judgment, and the grant of summary judgment for defendants in the former employee's libel action.

 

1951 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Chronister v. Atlanta


No. 37618


Court of Appeals of Georgia


99 Ga. App. 447; 108 S.E.2d 731; 1959 Ga. App. LEXIS 877



April 24, 1959, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson. January 21, 1959.

Rube Chronister filed an action for damages against the City of Atlanta in the Superior Court of Fulton County, which, as amended, alleges that in 1929 the defendant commenced operating the Atlanta Municipal Airport; in 1947 the plaintiff purchased a tract of land adjacent thereto on which is located his dwelling house; in 1952, the defendant constructed a new southwest runway which terminates approximately 500 yards from the northeast boundary of his property; the airplanes operating from this runway continually fly directly over petitioner's home at altitudes of 50 to 100 feet, which interferes with his reasonable use of his property, is a hazard to life and limb, has caused impairment of the health of himself and family, and is imminently dangerous to the plaintiff and his family. The defendant's negligence is alleged as follows: "The said City of Atlanta exercises general supervision and control of said Atlanta Municipal Airport by and through a paid official of the City of Atlanta designated as Airport Manager, and through the Aviation Committee of the Board of Aldermen of the City of Atlanta [***2] . . . The City of Atlanta permits and allows the use of such southwest runway by the various airlines in the foregoing manner, and has failed and refused to exert its supervisory power and control over the airlines in such a manner as to prohibit flights in the above manner by the various airlines operating from said airport, such operation constituting a continuing nuisance." Various general and special demurrers were filed. The trial court sustained the general demurrers and dismissed the petition, to which judgment exception is taken.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of an order entered in the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained defendant city's demurrer filed in the property owner's action alleging that the city's operation of an airport runway in close proximity to his property constituted a continuing nuisance.


OVERVIEW: The city commenced to operate a municipal airport in 1929. In 1947, the property owner purchased a tract of land adjacent to the airport. In 1952, the city constructed a runway contiguous to the boundary of the property owner's land. The trial court sustained the city's demurrer to the property owner's action alleging that the city refused to exercise its supervisory power and control over the airlines using its facilities in such manner as to prohibit them from making improper flights at low altitudes over the property owner's land. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order and ruled that the property owner was entitled to redress from the city for any use of the air space above his land that resulted in injury to him or his property. The court rejected the city's argument that because the airport was subject to federal regulation, the city had no power of control over the manner that aircraft used the runway facilities provided by the city. The court concluded that the fact that the location and altitude of landing operations was subject to federal control did not determine whether the city violated the rights of a surface owner by such flights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order sustaining the city's demurrer filed in the property owner's action alleging that the city's operation of an airport runway in close proximity to his property constituted a continuing nuisance.

 

1952 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Garland v. Tanksley


No. 37585


Court of Appeals of Georgia


99 Ga. App. 201; 107 S.E.2d 866; 1959 Ga. App. LEXIS 818



March 2, 1959, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lawyer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of the Atlanta Judicial Circuit (Georgia), which denied the lawyer's petition for supersedeas of respondent judge's judgment of contempt.


OVERVIEW: The lawyer filed a petition for supersedeas of the trial court's judgment denying the petition of supersedeas of the judge's contempt judgment. Counsel for the judge filed a motion to dismiss the petition on the ground that the relief prayed for was not within the jurisdiction of the court to grant. The court held that it had the authority to hear and decide the lawyer's petition. The court found that the trial court abused its discretion in denying the supersedeas when the lawyer was sentenced for two separate contempts to serve the maximum of 40 days, the lawyer would not have been able to gain a review of the judgment of the trial court under which he was imprisoned unless a supersedeas was granted. The court granted the lawyer's petition. Upon rehearing, the court modified the order granting supersedeas allowing the lawyer three days to apply for a new supersedeas.


OUTCOME: The court granted the lawyer's petition for supersedeas of the judge's contempt judgment. Upon rehearing, the court modified the order granting supersedeas allowing the lawyer three days to apply for a new supersedeas.

 

1953 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State Highway Dep't v. Wilson


No. 37290


Court of Appeals of Georgia


98 Ga. App. 619; 106 S.E.2d 544; 1958 Ga. App. LEXIS 642



October 14, 1958, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 13, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation. Tift Superior Court. Before Judge Gray. May 29, 1958.

On January 11, 1958, the State Highway Department of Georgia commenced a proceeding in the Superior Court of Tift County to condemn for public purposes certain property of Reid Wilson and others. Assessors were appointed on February 1, a hearing held on February 6, and an award entered and filed in the superior court on the same date, awarding the condemnee $ 12,140.50 as the value of the property plus consequential damages of $ 19,591.34 and finding no consequential benefits. On February 14, 1958, the State Highway Department filed its appeal to the jury pursuant to the provisions of Code §§ 36-601 and 36-1110. Judgment for the condemnee was entered by the court on February 24. On February 26, the sum of $ 31,731.84 was tendered into court for the benefit of the condemnees. On May 5, a motion by the condemnees to take down the tender was made and granted. On May 20, a motion to dismiss the appeal on the ground that at the time of filing of the appeal no tender or payment of the amount in question had been made. A motion to strike the vital paragraphs of this motion [***2] was made and denied, and the court then entered up judgment dismissing the appeal, and these judgments are assigned as error.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error State Highway Department of Georgia sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Tift County (Georgia), which dismissed an appeal of an assessor's condemnation award for defendant condemnee on the basis that the State failed to comply with a condition precedent to appeal by first tendering the amount of the award.


OVERVIEW: The State objected to the requirement for tending the award as a condition of appeal. On review, the court concluded that, based on case law and the constitutional law on condemnation, the trial court did not err in imposing the requirement. The court concluded that the issue was controlled by a case precedent that was binding on the State. The court read the case as holding that the Georgia Constitution required that there be such a prepayment before there was any taking at all, which meant not only physical appropriation but a legal taking as well, as first evidenced by the filing of the condemnation proceedings, or by any act where a property owner was deprived of some substantial interest in property. The court indicated that when an award of the assessors was returned, it was subject, under O.C.G.A. § 36-508, to become a judgment by a tribunal competent in law to fix the rights and liabilities of the parties to the proceedings. From that moment on, the court declared, the condemnor, meaning the State, had no justifiable excuse for refusing to abide the prepayment provision of the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1954 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Albany


No. 37160


Court of Appeals of Georgia


97 Ga. App. 731; 104 S.E.2d 488; 1958 Ga. App. LEXIS 868



June 23, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Possessing lottery tickets; petition for certiorari. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Crow. March 20, 1958.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possessing lottery tickets in a city court and filed a petition for certiorari in the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia). The trial court overruled the petition for certiorari, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the city ordinance under which she was convicted was illegal and void because it did not provide that the possession of lottery paraphernalia must be coupled with the intent to violate the ordinance, and she argued that the ordinance was in direct conflict with the provisions of Ga. Const. art. 1, § 2, para. 4; O.G.C.A. § 2-204, prohibiting lotteries and the sale of lottery tickets. The court held that the trial court did not err in overruling the petition for certiorari. The court found that the constitutional attack was too vague and general to raise any question as to the constitutionality of the ordinance insofar as it might have contravened the due-process clauses of the state and federal constitutions. It followed that the trial court did not err in overruling the certiorari insofar as it sought to raise the constitutionality of the ordinance under the state and federal due-process clauses. The court also held that Ga. Const. art. 1, § 2, para. 4; O.G.C.A. § 2-204, and O.G.C.A. §§ 26-6501, 26-6502, did not prohibit the mere possession of lottery tickets and other paraphernalia or make that possession a crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1955 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Lockridge-Rogers Lumber Co. v. East Point


No. 37069


Court of Appeals of Georgia


97 Ga. App. 357; 103 S.E.2d 160; 1958 Ga. App. LEXIS 777



March 21, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affidavit of illegality; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Andrews. December 9, 1957.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to the Supreme Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant lumber company appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which overruled the company's affidavit of illegality filed in response to a fieri fascias writ issued by plaintiff city for the collection of a sewer assessment. The trial court ordered that the levy proceed.


OVERVIEW: The company contended that an ordinance adopted pursuant to the city's charter requiring abutting land owners to pay the cost of sewers was violative of Ga. Const. art. I, § 1(3) providing that no person shall be deprived of life, liberty, or property without due process of law. The company also contended that the ordinance violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV for failure to afford a defendant in fieri facias any notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court noted that the U.S. Supreme Court, contrary to the Supreme Court of Georgia's holding that challenges to the constitutionality of a statute were required to particularize the challenged provisions, had held that a general attack upon an ordinance as a whole as being unconstitutional was sufficient to draw in question the constitutionality of the ordinance under the U.S. Constitution. The court concluded that the allegations of the company's affidavit were sufficient to raise the question as to the constitutionality of the city charter under the Fourteenth Amendment. Because the pleadings raised a question as to the constitutionality of a state law, the Supreme Court of Georgia had exclusive jurisdiction of the case.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the Supreme Court of Georgia.

 

1956 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Suwannee Longleaf Mfg. Co.


No. 37063


Court of Appeals of Georgia


97 Ga. App. 431; 103 S.E.2d 123; 1958 Ga. App. LEXIS 793



March 19, 1958, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for tax refund; isolated sale, etc. Clinch Superior Court. Before Judge Huxford. December 16, 1957.

A taxpayer bought tangible personal property within the State of Georgia at a sale other than at retail, the sale being a casual sale, and paid a 3 percent sales or use tax to the seller who remitted the tax, less his commission for collection, to the State. The taxpayer sued the Revenue Commissioner for a refund of the amount of the tax received by the Commissioner. The Commissioner's general demurrer to the petition for refund was overruled and the Commissioner excepted.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Revenue Commissioner challenged the judgment of the Clinch Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled the commissioner's general demurrer upon the taxpayer's claim for a refund of the amount of tax received by the commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer bought tangible personal property within the State of Georgia at a sale that was not a retail sale, but a casual sale. The taxpayer paid a three percent sales or use tax to the seller who remitted the tax, less his commission for collection, to the State of Georgia. The commissioner found that two separate taxes should be imposed. The court found that casual and isolated sales within the State were not subject to any tax under the sales and use tax statutes and affirmed the order overruling the demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment overruling the demurrer.

 

1957 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Fortson v. Clarke County


No. 36949


Court of Appeals of Georgia


97 Ga. App. 410; 103 S.E.2d 597; 1958 Ga. App. LEXIS 789



February 13, 1958, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 3, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's compensation. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Cobb. September 21, 1957.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from the Clarke Superior Court (Georgia) judgment for defendant county in his suit for workmen's compensation benefits. The issue was whether a county was an employer under the provisions of the Workmen's Compensation Act in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 114-101, as he claimed.


OVERVIEW: Whether the employee was entitled to workmen's compensation benefits from his county employer was based on whether the county was subject to the state's Workmen's Compensation Act in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 114-101. The administrative board awarded compensation. The superior court reversed. The court affirmed, overruling Walker v. Wilcox County, 97 S.E.2d 583 (Ga. App.), which had held that because of changes in constitutional and statutory enactments, counties were subject to the Workmen's Compensation Act. Though the original statute included municipal corporations and political subdivisions in coverage, it was declared unconstitutional until Walker. In 1945, it was made permissive for counties to provide workmen's compensation, with statutory authority to levy taxes to pay for it. The issue was whether subsequent statutory amendments reinstated the original act as to all counties or just those of a certain size. The court held that O.C.G.A. § 114-101, having been declared unconstitutional as to counties, was to that extent void, and until reinstatement by express legislative enactment, counties other than those of a certain size did not come within its provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the decision of the full workmen's compensation board, which had awarded the employee compensation, was affirmed as it was without error. The county was not subject to the workmen's compensation law.

 

1958 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Owens v. Floyd County


No. 36701


Court of Appeals of Georgia


96 Ga. App. 25; 99 S.E.2d 560; 1957 Ga. App. LEXIS 495



May 28, 1957, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Money had and received. Before Judge Hicks. Floyd Superior Court. March 8, 1957.

In Walden v. Owens, 211 Ga. 884 (89 S. E. 2d 492), the Supreme Court held that an act placing certain officers of Floyd County, Georgia, on a salary in lieu of fees was unconstitutional, and this court in Owens v. Floyd County, 94 Ga. App. 532 (95 S. E. 2d 389), an action in which the Clerk of the Superior Court of Floyd County sought to recover the fees he had paid into the county treasury of Floyd County under the act placing him on a salary in lieu of fees, held that the trial court erred in sustaining a general demurrer to the petition. Thereafter, after the judgment of this court was made the judgment of the trial court, the plaintiff's demurrers to the defendant's answer came on to be heard, and the trial court overruled certain of such demurrers, and on the trial the jury returned a verdict for the county, which verdict was made the judgment of the trial court. The plaintiff filed a motion for new trial on the usual general grounds which he later amended by adding several special grounds, and, having made a motion for a directed verdict at the conclusion [***2] of the evidence, made a motion for a judgment non obstante veredicto. Both the amended motion for new trial and the motion for judgment non obstante veredicto were denied and it is to these judgments that the plaintiff excepts, as well as to the judgment overruling certain of his demurrers to the answer, and to a judgment of the trial court passing on a demurrer filed by the defendant to an amendment to the plaintiff's petition filed after the judgment of this court was made the judgment of the trial court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the clerk of a superior court, sought review of a decision of the Floyd County Superior Court (Georgia). The decision denied the clerk's motions for a new trial and for judgment non obstante veredicto in his action against defendant county to recover fees paid into the county treasury under the Act of 1950, 1950 Ga. Laws 2389 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Georgia Supreme Court held that an act placing county officers on a salary in lieu of fees was unconstitutional, and the clerk filed an action against the county to recover fees that he had paid into the county treasury. The trial court sustained a general demurrer to the petition, and the court held that the trial court had erred. A jury returned a verdict in favor of the county. The trial court denied the clerk's motions for a directed verdict, for a new trial, and for judgment non obstante veredicto. The court reversed the decision. The court held that the clerk's campaign promises did not constitute any defense to the action. The court concluded that once the act was declared invalid, the clerk immediately had a right to demand an accounting from the county for the fees delivered to it under the act and was entitled to the fees delivered over and above the amount expended in the operation of the clerk's office, except those that the county was bound to expend when the office was operating on a fee basis. The court found that the clerk was not estopped from recovering the amount due him and that the parties had stipulated to an amount if the clerk was entitled to recover.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and directed the trial court to enter a judgment for the clerk.

 

1959 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Dixie Constr. Co. v. Williams


No. 36710


Court of Appeals of Georgia


95 Ga. App. 767; 98 S.E.2d 582; 1957 Ga. App. LEXIS 913



May 17, 1957, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affidavit of illegality. Before Judge McWhorter. Chatham Superior Court. February 13, 1957.

The Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., filed in the Superior Court of Chatham County its affidavit of illegality together with eventual condemnation money bond to the entry of levy on personalty and sales tax fi. fa. issued by the State Revenue Commissioner.

The parties stipulated the following facts: On March 17, 1951, the Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., defendant in fi. fa., entered into a contract with the Florida-Georgia Tractor Company of Jacksonville, Florida, for the purchase and sale of two tractors and a motor grader. The net purchase price of the equipment was $ 59,187.08. The equipment, which was the subject of the aforesaid purchase, was delivered by the seller, Florida-Georgia Tractor Company, to the purchaser, Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., at Savannah, Georgia, on April 17, 1951. The equipment was purchased by Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., for use and consumption within the State of Georgia, and, at all times after it was delivered, was used by the Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., in Georgia.

No sales [***2] tax was collected or returned by the Florida-Georgia Tractor Company on the said sale, and no sales or use tax return or remittance of the use tax with regard to the said purchase was ever made by Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc. On July 28, 1954, a proposed assessment of additional tax, penalty and interest on the purchase was made and mailed to Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc. On the 23rd day of August, 1954, Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., duly entered its protest to the proposed assessment and requested a hearing before the Commissioner of Revenue. No sales and use tax return was ever filed by Dixie Construction Company of Georgia, Inc., for the month of April, 1951. Counsel further stipulates that, except for the month of November, 1951, taxpayer has regularly filed sales and use tax returns for each and every month thereafter.

The case was heard without the intervention of a jury and the trial judge entered an order finding against the affidavit of illegality. It is to this ruling the defendant in fi. fa. excepts.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged the decision of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled against the taxpayer's affidavit of illegality to the entry of a levy issued by defendant tax commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that any liability for the use tax purchase was barred by the statute of limitation as set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 92-3447(a). In 1953, § 92-3447(a) was amended by adding the following: Provided, however, in the case of a false or fraudulent return with intent to evade payment of taxes imposed by this act or a failure to file a return, the tax may be assessed or a proceeding in court for the collection of such tax may be begun without assessment at any time. The court concluded that the controlling question in the case was whether the amendment would affect a sale that had taken place less than three years prior to the passage of the amendment. The court determined that the 1953 amendment of § 92-3447 (a) had the effect of extending the statute of limitation as to the collection of the use tax, and the trial judge did not err in ruling against the affidavit of illegality. Accordingly, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which ruled against the taxpayer's affidavit of illegality to the entry of a levy issued by the tax commissioner.

 

1960 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Atl. C. L. R. Co. v. Scott


No. 36441


Court of Appeals of Georgia


95 Ga. App. 70; 97 S.E.2d 325; 1957 Ga. App. LEXIS 716



January 18, 1957, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tort; cattle killed by train. Before Judge Lilly. Thomas Superior Court. August 1, 1956.

As counsel for the plaintiff concedes that the substance of the pleadings is correctly set forth in the brief submitted by counsel for the defendant, we shall more or less follow that statement in setting forth our statement of facts. The plaintiff filed his action against the defendant in the Superior Court of Thomas County alleging that the defendant, between 6 p. m. and 7 p. m. on July 16, 1953, was negligent in killing certain cattle belonging to the plaintiff on the defendant's right-of-way in Thomas County to the plaintiff's injury and damage in the sum of $ 8,300, the alleged value of six head of cattle alleged to have been killed. The plaintiff alleged that the defendant was negligent in failing to keep a lookout ahead, in failing to see the cattle on the tracks, in failing to blow the whistle or ring the bell to warn the cattle, in failing to reduce the speed of the train or bring it under control or do anything else to avoid striking the cattle. The plaintiff alleged that it was daylight at the time the cattle were killed and that the [***2] railroad track was straight and unobstructed in view for one mile. The plaintiff alleged that a fence post about the northeast corner of his pasture on the south side of the railroad gave way and fell, leaving an opening in the fence through which the plaintiff's cows went out and onto the tracks and right-of-way of the defendant, that during the morning of that same day, the plaintiff had inspected the fence and no post was down nor was there any opening in the fence.

The defendant filed its general demurrer to the petition and one special demurrer based upon the ground that the petition did not allege whether Thomas County was a "fence" or "no-fence" county. The defendant filed its answer either denying or negativing every paragraph of the petition. In addition, the defendant affirmatively alleged that Thomas County was a no-fence county, that the plaintiff's cattle were trespassing on the defendant's right-of-way, that its only duty was not to wilfully and wantonly injure the cattle after discovering their presence, that it had no reason to anticipate the presence of such cattle, that the sole proximate cause of any injury and damage to the plaintiff's cattle was the negligence [***3] of the plaintiff in failing to keep the cattle enclosed and off the defendant's right-of-way.

The defendant's demurrers were overruled and error is assigned here upon that judgment.

On the trial of the case it was stipulated that Thomas County is a county having adopted the stock law as provided in chapter 62-5 of the Code of Georgia of 1933, which law was in full force and effect at the time of the killing of the cattle for which suit was brought. The jury found in favor of the plaintiff for the sum of $ 7,175 and judgment was rendered accordingly.

The defendant's motion for a new trial, based upon the usual general grounds and 11 special grounds, was denied, and error is assigned here on that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad company sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Thomas County (Georgia), which overruled the railroad company's demurrers and denied the railroad company's motion for a new trial in a negligence action. Appellee cattle owner had brought the action against the railroad company alleging that the railroad company was negligent in killing certain cattle belonging to the owner.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was the degree of care is owed by a railroad company in the operation of its trains to livestock on its tracks and right-of-way in a no-fence county. The railroad company argued that under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 62-501 the owner of livestock was required to fence his cattle, and in a no-fence county cattle coming upon the right-of-way of the railroad company were trespassers, which changed the railroad company's duty from one of ordinary care to avoid injuring cattle on its right-of-way to a duty not to wilfully and wantonly injure cattle upon its right-of-way after it has discovered their presence. On appeal, the court held that, generally, the stock law, known as the no-fence law, did not change the degree of negligence from ordinary negligence to wilful and wanton negligence. The fact that the damage alleged was in a locality where the stock law was in operation could be considered along with all the other facts and circumstances of the case to be determined by the jury as to whether the railroad was liable. The court held that the trial court did not err in overruling the general demurrer or in denying the motion for new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1961 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Owens v. Floyd County


No. 36320


Court of Appeals of Georgia


94 Ga. App. 532; 95 S.E.2d 389; 1956 Ga. App. LEXIS 605



November 9, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Money had and received. Before Judge Hicks. Floyd Superior Court. June 8, 1956.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen challenged the judgment from the Floyd Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained defendant county's demurrers and dismissed the citizen's petition for money had and received. The citizen had sought the equitable recovery of fees that she had allegedly paid into the county under a mistake of law.


OVERVIEW: The citizen claimed that she had mistakenly paid in commission fees and that the county received the benefit of her fees which, in equity and good conscience, it could not retain. She did not seek payment from the county but rather sought the repayment of money already had and received by the county. A county official already paid himself the commissions and refunded the money to the county treasurer. However, the county refused to repay the citizen and claimed that it was not liable to any suit unless made so by statute, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 23-1502. The court found that, under the prior caselaw, a suit for money had and received, where it was against equity and good conscience for the one receiving it, including a county, was not based on a contract or a statute. Therefore, the court rejected the county's argument and found that although the money was paid through a mistake of law, with full knowledge of all the facts, it could be recovered because the county could not in good conscience retain it. The court found that the trial court committed reversible error in sustaining the demurrers and dismissing the petition. Accordingly, the court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment rendered by the trial court, which sustained the county's demurrers and dismissed the citizen's petition against it for money that she had allegedly paid into the court under a mistake of law.

 

1962 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cent. of G. R. Co. v. Hester


No. 36201


Court of Appeals of Georgia


94 Ga. App. 226; 94 S.E.2d 124; 1956 Ga. App. LEXIS 513



May 17, 1956, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tort; railroad crossing collision. Before Judge Henson. Fulton Civil Court. March 6, 1956.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant railroad company appealed a judgment of the Fulton Civil Court (Georgia), which entered a jury's verdict in favor of plaintiff individual in a tort action seeking damages for a railroad crossing collision and overruled the company's amended motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The individual sought damages for injuries suffered in a collision with a train due to the company's negligence. The company claimed that the individual was not entitled to recover damages because, by the exercise of ordinary care, he could have avoided any negligence. The civil court charged the jury that the burden shifted from the company to the individual. The civil court entered judgment for the individual on the jury's verdict and overruled the company's amended motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed the individual's judgment by finding that the civil court erred in overruling the company's request for a new trial. As the jury could have mistakenly inferred from the charge that the burden of proof in the case was at that time on the company, the erroneous charge constituted reversible error. The burden of proof always remained with the individual and the burden of procedure or the burden of introducing evidence was all that could shift back to the individual once the company introduced some evidence to rebut the prima facie presumption of the company's negligence established by the individual's proof of injury from the train collision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the civil court's judgment against the railroad company.

Hobbs v. New England Ins. Co.


No. 36131


Court of Appeals of Georgia


93 Ga. App. 687; 92 S.E.2d 636; 1956 Ga. App. LEXIS 831



April 2, 1956, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on insurance policy; constitutional question. Before Judge Perryman. McDuffie Superior Court. January 14, 1956.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to Supreme Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sought review of a decision from the McDuffie Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant insurance company in an action seeking recovery for a fire loss under the terms of an insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: A house owned by the insured burned. Unable to obtain satisfaction from his insurance company, the insured filed an action seeking recovery under the policy. The matter ultimately resulted in a verdict being directed in favor of the insurance company. The insured appealed, arguing, among other issues, that the trial court refused to entertain the insured's motion to strike the insurance company's pleas as a penalty for refusing to file answers to interrogatories propounded, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 38-1202(2). The court held that because the insurance company challenged the constitutionality of § 38-1202(2) , such a determination would be required in order to resolve the other issues on appeal, and because the court was without jurisdiction to make that determination, the matter should be transferred to the state supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the state supreme court for a determination of the constitutionality of the statute at issue.

1965 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ga. S. & F. R. Co. v. Wilson


Nos. 35705, 35827


Court of Appeals of Georgia


93 Ga. App. 94; 91 S.E.2d 71; 1955 Ga. App. LEXIS 486



October 18, 1955, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 10, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Damages. Before Judge Smith. Clinch Superior Court. March 7, 1955.

Furman Wilson filed an action for damages against the Georgia, Southern & Florida Railway Company in Clinch Superior Court, based on the alleged wrongful death of the plaintiff's son.

The petition was in two counts. Count one, as finally amended alleged: that the defendant operated a railroad in Clinch County, Georgia, and that its track ran through a community known as Headlight in that county, at a point where the tracks were straight and had no obstructions for several miles which would prevent the operating personnel from seeing clearly up and down the tracks at this point; that Furman Wilson, Jr., was the plaintiff's son who at the time of his death was 21 years of age without living mother, wife or children; that the deceased son suffered severe attacks of asthma which sometimes rendered him helpless; that on January 13, 1952, he was overcome with such an attack while on a well beaten path across the railroad 75 feet north of a public crossing in Headlight; that the path had been continuously used by the public with knowledge and without disapproval of the defendant;  [***2] that the employees neither reduced the speed of the train nor gave any warning and ran over and killed the plaintiff's son.

Count two was the same as count one except it placed the plaintiff's son two hundred feet west of the crossing, and alleged wilful and wanton negligence.

The witness for the plaintiff testified in reference to the pathway referred to in the petition as a crossing, that it had been generally used for a considerable time by the public and that the defendant had indicated no disapproval of this use. One witness dated the use of the pathway from World War I. The defendant's witnesses testified that the path did not exist at the time the plaintiff's son was killed; the defendant's employees particularly denied that they had observed it being used by anyone.

It appears from the plaintiff's testimony that his son was 21 years old at the time he was killed; his mother did not survive him; that he had never been married, and had a stated earning capacity. The plaintiff further related that his son had suffered with an asthmatic condition all his life, that when a severe attack seized him it would choke him down and that he had to stop wherever he happened to be;  [***3] before his departure from home on the day of his death he was choking with asthma; that he used Vick's salve in obtaining relief from such attacks.

The plaintiff gave evidence that certain articles carried by his son on the day he lost his life, namely his shoes, a rope and a bottle of Vick's salve were found on the pathway where the plaintiff contended the train struck him. Witnesses testifying in behalf of the defendant testified that these articles were discovered after the tragedy about one-half mile from the crossing at Headlight, and approximately that distance from where the plaintiff claimed that contact between his son and the engine was made, at which point there was no pathway. There was evidence that the railroad track from the direction from which the train was proceeding to the pathway where the plaintiff maintained his son was killed, was level and straight for approximately three miles. The evidence was conflicting as to whether the day was clear or hazy. The plaintiff testified positively that the day was clear and one of the plaintiff's witnesses swore it was "kinder hazy."

The plaintiff testified that he lived about three hundred fifty to four hundred yards [***4] or farther from the locale of the pathway; that from the location of his home he could hear the whistle and bells of the engines when they approached the crossing at Head-light and the pathway in question; that on the occasion of his son's death the whistle of the train was not blown nor its bell rung as the engine traveled toward the crossing and pathway.

The engineer in charge of the defendant's locomotive on the occasion under investigation testified that when coming in sight of the place where the young man was killed that the train was traveling from forty-five to fifty miles per hour; that when he first observed the object on the track ahead that later turned out to be the plaintiff's son he was not able to discern what it was at a distance of two hundred to two hundred fifty yards, but when the engine approached closer to the object he thought it might be a piece of a cow with buzzards eating it; he testified as the examination progressed that he took the object to be a faulty belt which frequently fell from trains and lay on the tracks; that these belts were about eight inches wide and fourteen feet long; that at the point where he first observed the object, which he later [***5] discovered to be a man, he would have been unable normally to stop the train before striking the man; that when in about one hundred to two hundred fifty feet from where the engine did strike him, he was able for the first time to determine that the object on the track was a man; that he did everything that was possible to prevent running over the man; that he applied the locomotive's brakes, rang the bell and sounded the whistle.

Another engineer in the defendant's service, who was the only other person on the engine at the time, corroborated the first engineer's testimony as to the speed of the train, the sounding of the going, and the application of the brakes. He further testified that when at a distance of three hundred fifty to four hundred yards from the deceased he first saw him, he thought that the object ahead was a pulley belt of the description testified to by the other engineer; that the belts did frequently fall and remain on the tracks, and he further related that when in about two hundred to three hundred feet of the object he too discovered that it was a man; that he then apprised the engineer who was operating the engine of that fact, and the latter at the same [***6] time applied the brakes, and sounded the whistle. The engine was a General Motors diesel, and there was evidence that both engineers were qualified and experienced in handling a locomotive of that kind. The evidence contained other details that are not important to the decision of the case.

The case went to the jury on the issue of simple negligence and a verdict was returned for the plaintiff. The defendant filed a motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict and a motion for new trial on the general grounds and amended it by adding 13 special grounds. The trial judge denied each of these motions, the defendant excepted and the case is here for review.

The evidence is not set out in detail in this statement of fact for the reason that so much of it as is necessary to a clear understanding of the rulings made is extensively discussed in the opinion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on main bill of exceptions, cross-bill dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a railroad, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Clinch County (Georgia), which was entered for plaintiff, a parent of an adult child victim, in his action for damages that alleged the victim was killed on a railroad track by a train as a result of negligence.


OVERVIEW: The victim suffered severe asthma attacks that sometimes rendered him helpless. The parent alleged that a train ran over and killed the victim after the victim was overcome by such an attack while he was on a well-beaten path across a railroad track north of a public crossing at a community along the track. The parent also alleged that the path had been in continuous use with knowledge and without objection by the railroad and that the railroad's employees neither reduced the train's speed nor gave any warning. The court held that the trial court properly charged the jury in the language of O.C.G.A. § 94-1108 as to the shifting of the burden of evidence, as distinguished from the burden of proof. The trial court properly instructed the jury that if it believed the railroad's employees did violate a public-crossing law, it could consider that fact in its determination of whether their negligence caused the employee's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment. The parent's cross-bill was dismissed.

 

1966 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. Day


No. 35836


Court of Appeals of Georgia


92 Ga. App. 680; 89 S.E.2d 674; 1955 Ga. App. LEXIS 687



October 5, 1955, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to legitimatize child. Before Judge Davis. Walker Superior Court. June 11, 1955.

On July 24, 1954, John D. Day (hereinafter called the plaintiff), filed his petition in the Superior Court of Walker County, alleging that he is a resident of Walker County; that he is the father of an illegitimate female child, three years of age, born on March 18, 1951, in Hamilton County, Tennessee, and now residing in Fulton or DeKalb County, Georgia, whose name is Daphne Virginia Bennett; that the mother of said child is Barbara Jean Bennett (hereinafter called the defendant); that the mother of said child is now in life and residing in Atlanta, Georgia, and that the plaintiff desires that the name of said child be changed from the name Daphne Virginia Bennett to the name Daphne Virginia Day; and he prays that said child may be legitimatized by the name last mentioned. The petition so filed was verified by the plaintiff on July 24, 1954, and a notice by the plaintiff was attached to the petition, directed to the defendant, advising of the filing of said petition to the August term, 1954, of Walker Superior Court, and reciting that the application would be heard at the August term,  [***2] 1954, of said court on August 16, 1954, at 10 o'clock a. m. Following the petition appears the order of Hon. Freeman C. McClure, Judge Superior Courts, Lookout Mountain Circuit, dated August 13, 1954, ordering that a copy of the petition and order be served upon the mother of the child, the defendant, and that said petition be heard at the courthouse in Walker County, Georgia, on August 23, 1954, at 5 o'clock p. m. Service of the petition and order upon the defendant on August 18, 1954, is shown by the affidavit of Bernard W. Harper. By order of August 21, 1954, the court granted the defendant until September 4, 1954, to file demurrers, pleas, and objections in said cause and set same for hearing on September 24, 1954 at 5 o'clock p. m.

On August 27, 1954, and before any trial or hearing in said cause, the defendant filed her plea to the jurisdiction of the court, asserting therein: that she is the natural mother of the child named in said cause, and that the Superior Court of Walker County, Georgia, ought not to have or take cognizance of said suit because at the time of the commencement of same, on July 24, 1954, and thenceforth, the said defendant resided in the County of DeKalb,  [***3] Georgia, and is now a resident of said County of DeKalb and is not a resident of the County of Walker; and that the Superior Court of DeKalb County, Georgia, has jurisdiction of this case, and the Superior Court of Walker County has not, for the further reason that the child, Daphne Virginia Bennett, the subject for which the petition in said cause has been brought to legitimatize, was at the time of the filing of said suit and is now a resident of DeKalb County, Georgia, and the Superior Court of DeKalb County, Georgia, has jurisdiction of said child, and the Superior Court of Walker County, Georgia, has not. The plea to the jurisdiction was duly verified by the defendant and duly served upon opposing counsel, as shown by the certificate of service attached thereto.

On the same date of August 27, 1954, the defendant also filed her plea in abatement to the petition filed in said cause, asserting in said plea that she is the natural mother of said child; that the petition should abate for the reason that an action has been filed by Mr. and Mrs. H. L. Hatton for the adoption of the minor child, which proceeding is pending in the Superior Court of DeKalb County, Georgia; that the defendant [***4] has heretofore and in connection with said adoption proceedings given her consent to the same, and temporary custody of said child has been heretofore awarded to the said Mr. and Mrs. H. L. Hatton; and that the mother of said illegitimate child is entitled to exercise all parental power as to said child under the provisions of Georgia Code §§ 74-203 and 74-405; and since her consent has been given as aforesaid and in connection with said adoption proceedings, pendency of same is a bar to this proceeding to legitimatize said child, filed subsequently to the filing of said adoption proceedings. The plea in abatement further asserts that the child is a resident of DeKalb County, Georgia, and that the superior court of said county in which said adoption proceeding is pending has jurisdiction thereof. The plea in abatement concludes that the Superior Court of Walker County, Georgia, should not try the petition of the defendant to legitimatize said child for the reasons stated; and that same should be abated until the final judgment and decree upon said adoption proceeding pending in the Superior Court of DeKalb County, Georgia. The plea in abatement is duly verified by the defendant,  [***5] and service thereof was perfected in accordance with the certificate of service attached thereto.

On the same date the defendant filed her answer, objecting to the granting of the prayers of the petition. The objection as so filed by the defendant prayed that the prayers of the petition be denied, and that he not be permitted to legitimatize said Daphne Virginia Bennett, and that her name not be changed to Daphne Virginia Day.

In support of her objection to the legitimation of her child by the petitioner, the defendant alleged in her answer that she is the natural mother of Daphne Virginia Bennett, and by reason of such relationship is entitled to file her objections and be heard in this cause; and without admitting the paternity of the child by the plaintiff, the answer avers that the petition of the plaintiff to legitimatize the daughter of the defendant is not filed in good faith, but is fraudulently brought, and that he has no parental interest in said child.

The answer makes numerous detailed averments of unfitness and fraud upon the part of the plaintiff, which may be summarized in part as follows: that the plaintiff is a married man 62 years of age, of intemperate habits,  [***6] frequently engaging in adulterous relationships with other women, violent and abusive in conduct, unfit to have the custody or control of a 3-year-old female child, addicted to the excessive use of intoxicants, a professional gambler convicted of the offense of illegal enterprises, who will leave no estate for said child to inherit; that plaintiff has brought his petition to legitimatize said child in bad faith and fraudulently as a part of a scheme to gain control of said child in order that he may, through the mother's love and affection of said child and concern for her welfare, force the defendant to renew her cohabitation and adulterous relationship with him; that he has not contributed anything toward the support of said child, has denied his paternity of the child, and, while cohabiting with the defendant, refused upon request to render said child legitimate. The answer alleges at length numerous facts and specific acts upon the part of the plaintiff in support of the foregoing averments. The answer further alleges that the defendant, having separated from the plaintiff, is living an upright and moral life and adequately providing for the support of said child from her earnings [***7] as a waitress; and that she is a fit and proper person to have the custody of the child, and to have the child bear her name until such time as the child may be adopted by fit and proper adoptive parents; that Mr. and Mrs. H. L. Hatton of DeKalb County, Georgia, have instituted adoption proceedings in the Superior Court of DeKalb County, Georgia, for the adoption of said child; and that they have temporary custody of the child under those proceedings pending the final order of adoption.

On September 24, 1954, said case came on for a hearing before the court, and after argument of counsel an oral motion was made by counsel for the plaintiff to dismiss the plea to the jurisdiction and to dismiss the plea in abatement filed in said cause by the defendant; and said plea to the jurisdiction and said plea in abatement were each, by orders dated September 24, 1954, dismissed.

To the orders sustaining the plaintiff's oral motions to dismiss said plea to the jurisdiction and said plea in abatement the defendant excepted and by her bill of exceptions excepts to said rulings of the court; and the questions raised by the assignments of error on the court's order sustaining the motion to said [***8] plea to the jurisdiction and on the order sustaining the motion to the plea in abatement are now before this court for review.

On said date of September 24, 1954, the case proceeded to trial on its merits before Honorable Freeman C. McClure, judge of said court, in accordance with the provisions of Code § 74-103. A jury trial was not waived by objector nor was trial by a jury dispensed with by agreement of the parties or by agreement of counsel for the parties, but same proceeded to hearing before the court without a jury, under the provisions of said Code section, which makes no provision for a jury trial in such cases.

Upon said hearing and at the conclusion of the evidence submitted by the plaintiff and at the conclusion of the evidence submitted on behalf of the defendant, the court, upon oral motion of the plaintiff, continued the hearing to a subsequent unspecified date in order to enable the plaintiff to obtain additional evidence in the form of depositions.

By order dated October 29, 1954, the court set said matter for conclusion in a hearing thereon for November 20, 1954, at 10 o'clock a. m., and on said date the plaintiff presented additional evidence in the form of [***9] depositions taken in said cause, at the conclusion of which the court entered its final order, judgment and decree denying the prayers of the plaintiff to legitimatize the child, and taxing the costs in the case against the plaintiff.

On December 9, 1954, the plaintiff filed a motion for new trial upon the following grounds: (1) Because the decision of the court is contrary to evidence and without evidence to support it. (2) Because the decision is decidedly and strongly against the weight of the evidence. (3) Because the decision is contrary to law and the principles of justice and equity.

The foregoing proceedings were held before Honorable Freeman C. McClure, Judge of the Superior Court, Walker County, Georgia. On January 1, 1955, the said judge was succeeded as Judge of the Superior Court of Walker County, Georgia, by Honorable John W. Davis.

On May 10, 1955, the plaintiff filed his amendment to the original motion for new trial, setting forth several special grounds alleging error in excluding certain testimony offered on behalf of the plaintiff regarding plaintiff's character 20 years before this trial, and in excluding part of the deposition of a witness for the plaintiff [***10] which was excluded by the court because of the refusal of the witness to submit to complete cross-examination. The full and complete grounds of the motion as amended are set forth in the record specified in this case.

The plaintiff's motion for new trial came on for a hearing before Honorable John W. Davis, at a subsequent date, and at said hearing, prior to consideration of said motion for a new trial by the court, the defendant made an oral motion in open court as follows: "Defendant, Barbara Jean Bennett, moves to dismiss petitioner's motion for a new trial and amendment to motion for new trial upon the grounds that same is not the proper procedure, a direct bill of exceptions being the proper procedure."

By order dated June 11, 1955, Honorable John W. Davis denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the motion for new trial, filed by the plaintiff. To this order denying the defendant's motion, the defendant excepted and in her bill of exceptions assigns the order denying said motion as error. By order dated June 11, 1955, Honorable John W. Davis, entered the following order: "The motion for new trial in the above-styled matter is granted."

The defendant assigns error upon the [***11] rulings of the court overruling her plea to the jurisdiction, overruling her plea in abatement, and overruling her motion to dismiss the motion of the plaintiff for a new trial, and this cause is now before the Court of Appeals upon those assignments of error.

The issues of law involved are: (1) whether or not the court erred in overruling the defendant's plea to the jurisdiction; (2) whether or not the court erred in overruling the defendant's plea in abatement; (3) whether or not the court erred in denying the defendant's motion to dismiss the motion for a new trial filed by the plaintiff; (4) whether or not the court abused its discretion in granting a first new trial.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Walker County (Georgia), which denied her motion to dismiss appellee father's complaint to legitimize the child and her motion to dismiss his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The father filed an action in his county of residence to legitimize the child. The mother objected to the father's action because of an adoption proceeding in another court. The trial court denied the mother's motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the father's petition to legitimize the child. The father filed a motion for a new trial and the mother objected. The trial court granted the motion for a new trial and the mother appealed. The appellate court rejected the mother's argument that a statute relied upon by the trial court to determine jurisdiction was unconstitutional because the issue of unconstitutionality was not raised in the trial court. The court found that because neither party requested a jury trial, it was not error for the trial court to rule on the facts and law. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the father's motion for a new trial because the father presented evidence that supported his claim to legitimize the child and it was possible that, because of a change of judges in the trial court, the new judge felt that the father's petition should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the father's motion for a new trial.

 

1967 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Beard v. City of Atlanta


No. 35422


Court of Appeals of Georgia


91 Ga. App. 584; 86 S.E.2d 672; 1955 Ga. App. LEXIS 815



January 26, 1955, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 2, 1955, 91 Ga. App. 584.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari. Before Judge Moore. Fulton Superior Court. May 20, 1954.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant barber sought review of the judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which found the barber in violation of ordinances established by plaintiff city to regulate the trade of barbering.


OVERVIEW: The trade of barbering was regulated by the state code, which created the State Board of Barbering Examiners. The city enacted ordinances to further regulate the trade within the city. One city ordinance required a barber to obtain an annual permit from the city. The trial court found the barber in violation of that ordinance, but on appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the city ordinance, in attempting to regulate a trade already under state regulation, came within the constitutional inhibition that no special law was to be enacted in any case for which a provision had been made by an existing general law. The permit was not a mere occupation tax imposed by the city as a revenue measure. The city had no charter power to require payment of the fee in question, and the ordinance under which the fee was imposed was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which had been in favor of the city.

Walters v. State


No. 35215


Court of Appeals of Georgia


90 Ga. App. 360; 83 S.E.2d 48; 1954 Ga. App. LEXIS 714



July 8, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment for involuntary manslaughter. Before Judge Andrews. Fulton Superior Court. March 29, 1954.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled his demurrers to an indictment for involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his indictment for involuntary manslaughter by filing demurrers, which the trial court overruled. The court found that the indictment was well drawn, in that it correctly and distinctly set forth the offense of involuntary manslaughter in the commission of an unlawful act. The court held that the ordinances in question were clear and specific. The court found no merit in any of the demurrers and held that the trial court properly overruled them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1969 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Housing Authority of Savannah v. Savannah Iron & Wire Works, Inc.


No. 35077


Court of Appeals of Georgia


90 Ga. App. 150; 82 S.E.2d 244; 1954 Ga. App. LEXIS 656



May 12, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Before Judge Alexander, pro hac vice. Chatham Superior Court. January 4, 1954.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed suit against defendant, the Housing Authority of Savannah, seeking to determine an amount of just compensation for the taking of its property. The Housing Authority filed general and special demurrers to the petition. The Superior Court of Chatham County (Georgia) overruled the demurrers. The Housing Authority appealed.


OVERVIEW: The facts indicated that there was no extreme necessity and great urgency for the Housing Authority to exercise the right of eminent domain without first providing for just compensation for the property owner. Thus, the Housing Authority was without authority of law to enter into the estate of the property in issue without proper condemnation proceedings, and the property owner was not required, under the law, to surrender the possession of its estate without first requiring the Housing Authority to condemn the property under the proceedings provided for condemnation under Georgia law. However, both parties had an agreement by which the Housing Authority took possession of the property and the property owner moved out. The parties had a right to make the agreement, but the agreement left the amount of just compensation to be determined thereafter. The parties, however, could not agree on just compensation. The court held that the property owner set out a valid cause of action. The claim was based on the proposition that the Housing Authority took the property owner's land without paying adequate compensation therefor, contrary to Ga. Const. art. I, § III, para. I, O.C.G.A. § 2-301.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1970 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Bankers Life & Casualty Co. v. Cravey


No. 34990


Court of Appeals of Georgia


90 Ga. App. 113; 82 S.E.2d 150; 1954 Ga. App. LEXIS 649



May 11, 1954, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Before Judge Whitman. Fulton Superior Court. September 24, 1953.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company appealed orders from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) sustaining defendant's general demurrers and dismissing appellant's petition for a declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurance company petitioned the court for a declaratory judgment that it, while unlicensed, had the right to write insurance within the state. The court affirmed the dismissal of the first count of the petition, appellant's claim that the appellee Comptroller-General wrongfully refused appellant a license pre-petition, as the time had past and the question was moot. The court also affirmed the dismissal of appellant's second count, that it could continue to write insurance though unlicensed to do so in the state, as being speculative because there was not yet an actual controversy about appellants actions, and because the insurance licensing statute was clear and unambiguous, it needed no declaratory judgment to express its unmistakable mandate.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing appellants petition was affirmed because issues presented for declaratory judgment were moot, speculative, or unambiguous.

 

1971 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Wade v. Hopper


No. 34762


Court of Appeals of Georgia


89 Ga. App. 87; 78 S.E.2d 809; 1953 Ga. App. LEXIS 909



October 30, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Damages. Before Judge Anderson. Houston Superior Court. February 20, 1953.

This is a damage suit involving the collision of two motor vehicles driving in the same direction. Richard J. Hopper, plaintiff in the court below (the defendant in error here), we shall hereinafter call the plaintiff. Charles W. Wade we shall call the defendant. The plaintiff was driving in what is generally known as a house trailer, which the plaintiff himself was operating. The defendant's motor vehicle was a truck driven by an agent of Wade. The two vehicles were driving in the same direction, on U. S. Highway No. 41 in Houston County, Georgia. The defendant's truck was traveling behind the plaintiff's vehicle. The collision took place, according to the plaintiff's version, when the vehicle of Wade negligently attempted to pass the vehicle of the plaintiff. According to the defendant's contentions, the collision occurred when the plaintiff's vehicle was bumping and swerving on rough pavement and the house trailer came loose from the motor-vehicle portion of the house trailer, and the defendant's vehicle did not strike the plaintiff's vehicle but, on the contrary, the plaintiff's vehicle struck [***2] that of the defendant. The plaintiff and the defendant were nonresidents of the State of Georgia. The suit was brought in the Superior Court of Houston County.

To the petition, as amended, the defendant filed a plea to the jurisdiction and in bar subject to his general and special demurrers to the petition, and to the answer to the petition, and a cross-action embraced in the answer, respectively. The court overruled the plea to the jurisdiction and the demurrer. To these judgments the defendant filed exceptions pendente lite. A verdict for $ 7,500 was returned in favor of the plaintiff.
