The defendant filed an amended motion for new trial, which was denied. He assigns error, in exceptions pendente lite, on his pleas to the jurisdiction and in bar, on the exceptions pendente lite overruling his demurrer, and on the judgment denying his amended motion for new trial. We will discuss these questions in the order named.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver appealed from a decision of the Houston Superior Court (Georgia), which awarded damages to plaintiff driver following a vehicle collision of the parties while driving in the same direction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant objected to plaintiff's claim for loss of earnings for three months on the ground that the plaintiff did not allege whether a contract of employment was oral or written. The court found that despite conflict in the evidence, it was sufficient to support the damage award to plaintiff. The evidence permitted the jury to find against defendant under the law of comparative negligence. The court rejected defendant's claim that the charge to the jury on comparative negligence should have been amplified. Moreover, there was no error by the superior court in not charging the jury on the principle of impeachment with respect to a document offered and admitted for that purpose, because there was no appropriate written request to limit the use of the document. The court concluded that the damage award was not based upon a breach of contract; it was for the loss of earnings caused by the negligence of defendant. As a result, the tort claim for damages was not limited in the same fashion as damages sought under a contract, and the evidence by plaintiff as to lost wages was acceptable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

1972 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cherokee Brick & Tile Co.


No. 34735


Court of Appeals of Georgia


89 Ga. App. 235; 79 S.E.2d 322; 1953 Ga. App. LEXIS 943



October 14, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 18, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for refund of sales tax. Before Judge Atkinson. Bibb Superior Court. May 8, 1953.

Cherokee Brick & Tile Company, a corporation, brought an action against the State of Georgia and Charles D. Redwine as the State Revenue Commissioner for a refund of sales and use taxes. It alleged in its petition, as finally amended, substantially the following: The plaintiff is entitled to recover from the defendant $ 3,761.79, which is the sum of the sales taxes illegally collected from the plaintiff. The plaintiff was and is engaged in the business of making, fabricating, and processing brick and clay products. During the period from April 1, 1951, through January 31, 1952, the plaintiff used 771,397 thousand cubic feet of natural gas. On or about February 23, 1952, the plaintiff paid to the State Revenue Commissioner, under protest, $ 3,765.73, which was the tax, at the rate of three percent, on the entire 771,397 thousand cubic feet of gas used by the plaintiff during the period indicated, less an allowance for footage used pursuant to a contract with Macon Natural Gas Company, which contract was entered into prior to the passage of the [***2] Sales Tax Act. This allowance amounted to $ 164.07 and was three percent of the purchase price of the gas sold to the plaintiff pursuant to the contract. Of the total amount of gas used by the plaintiff for the indicated period, 775,000 cubic feet of such gas was used by the plaintiff for general heating purposes. The sales tax on this amount so used came to $ 3.94, which, when deducted from the amount of taxes paid, leaves $ 3,761.79, which is the amount of the refund sought. The plaintiff is not seeking to recover the tax of $ 3.94 on the gas used for general heating purposes. Of the 771,397 thousand cubic feet of gas used by the plaintiff, 770,622 thousand cubic feet of it was used by the plaintiff in its brick kilns in the following manner: The gas was ignited and the flaming gas burned over, around, and in direct contact with the raw clay and clay products being made by the plaintiff for sale to its customers and in such a manner that nothing intervened between the flaming gas and the clay and clay products. The effect of the flaming gas, burning at a temperature of from 2,000 to 2,100 degrees Fahrenheit, was to cause the raw clay to be changed through physical and chemical [***3] reactions so as to convert the raw clay into brick and clay products. The gas used in such manner was an industrial material used directly by the plaintiff in fabricating, converting, and processing articles of tangible personal property for resale, and the sale and use of such gas was, therefore, exempt from the Georgia Sales and Use Tax under section 3 (c) 2 of the Retailers and Consumers Sales and Use Tax Act (Ga. L., 1951, pp. 360, 365). The plaintiff at all times measured, and kept records of, the number of cubic feet of such gas used in its kilns, and the cost of that gas was a direct manufacturing cost and was so treated in the plaintiff's books and cost-accounting records. Under generally accepted principles of cost accounting, the treatment of such cost as a direct manufacturing cost was correct. On May 22, 1952, the plaintiff filed with the State Revenue Commissioner a claim for the refund of such tax of $ 2,761.79, a copy of which claim was attached to and made a part of the petition. On July 17, 1952, the Revenue Commissioner denied the claim for refund. If the act approved February 25, 1953 (Ga. L. 1953, pp. 194-195), should be construed as having any adverse effect [***4] upon the right of action of the plaintiff as set out in the petition, it would deprive the plaintiff of rights which were vested in it prior to the enactment of that law, and the law, so construed, would be unconstitutional and void as being in violation of article I, section III, paragraph II of the Georgia Constitution of 1945 (Code, Ann., § 2-302), which provides: "No bill of attainder, ex post facto law, retroactive law, or law impairing the obligation of contracts, or making irrevocable grant of special privileges or immunities shall be passed," in that the law so construed would be an ex post facto law, a retroactive law, and a law impairing the obligation of contracts.

The general and special demurrers of the defendants were overruled, and they have appealed to this court from that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and revenue commissioner, sought review of a judgment from the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled their general and special demurrers in plaintiff corporation's action for a refund of sales and use taxes.


OVERVIEW: The corporation brought an action against the state and the revenue commissioner for a refund of sales and use taxes on natural gas used in the business of making, fabricating, and processing brick and clay products. The trial court overruled the state and revenue commissioner's general and special demurrers. The court reversed this judgment. The court concluded that the trial court erred in overruling the general demurrer because the corporation was not entitled to a refund. The court found that the sale, use, and consumption of the gas was not exempt from taxation because it was not directly used in the manufacturing process of brick and clay products within the meaning of § 3(c)(2) of the Retailers and Consumers Sales and Use Tax Act, 1951 Ga. Laws 360.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that overruled the general and special demurrers of the state and the revenue commissioner in the action for a refund of sales and use taxes brought by the corporation.

 

1973 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Banks County v. Stark


No. 34535


Court of Appeals of Georgia


88 Ga. App. 368; 77 S.E.2d 33; 1953 Ga. App. LEXIS 1091



May 20, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 12, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Money rule. Before Judge Henry H. West, Presiding. Banks Superior Court. September 25, 1952.

Banks County, acting by its named Commissioners of Roads and Revenues, filed its petition in the Superior Court of Banks County against the Solicitor-General of the Piedmont Judicial Circuit, the Clerk of the Superior Court and a former Sheriff of Banks County, alleging that the respondents have, between December 31, 1944, and December 31, 1951, come into possession and retained sums totaling $ 30,404.47 (of which $ 4,250.97 came from sales of condemned automobiles, and the remainder from fines and forfeitures), belonging to the petitioner, and seeking a rule nisi requiring the respondent officers to show cause why such money should not be paid over to Banks County. The respondents filed separate demurrers, pursuant to which the plaintiff filed certain amendments. The Judge of the Superior Court of Banks County disqualified himself, and with the approval of counsel representing all parties the case was referred to the Judge of the Superior Court of the Western Circuit. On the date of the hearing, the respondents filed a joint demurrer based on [***2] several general grounds and numerous special grounds. This latter demurrer was a renewal also of all the grounds of the three separate demurrers filed on behalf of each of the respondents. On the hearing the trial court sustained the general demurrer without stating the particular ground or grounds thereof that were being sustained. He did, however, file a memorandum opinion setting forth his reasons for sustaining the general demurrer. He also provided in his order that the special demurrers were not determined.

On the judgment sustaining the general demurrer and dismissing the petition the plaintiff assigns error. The case was first carried to the Supreme Court on the theory that it was an equity case, and was transferred by the Supreme Court to this Court. See Rucker v. Stark, 209 Ga. 496, 74 S. E. 2d 74.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Banks County (Georgia), which dismissed the county's petition for a rule nisi requiring respondents, certain court officials and a former sheriff, to show cause why money from sales of condemned automobiles belonging to the county should not be paid over to the county. The county's right to any surplus of the fine and forfeiture fund was governed by O.C.G.A. § 27-2921 (Supp.).


OVERVIEW: The officials had collected money from the sale of condemned cars but had not turned any of the money over to the county. On appeal, the county argued that the trial court erred in sustaining a general demurrer to the petition because the petition did state a cause of action. The court agreed and reversed the dismissal. In doing so, the court held that the allegations constituted a cause of action under § 27-2921. Also, trial court was in error in its assumption that the county was not a proper party. Thus, the petition did not need an amendment naming a bank, acting as the county treasurer, as usee. The county, by amendment, merely perfected its petition so as to designate its proper official to receive the money on its behalf, but did not, as the trial court mistakenly concluded, step aside and make the county treasurer the party plaintiff in its stead. Further, the demurrer on the ground that the amendment to the petition converted the action into a mandamus proceeding was without merit. Also, the trial court had jurisdiction over the parties because the action could have been brought in the county of residence of either of the officers under O.C.G.A. § 2-4904.


OUTCOME: The dismissal was reversed.

 

1974 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Beazley v. De Kalb County


No. 34558


Court of Appeals of Georgia


87 Ga. App. 910; 75 S.E.2d 657; 1953 Ga. App. LEXIS 879



March 18, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Validation of revenue-anticipation certificates; from DeKalb Superior Court -- Judge Guess. December 30, 1952.

Pursuant to a resolution of the Commissioners of Roads and Revenues of DeKalb County under the Revenue Certificate Law of 1937, as amended, the State of Georgia, on November 25, 1952, filed a petition against DeKalb County, seeking a validation of certain revenue-anticipation certificates, in the sum of $ 12,000,000, sought to be issued by DeKalb County for the acquisition and construction of truck and railroad freight terminal facilities, the structures to contain about 2,000,000 square feet of storage space and to be located on a tract of land consisting of approximately 120 acres lying adjacent to a line of the Seaboard Railway and between two main highways in DeKalb County. Hearing of the rule nisi was set for December 8, 1952. The county filed an answer praying for judgment in favor of such validation. On December 8, the intervention of F. W. Beazley Sr., a warehouseman, also a citizen and taxpayer of DeKalb County, was filed, and the hearing on the rule nisi was continued until the morning of December 9. The intervenor moved [***2] for a continuance, which motion was overruled. After hearing evidence the trial court entered judgment in favor of validation of the revenue certificates. The intervenor thereafter filed his bill of exceptions directed to the Supreme Court, assigning error on the failure of the trial court to grant the continuance and on the judgment validating the certificates. The Supreme Court transferred the case to this court. The bill of exceptions assigns error as follows: (1) on the failure of the trial court to grant a continuance on motion of the intervenor; (2) because the resolution of the county commissioners, setting out the purposes for which the bonds are sought to be issued, is in violation of pertinent provisions of the Constitution of the State of Georgia; (3) that it is unconstitutional as tending to create a monopoly; and (4) because the evidence elicited on the hearing shows the project to be wholly unreasonable, unsound, and impracticable.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor warehouseman appealed an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) entering judgment validating the revenue certificates and denying the warehouseman's motion for a continuance in an action in which plaintiff Commissioners of Road and Revenues of DeKalb County (Georgia) requested the certificates from defendant DeKalb County (Georgia) to acquire and construct truck and railroad freight terminal facilities.


OVERVIEW: The intervenor argued that the trial court erred in failing to grant a continuance, that the resolution violated the Georgia Constitution and created a monopoly, and that the evidence showed that the project was unreasonable. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court had wide discretion in granting continuances and it did not abuse its discretion in denying the continuance. The statute authorized the building of a certain number of masonry structures and the court found that the structures were a terminal within the meaning of O.C.G.A. § 87-802(a)(2) even though the term was undefined. The word terminal was given the same significance as the other structures mentioned in the statute and it was evident that the general assembly intended the construction of something that produced revenue. The undertaking by DeKalb County was in keeping with the word terminal. The resolution did not have the effect of creating a monopoly and provided that all leases were to be for reasonable and fair rentals. The State made a prima facie case that the project was unreasonable and the intervenors did not carry the burden of presenting evidence to rebut that presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1975 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


No. 34338


Court of Appeals of Georgia


87 Ga. App. 244; 73 S.E.2d 502; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 658



November 19, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Violating liquor law; from Marion Superior Court -- Judge Fort. September 10, 1952.

During the October term, 1951, of the Superior Court of Marion County, the grand jury of that county returned an indictment against James V. Brown, Willie L. Johnson, Joe Talley, and Albert Benning, charging therein that the defendants in said State and county, on October 21, 1951, did unlawfully make, manufacture, and distill intoxicating, alcoholic, and illicit liquors. James V. Brown pleaded not guilty to said charge, and on April 29, 1952, was tried under said indictment for the offense of manufacturing illicit intoxicating liquor. The jury returned a verdict of guilty as charged. The defendant moved for a new trial on the general grounds, which motion the trial judge overruled. The bill of exceptions assigns error on the overruling of the motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Georgia), which entered a jury's verdict convicting him for unlawfully making, manufacturing, and distilling intoxicating alcoholic and illicit liquors in violation of O.C.G.A. § 58-206 and overruled his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Four law enforcement officers discovered a still at the end of a road in a dry county. Upon arresting the two men operating the still, the officers found 31 one-gallon cans, 150 gallons of whiskey, and a 1600-gallon still with an unusual burner. Defendant drove a car codefendant as a passenger with 126 one-gallon cans commonly used as whiskey containers towards the still. Two officers apprehended defendant 100 feet from the still and discovered on his person a bill for two pieces of pipe and some sketches of the unusual burner. Codefendant, who had run from the car, was apprehended and arrested. Defendant claimed that he had come to the still to buy whiskey. One operator who claimed that he owned the still had a sales ticket for gasoline sold on credit to defendant. The jury found defendant guilty of manufacturing whiskey. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction by finding that the jury was authorized from all the facts and circumstances that defendant and the operator with the sales receipt were acting with a common interest and purpose to unlawfully distill intoxicating liquor. By assisting in the operation of the still, defendant was guilty of making whiskey.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawfully distilling, manufacturing, or making alcoholic liquors.

 

1976 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Washburn v. Foster


No. 34214


Court of Appeals of Georgia


87 Ga. App. 132; 73 S.E.2d 240; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 630



October 24, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 8, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on bond; from Fulton Superior Court -- Judge Andrews. June 27, 1952.

E. E. Washburn brought suit against A. B. Foster, Sheriff of Fulton County, and the surety on his official bond, seeking to recover $ 10,000, which the plaintiff alleged he had deposited with the sheriff in order to obtain the release of one Fred Martin, who was in the custody of the sheriff on January 5, 1945, to answer a charge of misdemeanor in the Criminal Court of Fulton County. The petition alleges, in substance: that an appearance bond of $ 15,000 was required by the sheriff as bail for Martin, and he required in addition to an appearance bond, which was duly executed and approved, that $ 15,000 as a cash bond be turned over to him; that the plaintiff put up with the sheriff a cash bond of $ 10,000; that Martin appeared in court as required by said bond and was convicted on January 15, 1945, and after his conviction it was necessary for him to make a supersedeas bond, to be approved by the Clerk of the Criminal Court of Fulton County, in order to secure his release from the custody of the defendant sheriff pending a review of his case by the appellate courts [***2] of this State; that the plaintiff and others signed a certiorari or appeal bond for Martin, which was approved by the Clerk of the Superior Court of Polk County on February 1, 1945, and, on February 3, 1945, by the Clerk of the Criminal Court of Fulton County, who accepted the certiorari bond; that the plaintiff authorized the defendant Foster to pay the $ 10,000 to the Clerk of the Criminal Court of Fulton County, and the defendant Foster accepted the assignment and agreed to do so, but he failed to deliver the money to the Clerk of the Criminal Court of Fulton County and failed to pay the money to the plaintiff; that thereafter, on October 22, 1947, Martin was arrested to serve the sentence imposed and, as a result, the appeal bond was exonerated and became null and void. The prayers of the petition are for process and for judgment against the defendants for $ 10,000 with interest from the time the money was deposited with the defendant Foster.

The defendants demurred to the petition upon the ground that it failed to set out a cause of action against either of them, and that any claim the plaintiff might have had against them was barred by the statute of limitations. The trial [***3] judge sustained these grounds of demurrer, and the plaintiff excepted.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff payor brought suit against defendants, the sheriff and the surety on his official bond, seeking to recover money that the payor alleged he had deposited with the sheriff in order to obtain the release of an arrestee who was in the custody of the sheriff. Defendants demurred to the petition upon the ground that it failed to set out a cause of action against either of them. The trial court sustained the demurrer. The payor appealed.


OVERVIEW: An appearance bond was required by the sheriff as bail for the arrestee. In addition to an appearance bond, which was duly executed and approved, he required that a cash bond be turned over to him. The payor authorized the sheriff to pay the money to the Clerk of the Criminal Court. However, the sheriff failed to do so. The payor sought to recover the money turned over to the sheriff with interest. The court reversed the judgment. The court found that under the allegations of the petition, the sheriff at the time the suit was instituted held the money sued for as trustee for the payor, who was the legal owner of the same. The court held that the allegations of the petition were sufficient to show that the sheriff accepted the money under color of and by virtue of his office. Clearly, the sheriff had no right to require a cash bond or a deposit of money in lieu of bail or in addition to bail, and his action in so doing rendered him and his sureties liable on his official bond to anyone aggrieved. Therefore, the trial judge erred in sustaining the general demurrers.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining the demurrers filed by the sheriff and the sureties was reversed.

 

1977 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. v. Crist


No. 33981


Court of Appeals of Georgia


86 Ga. App. 584; 71 S.E.2d 910; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 1014



July 21, 1952 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at 86 Ga. App. 584 at 588.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of May 1, 1952, Reported at 86 Ga. App. 584.



DISPOSITION: Rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee filed a motion for rehearing in his appeal from a judgment of the trial court (Georgia). The employee contended that controlling case law was not given the proper effect in an action arising under the Workmen's Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The court reconsidered the present case and found that some of the language in the original opinion should be somewhat modified. The court ruled that it was a legal absurdity that the payment by a tortfeasor was a condition precedent to subrogation under O.C.G.A. § 114-403 (amend. 1937). Consequently, the court ruled that it was just as much a legal absurdity that payment by the tortfeasor was made a condition precedent to a proceeding by the employee against the tortfeasor. A recovery in that proceeding (which proceeding, after payment by the tortfeasor, was impossible) was made a condition precedent to an employer's, or an insurance carrier's, reducing the amount of compensation by the amount of "net damages recovered" in that proceeding. Therefore, if the employer, or the insurance carrier, in the present case was entitled to either reduce or to discontinue compensation, it was so by virtue of apply the principles stated in the cases cited in the original opinion in the present case, that the law as it existed prior to the invalid amendment of 1937 remained in full force. The court considered itself bound by those decisions, and adhered to the original judgment of reversal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the employee's motion.

 

1978 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Bohannon


No. 34077


Court of Appeals of Georgia


86 Ga. App. 236; 71 S.E.2d 440; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 922



May 20, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Adoption; from Emanuel Superior Court -- Judge Humphrey. March 3, 1952.

The plaintiffs in error filed a petition in the Superior Court of Emanuel County for the adoption of a two-year-old female child, the petition alleging that the mother had consented to such adoption and the father's whereabouts was unknown. The testimony of the plaintiffs revealed no reason why the child should not be adopted by them, but on the contrary showed that they had taken her from a destitute and unsuitable environment with the natural mother's full consent, had become attached to her, and were rearing her in an atmosphere of affection and economic independence. The only other testimony offered was that of the County Director of Public Welfare, who stated that the board had made an investigation and recommended against the adoption, which report was in the hands of the trial judge. The report was not offered in evidence, and the court, at the conclusion of the hearing, denied the petition and awarded the child to the State Department of Public Welfare for further disposition, upon which ruling of the court error is here assigned.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in error, prospective adoptive parents, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Emanuel County (Georgia), which denied their petition for adoption of a child and awarded the child to the Georgia State Department of Public Welfare for disposition. The trial court had a Department report, which recommended against the adoption; however the report was not admitted into evidence and was not made available to plaintiffs in error.


OVERVIEW: The testimony of plaintiffs in error revealed no reason why the child should not have been adopted by them. The only other testimony offered was that an investigation and recommendation against the adoption had been made by the Department. On appeal from the denial of their petition for adoption, plaintiffs in error argued that they should have had access to the Department report. However, the court concluded that there was no showing of what, if any, effort was made by plaintiffs in error to examine the report. O.C.G.A. § 74-419 required a written application to have been made that showed good cause for examination of the report. Plaintiffs in error contended that the trial court's consideration of the report violated their constitutional rights to due process. However, the court held that plaintiffs in error were not allowed to raise the issue for the first time on appeal. The court upheld the denial of the adoption petition and concluded that the trial court did not err by considering the report. O.C.G.A. § 74-413 included a mandatory provision that the trial court should consider the Department's recommendations in adoption proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which denied the petition for adoption and awarded the child to the Department for further disposition.

 

1979 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


No. 33909


Court of Appeals of Georgia


85 Ga. App. 298; 69 S.E.2d 206; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 720



January 31, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Uttering worthless check; from Thomasville City Court -- Judge Craigmiles. October 29, 1951.

C. L. Thompson Sr. was tried and convicted in the City Court of Thomasville on an accusation in two counts, charging him with uttering checks for $ 23.72 and $ 30.69 respectively, knowing that the maker or drawer did not have sufficient funds or credit with said bank for the payment thereof, with intent to defraud. It appeared on the trial of the case that the checks were signed, "Thompson Foundry and Machine Company, Payroll Account, by C. L. Thompson Sr., Vice President and Secretary and Treasurer." One of the checks was dated March 25, 1950, payable to the order of Pauling Hamilton, and the other dated April 14, 1950, payable to the same person; that each of the checks was issued at the conclusion of a week during which the payee had rendered services as an employee of Thompson Foundry and Machine Company, and was in payment of the services so rendered; that the checks were worthless, there not being in the bank funds sufficient to cover them; and that they had not subsequently been made good by the defendant or his company.

The jury returned a verdict of guilty. The defendant filed [***2] a motion for a new trial, which was subsequently amended by adding two special grounds, and the overruling of the motion is assigned as error.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the City Court of Thomasville (Georgia) of uttering worthless checks, there not being in the bank funds sufficient to cover them, and they subsequently had not been made good by defendant or his company. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was overruled. Defendant challenged his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the issue was whether defendant, who held three offices of a corporation which bore his name, including that of treasurer, issued the checks with intent to defraud, knowing that there were no funds in the drawee bank sufficient to cover them. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to form the basis of the conviction, as it appeared that the prosecutrix was an employee of the firm and had worked for it for stated intervals of time on credit; that her services for the intervals in question had been fully rendered before the checks were issued; and that the checks therefore represented items of account rather than checks given for a cash consideration. The court agreed with the argument and reversed defendant's conviction. The evidence failed to show an intent to defraud.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

 

1980 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Leggitt v. Allen


No. 33826


Court of Appeals of Georgia


85 Ga. App. 280; 69 S.E.2d 106; 1952 Ga. App. LEXIS 715



January 23, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Partition; from Dooly Superior Court -- Judge Gower. November 18, 1951.

Dempsey S. Brown, Bruce Brown, Mrs. O. L. Allen, and Mrs. Tom Harper applied to the superior court for partition of a described tract of land, containing 185.42 acres, more or less, and they alleged: that they were tenants in common with Willie H. Leggitt, Virginia Leggitt, and Woodrow W. Brown, each owning a one-seventh undivided interest in said land; that no provision had been made as to how said land was to be divided between the co-owners thereof; that the whole title to the said land was vested in the applicants and the named defendants as the sole surviving heirs at law of Amory C. Brown, their brother, who died intestate on October 21, 1948; that the applicants and the defendants are all sui juris and under no disabilities; that, on December 6, 1948, the court of ordinary entered an order declaring that no administration on the estate of Amory C. Brown was necessary; that, by virtue of said order, the applicants are estopped to administer the estate of their deceased brother for the purpose of making distribution among his heirs at law; that the interest of the cotenants in said land is unrepresented,  [***2] there being no one in active charge of the same; that, on October 28, 1947, Amory C. Brown encumbered said property with a deed to secure debt to Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company for a loan of $ 5000 principal, said deed providing for payments of $ 250 on November 1 of each year from 1948 to 1967, with interest at 4% per annum on the unpaid principal; that, on November 1, 1950, the unpaid principal will be $ 4500, and there will be due on said date a principal instalment of $ 250, and interest of $ 179.74; that the 1949 and 1950 taxes on said lands have not been paid and no return of the property has been made for these years; that no accounting of the rents and profits to the several cotenants has been made since the death of Amory C. Brown; that it is impossible to make a fair and equitable division of the property by metes and bounds by reason of the improvements thereon, and because the value of the entire property would be depreciated by such a division; that the applicants have given notice in writing at least twenty days before the date of this application of their intention to make the same, the notice having been duly served on Willie H. Leggitt, Virginia Leggitt, and [***3] Woodrow W. Brown; that the applicants present their title deeds for examination, and desire that the property be partitioned between the cotenants by a sale thereof by commissioners.

Virginia Leggitt and Willie H. Leggitt demurred to this application on the grounds: (1) that Code § 85-1511, under which the application was brought, is unconstitutional in that it deprived the demurrants of their rights to a trial by jury of the issue of whether a division in kind should be made; (2) that it was not alleged that Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company, holder of a paramount title to the property as evidenced by the alleged deed to secure debt, had been notified of the application or made a party thereto; (3) that the allegations as to the necessity for partition by sale are conclusions of the pleader unsupported by the facts alleged; and (4) that no cause of action is set forth. This demurrer was overruled, and the demurrants excepted pendente lite.

The court appointed three commissioners to ascertain whether a division by metes and bounds or by a sale of the lands and division of the proceeds would be more beneficial to the parties at interest. Virginia Leggitt and Willie H. Leggitt [***4] also objected to the return made by the commissioners, on the grounds: (1) that no lawful statutory partition could be made without joining Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company as the holder of an encumbrance superior to the rights of the applicants; and (2) traversing the return of the commissioners by alleging that a division in kind would be practicable, provided the rights of the insurance company were properly represented in the proceeding. These objections were overruled, and the objectors excepted pendente lite.

After reciting that the three commissioners appointed had made their report to the court that a fair and equitable division of the lands in question could not be made by metes and bounds, by reason of the improvements made thereon, that the value of the land would be depreciated by such a division, and that it would be impossible and impracticable to divide the land into separate equal tracts, and further recommending that the land be sold and the proceeds divided among the common owners as their interest might appear -- the court ordered that the described property by sold by the commissioners after advertisement; that the rights or interests of all parties be remitted [***5] to the proceeds arising from the sale, at which sale the parties were authorized to bid; that no deed would be made to the purchaser until the same should be confirmed by the court, at which time the parties interested were required to show cause why such confirmation should be granted or refused; that a copy of the order be mailed to Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company; and that its lien be paid off in full from the proceeds of the sale of the property. Viriginia Leggitt and Willie H. Leggitt excepted to this judgment, and assigned error thereon by reason of the antecedent rulings on their demurrer and their objections to the commissioners' return, and because the judgment was based upon fatally defective pleadings, without having made Mutual Benefit Life Insurance Company a party to the proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant co-tenants sought review of an order from the Dooly Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled defendants' demurrer and entered judgment in favor of plaintiff co-tenants on their petition seeking a partition of a certain tract of land.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed. The court determined that the petition showed that a recorded deed to secure debt was outstanding against the property sought to be partitioned, and the grantee of the deed had not been properly notified of the application for partition, which was required under O.C.G.A. § 85-1506. As such, the court held the petition should have been dismissed on the ground of the demurrer raising that point.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order overruling defendants' demurrer and granting plaintiffs' petition for partition of certain land.

 

1981 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Atlantic C. L. R. Co. v. Thomas


No. 33281


Court of Appeals of Georgia


83 Ga. App. 477; 64 S.E.2d 301; 1951 Ga. App. LEXIS 890



March 14, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Damages; from Ware Superior Court -- Judge Thomas. July 22, 1950.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant railroad challenged a decision of the Ware Superior Court (Georgia), which rendered a judgment against it and defendant taxicab owner in plaintiff passenger's action to recover damages for injuries he sustained when the owner's taxicab collided with the railroad's train. The trial court also overruled the railroad's amended motion for new trial. Judgment was rendered against defendants in the sum of $ 45,925.


OVERVIEW: In his suit, the passenger claimed that the joint and concurring negligence of defendants was the proximate cause of the passenger's injury and damage. The court found that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that when the passenger made out his prima facie case the burden shifted to the railroad. The charge required the railroad, not merely to introduce some evidence contrary to the acts of negligence testified to on behalf of the passenger, but to establish absolutely that the railroad, through its servants, exercised ordinary care and diligence. The railroad was also required to sustain its contention that the sole proximate cause of the passenger's injury was the negligence of the taxicab driver. The error was not cured by the subsequent charge because it assumed a situation where the passenger did make out a prima facie case and erroneously informed the jury in effect that in such circumstances the burden of proof shifted to the railroad. Further, the trial court erred in instructing the jury that recovery would be defeated only if the passenger failed to establish the negligence and that such negligence was the proximate cause of the injury complained of.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1982 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Kenimer v. State


No. 33216


Court of Appeals of Georgia


83 Ga. App. 264; 63 S.E.2d 280; 1951 Ga. App. LEXIS 847



January 27, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: Contempt; from Fulton Superior Court -- Judge Pharr. June 7, 1950.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on condition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of the Atlanta Judicial Circuit (Georgia), which granted a citation filed by the Solicitor-General of the Atlanta Judicial Circuit, acting for and in behalf of the State of Georgia, for contempt of court for violation of a previous order relative to defendant's child.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment against defendant finding him guilty and in contempt of court on each of 238 counts, and ordered that he be punished by imprisonment in the common jail of the county for five days on each count and that he pay a fine of $ 50 on each count. On appeal, the court affirmed. It rejected defendant's contention that the sentence imposed was excessive, unusual, and cruel. However, while the trial court was authorized to hold defendant guilty of 238 separate contempts, they were all based on only one culpable intent. As such, there was one contempt coupled with that culpable intent, and 237 other technical violations. The sentence of the trial court over and above the maximum fixed for the first offense for each of the remaining 237 technical violations totaling the equivalent of one other maximum offense was an abuse of judicial discretion and so cruel and unusual as to contravene Ga. Const. art. I, § 1, para. IX.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding defendant in contempt was affirmed on condition the trial court amend the judgment so as to delete from the sentence all imprisonment over and above 40 days in jail and all of the fines over and above the sum of $ 400.

 

1983 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ivy v. Ferguson


No. 33272


Court of Appeals of Georgia


82 Ga. App. 600; 62 S.E.2d 191; 1950 Ga. App. LEXIS 1171



October 31, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint; from Fulton Civil Court -- Judge McClelland. July 25, 1950.

J. D. Ferguson brought suit against C. N. Ivy in the Civil Court of Fulton County under the provisions of the Housing and Rent Act of 1947 as amended, seeking treble damages and alleging that he was a tenant of the defendant between the dates of November 8, 1947, through October, 1949; that he had paid to the defendant rental in the amount of $ 50 per month; that the maximum lawful rental effective during the above period as established by the Housing Expediter is $ 35 per month; that he is entitled to treble the amount of overcharge for a period of 23 1/2 months, or a total of $ 1057.50 plus attorney fees. There was no demurrer to the petition, nor did the defendant plead the bar of the statute of limitations. The evidence on the trial of the case showed that on October 5, 1949, the Office of the Housing Expediter passed an order decreasing the maximum rent allowable on such housing accommodations from $ 50 per month to $ 35 per month on the grounds stated in § 825.5 (c) (1) of the Controlled Housing Rent Regulations (Federal Register, September 17, 1949) as follows: "The maximum rent for housing accommodations [***2] . . is higher than the rent generally prevailing in the Defense Rental Area for comparable housing accommodations on the maximum rent date." This order was made retroactive to November 1, 1947, under the provisions of § 825.4 (e) providing in part as follows: "Where housing accommodations are changed on or after April 1, 1948, by a substantial increase or decrease in dwelling space, the maximum rent for the housing accommodations resulting from such change shall be the first rent charged after such change. . . And provided further, That the rent received for any rental period commencing on or after the date of the first renting shall be received subject to refund to the tenant of any amount in excess of the maximum rent which may later be fixed by an order under § 825.5 (c) (1) or (6). Such amount shall be refunded within 30 days after the date of the issuance of the order unless the refund is stayed in accordance with the provisions of Revised Rent Procedural Regulation 1 or Rent Procedural Regulation 2 (Part 840 of this chapter). The order entered by the Expediter shall fix the maximum rent retroactively to the date of first renting after such change."

The trial judge directed [***3] a verdict in favor of the plaintiff for treble damages in the amount of $ 1057.50. The defendant filed a motion for a new trial on the general grounds only, and the overruling of this motion is assigned as error.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant filed suit against defendant landlord under the provisions of the Housing and Rent Act of 1947, seeking treble damages and alleging that he had paid to the landlord monthly rentals over a nearly two-year period which were more than the maximum lawful rental rate as established by the Housing Expediter. The Fulton Civil Court (Georgia) directed a verdict in favor of the tenant for treble damages. The landlord appealed.


OVERVIEW: The order of decrease in the case involved § 825.4(e) of the Controlled Housing Rent Regulations. Thus, the first rent charged was the lawful maximum rent, subject to review by an area rent director, but until reviewed and fixed by him, it remained the legal rent. The monthly rent complained of, being the first rent charged after the housing accommodations had been improved, was the maximum rent prior to the date of the order of the area rent director reducing the maximum rent. As such, the landlord prior to the date of the order of the area rent director received no rent in excess of the maximum. Thus, the trial court erred in awarding the tenant treble damages. The court further held that the order complained of was void. It directed the landlord to refund rents collected by him from the tenant at a time when he was legally receiving the proper maximum rent, the first rent charged after the tenant took possession and after the landlord had made substantial improvements in the house, the landlord having occupied the same for more than 24 months prior to renting it to the tenant. Thus, the landlord did not waive his right to attack such an order in the instant action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1984 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Grant v. McKiernan


Nos. 32852, 32853


Court of Appeals of Georgia


82 Ga. App. 82; 60 S.E.2d 794; 1950 Ga. App. LEXIS 1057



July 7, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Damages; from Habersham Superior Court -- Judge Frankum. October 17, 1949.

This case arose out of a collision between two automobiles. Mrs. Mary Hinson McKiernan, whom we shall call the plaintiff, brought suit in Habersham Superior Court against Mrs. Naomi Grant, whom we shall call the defendant, for total damages of $ 5,000, $ 1,500 for damage to her automobile, and $ 3,500 for physical injuries and pain and suffering.

The petition alleged that as the plaintiff, on January 6, 1949, was driving her automobile on U. S. Highway No. 23, in a northerly direction, about one mile south of Gainesville, Ga., the defendant, who was driving in the opposite direction, suddenly and without warning turned the automobile she was driving to the left, crossed the center line of the highway and struck the plaintiff's automobile with such force that both automobiles were knocked off the road and onto the shoulder of the plaintiff's right-hand side of the road. As statutory negligence the plaintiff alleged the defendant's failure to turn her automobile to the right of the center of the highway when meeting the plaintiff's automobile, and her failure to give the "left-turn" signal. She also alleged [***2] common-law negligence of the defendant in failing to keep a lookout ahead, and in failing to grant her the right of way in that the impact occurred on the plaintiff's right-hand side of the highway. The petition set forth particulars of the damage to the plaintiff's automobile, and the extent, nature and result of her personal injuries.

The defendant filed her plea and answer in the nature of a cross-action and alleged the negligence of the plaintiff as the proximate cause of the collision. She admitted that the highway south of the point of the collision is practically straight for a distance of from six hundred to seven hundred feet, but that there is a hill, the top of which is from two hundred and ninety to three hundred feet south of the point of the collision, and that the top of this hill is the first point at which an automobile approaching from the south comes into view of one driving in a southerly direction at the place of the collision. She alleged the following statutory negligence of the plaintiff: Driving at a speed of from sixty to sixty-five miles an hour, and further alleged, "The collision occurred in a restricted school speed zone. The speed limit at this point [***3] was reduced to a rate of thirty-five miles per hour, and said restricted school speed zone was called to the attention of plaintiff and the general public by signs conspicuously posted on the highway some three hundred feet and six hundred feet south of the point of collision." She further alleged that after giving the "left-turn" signal, she slowed down her automobile and was in the act of turning across the highway into a by-road when she saw the plaintiff's automobile come over the top of the hill at an excessive speed and in the emergency thus created by the plaintiff she did not attempt to complete the turn, but stopped her automobile in a position protruding slightly across the center line of the highway, endeavoring thus to avoid being struck by the plaintiff's automobile.

She further alleged in paragraph 24: "Adjacent to the point of collision in said highway, there was a filling station on the west or plaintiff's left side of said highway, and that portion of the southbound traffic lane of said highway which remained unobstructed, the paved shoulder of the highway and concrete apron of said filling station afforded plaintiff with at least fifty feet of paved area, unobstructed [***4] and clear of traffic in which to turn to her left and pass the automobile operated by defendant, had she been driving her automobile at a lawful rate of speed and had had said automobile under control." In paragraph 25, she alleged: "Adjacent to the point of collision in said highway, there was a filling station on the east or plaintiff's right side of said highway, the shoulder of said highway and apron of said filling station having an all-weather surface, and that portion of the northbound traffic lane of said highway which remained unobstructed, the surface shoulder of the highway and surfaced apron of said filling station afforded plaintiff with from fifteen to twenty feet of surfaced area, unobstructed and clear of traffic in which to turn to her right and pass the automobile operated by defendant, had she been driving her automobile at a lawful rate of speed and had had said automobile under control."

Briefly summarized she alleged the following negligence of the plaintiff: Excessive rate of speed of from sixty to sixty-five miles an hour; driving in a restricted speed zone at such speed and in excess of thirty-five miles an hour; failure to maintain a proper lookout; failure [***5] to have her automobile under control; failure to turn either to her right or to her left as specified in paragraphs 24 and 25 quoted above; in failing to reduce the speed of her automobile under the circumstances alleged; in failing to sound her horn.

She further specified the damage done to her automobile by the impact of the plaintiff's car and the nature and extent of her personal injuries and prayed for judgment of $ 25,000 against the plaintiff.

The case was tried before a jury which returned a verdict of $ 1,000 for the plaintiff. The defendant filed her motion for new trial on the general grounds and amended by adding two special grounds assigning error on the charge. This motion was overruled and the plaintiff excepted and assigns this judgment as error in this court. The plaintiff in the court below excepts by cross-bill to a ruling of the court during the course of the trial, the particulars of which are given in the opinion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on the main bill of exceptions. Cross-bill dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver, an alleged tortfeasor, appealed a decision in favor of plaintiff complainant by the Superior Court of Habersham County (Georgia) in the complainant's negligence action against the driver. The driver, by cross-bill, excepted to the overruling of her motion for a new trial. The driver contended that it was the complainant who was negligent.


OVERVIEW: The complainant claimed that the car accident was caused by the driver's negligence. The driver claimed that it was the complainant's speeding that caused the car accident. The court held that the driver was liable. The driver waived the issue of the constitutionality of the law establishing a speed limit as having been unconstitutional under Ga. Const. art. III, § 1, para. 1, because the issue was not raised before the trial court at the earliest opportunity. The trial court did not have to charge the jury regarding the alleged negligence per se of the complainant for her having sped through a school zone under O.C.G.A. § 68-301(c) because neither party fell within the class protected by § 68-301(c). Thus, the mere fact that the complainant sped through the school zone did not mean that the complainant was negligent per se. While the trial court should have given a jury instruction that the driver acted reasonably under emergency circumstances, the error was harmless because the instruction would have helped the complainant, not the driver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on the main bill of exceptions and dismissed the cross-bill.

 

1985 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Kenimer v. State


No. 32908


Court of Appeals of Georgia


81 Ga. App. 437; 59 S.E.2d 296; 1950 Ga. App. LEXIS 914



April 14, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Contempt; from Fulton Superior Court -- Judge Pharr. December 3, 1949.

By virtue of an order passed by Judge Ralph H. Pharr, one of the judges of the superior court of the Atlanta Judicial Circuit, Hon. Paul Webb, Solicitor-General of said circuit filed a citation for contempt against Charles M. Kenimer Jr. The petition contained two hundred and thirty-eight counts. Preceding the first count were the following allegations: "On the 9th day of November, 1948, in the case of Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer, now Senter, vs. Charles M. Kenimer Jr., No. A-1255, Fulton Superior Court, the said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., filed an application and petition asking that he be awarded the custody of Betty Ann Kenimer, minor daughter of said parties, who was then in the lawful custody and possession of her mother, said Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer, now Senter, and residing with her mother in Clarke County, Georgia, all of which appears of record in said case. 2. Thereafter, as further appears of record in said case, the mother of said child filed a plea to the jurisdiction of the Superior Court of Fulton County, which plea was resisted by said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., and it was adjudged and determined [***2] in said court, His Honor Edgar E. Pomeroy, Judge thereof then and there presiding, on January 10, 1949, that the Superior Court of Fulton County had jurisdiction of the question of the custody of said child. 3. Thereafter, as further appears of record in said case, said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., filed in said court, on the 14th day of January, 1949, a motion and petition praying that a custodian be appointed for said child pending the litigation, which motion and petition duly and regularly came on for hearing before said court, His Honor Ralph H. Pharr, Judge thereof then and there presiding, on the 28th day of January, 1949, all as appears of record, said child then being, as aforesaid, in the lawful custody and possession of her said mother in Clarke County. 4. On said last mentioned hearing on January 28, 1949, upon said petition for the appointment of a custodian, the court entered an order and judgment thereon denying the application of said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., for an order changing the custody of said child from her said mother to a custodian named by the court, pending the determination of the question of permanent custody then in issue; further providing in said order [***3] that said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., be allowed to visit his said child on Saturday, February 5, 1949, and on alternate Saturdays thereafter between 9:00 a. m. and 4:30 p. m., and that said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., be allowed on said occasions to take said child in his automobile for such visits, provided on such occasions he was accompanied at all such times during such visits by either Dudley Cook, Esquire, or Durwood T. Pye, Esquire, his attorneys, who, as the court provided in said order, were charged, as officers of the court, with the trust in so accompanying said Kenimer of seeing that said child was returned to the home of her said mother by 4:30 p. m. on each day of visitation, said Kenimer being by said order given like right of visitation on Sunday, February 13, 1949, and on alternate Sundays thereafter under the conditions above stated; the court further providing in said order that the mother of the child was directed to have the child dressed and prepared to accompany her father on the day of each such visitation; all of which appears of record in said case. 5. On Saturday, February 5, 1949, the said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., accompanied by one of his said attorneys, Durwood [***4] T. Pye, Esquire, went to the home of the mother of said child in Clarke County, and carried the child from Clarke County to the home of the child's paternal grandparents, Mr. and Mrs. Charles M. Kenimer Sr., 557 St. Charles Avenue, Northeast, Atlanta, Fulton County, Georgia, for the first visit provided for under the terms of said order of January 28, 1949. 6. While at said 557 St. Charles Avenue, Atlanta, Fulton County, Georgia, on February 5, 1949, the said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., wilfully took, removed and spirited said child away, with the purpose and intention of removing the child beyond the jurisdictional limits of the State, and thereafter carried her beyond the jurisdictional limits of the State of Georgia, and beyond the jurisdictional limits of the United States of America, and failed and refused to return said child to the home of her mother in Clarke County, Georgia, on Saturday, February 5, 1949, as required by the order and judgment of said court so to do, and failed and refused to return said child to the home of the mother of the child and to the custody and possession of said mother, as required by the order of said court so to do, each and every day thereafter until [***5] and including October 1, 1949, all in violation of and in contempt of the orders, judgments and authority of said court, and for the purpose of preventing the effectual exercise of the jurisdiction of the court which he had invoked on the question of the custody of said child; contrary to and in flagrant disobedience of the authority, orders, judgments and jurisdiction of said court, and contrary to the good order, peace and dignity of the State. 7. Thereafter, said Superior Court of Fulton County, His Honor Ralph H. Pharr, Judge thereof presiding, conducted an investigation into the matters set forth in paragraph 6 above, witnesses being examined under oath, and on October 6, 1949, issued an order directing the Solicitor-General of the Atlanta Judicial Circuit to institute proceedings relating to the contempt of said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., which order is hereby attached. 8. Said Charles M. Kenimer Jr., is hereby, by the authority of the State, and the State's Solicitor-General, Atlanta Judicial Circuit, and by the authority of said court, charged and accused with the following separate and specific several acts of wilful contempt, each as set forth in the following counts, to wit:"  [***6] Count one is a follows: "Charles M. Kenimer Jr., is charged with contempt of the Superior Court of Fulton County in that he did, in Fulton County, Georgia, on February 5, 1949, the date herein alleged being an essential averment as to this transaction, take, remove and spirit away the child, Betty Ann Kenimer, from 577 St. Charles Avenue, Northeast, Atlanta, Fulton County, Georgia, and failed and refused thereafter on said day to return said child to the home of the mother of said child, Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer Senter, in Clarke County, Georgia, in violation of the order of this court of January 28, 1949, in said case, requiring him to so return said child to the custody of the mother; and in that he did on February 5, 1949, the date herein alleged being an essential averment as to this transaction, remove the child, Betty Ann Kenimer, without the jurisdictional limits of this State, for the purpose of interfering with and impeding the effective exercise of the jurisdiction of the Superior Court of Fulton County respecting the determination of the custody of said child invoked by him in said case of Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer, now Senter, vs. Charles M. Kenimer Jr., No. A-1255, Fulton [***7] Superior Court." The other two hundred and thirty-seven counts are the same as count one except that each deals with the failure to return the child on a specified day. In response to the citation the respondent filed the following answer: "1. The defendant admits all of paragraph 1, with the exception of the allegation that his daughter, Betty Ann Kenimer, was in the lawful possession and custody of her mother on the date named therein. He denies the allegation that Betty Ann Kenimer was in the lawful custody and possession of her mother. 2. Paragraph 2 is admitted. Answering this paragraph further, defendant says that the plea to the jurisdiction was decided adversely to Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer (now Senter) and that she had filed in this court exceptions pendente lite to the judgment of the court against her plea to the jurisdiction, and this question is subject to final determination if and when the case should ever reach an appellate court. 3. The defendant admits paragraph 3, with the exception that said child was then in the lawful custody and possession of her said mother, which he denies. 4. Paragraph 4 of plaintiff's petition is admitted. 5. Paragraph 5 of plaintiff's [***8] petition is admitted. 6. Paragraph 6 of plaintiff's petition is denied. 7. Paragraph 7 of plaintiff's petition is admitted. 8. Paragraph 8, and each count set forth therein is hereby denied. 9. This defendant says that on the 5th day of February, 1949, he removed his said child from the backyard of his parents' home in Atlanta, Georgia, and beyond the jurisdiction of the State of Georgia, and that on the 1st day of October, 1949 he returned to the State of Georgia, and that on the 2nd day of October, 1949 his attorneys called the Solicitor-General of Fulton County, Georgia, and that he surrendered himself and his daughter to the Solicitor-General at Augusta, Georgia on the night of October 2, 1949, and that on the 3rd day of October, 1949 he returned to Atlanta, Georgia in company with the Solicitor-General, and his daughter was delivered to her mother in the Fulton County court-house on said date. 10. This defendant denies that he is, or has been in contempt of court. He says that this case originated in this court on petition brought by Mrs. Muriel Moran Kenimer for divorce against him. Pending the final disposition of said case, this defendant and the said Muriel Moran Kenimer [***9] entered into a written agreement as to a settlement of alimony and the custody of their minor daughter, Betty Ann Kenimer. This written agreement was ordered filed as a part of the record in the case and is recorded in the clerk's office of this court in Minute Book 245, page 198, and when the final decree was entered in said case on September 18, 1947, his former wife was granted a divorce, his disabilities were removed and the written agreement as to alimony and the custody of the child was made a part of the final decree in said case. This final decree is recorded in Minute Book 51, page 57, in the clerk's office of this court. This agreement, which was made a part of the final decree in said case, provided in part as follows: 'It is further understood and agreed between the parties hereto that the custody of the said minor daughter, Betty Ann Kenimer, shall be vested jointly in both parties hereto, defendant paying all bills for the support, maintenance and education of said minor daughter, and in the event either or both of the parties hereto remarry, then it is agreeable that the court determine the custody of said minor daughter upon proper application of either party.' 11.  [***10] This defendant says that the only orders in this case after the original decree was the order signed by Judge Frank A. Hooper on the 28th day of December, 1948, which order is recorded in Minute Book 262, page 256, and the order signed by Judge Ralph H. Pharr on the 28th day of January, 1949, recorded in Minute Book 251, page 57, and that under the original decree of this court, the order of Judge Frank A. Hooper and the order of Judge Ralph H. Pharr, he was vested with joint control and custody of his minor daughter and that under these orders he had a right to remove her from the jurisdiction of this court. 12. Therefore, this defendant says that he is not guilty of contempt of this court and he here and now pleads not guilty under the petition for a rule and every count thereof." The respondent also filed the following demurrers: "1. The petition, on its face, shows that this defendant has not violated the order of the court dated January 28, 1949, signed by Judge Ralph H. Pharr and referred to in paragraph 4 of the petition, or of any other order of this court, for the reason that said order charged Dudley Cook and Durwood Pye with the responsibility of returning Betty Ann Kenimer [***11] to her mother on the dates of visitation set out in said order, and not this defendant. 2. The petition, on its face, shows that the alleged removal and keeping of Betty Ann Kenimer beyond the jurisdiction of this court is not and was not at any time contrary to the said order referred to in paragraph 4 of the petition on which the rule in this case is based. 3. Counts 2 to 238, inclusive, set forth no grounds as basis for contempt proceeding on the part of the court, for the reason that the petition on its face shows that if any contempt, as alleged, has been committed, the petition and the 238 counts contained therein charge the defendant with but one contemptuous act or the continuance of the same contemptuous act for the period of 238 consecutive days and, under the law, there can be no separate punishment for each continuous day. 4. The petition nowhere alleges that the defendant has actual notice of the court order alleged to have been violated, and is therefore fatally defective. 5. The petition as a whole and no count thereof sets forth any facts which would authorize this defendant to be adjudged in contempt of the court. 6. The petition, on its face, shows that if this [***12] defendant has committed any act amounting to contempt, it would be a civil contempt, and this defendant has now purged himself of any alleged civil contempt by having surrendered his daughter. 7. The petition and the prayer thereto seeks to induce the court to violate paragraph 9, section 1, article 1, of the Constitution which prohibits excessive fines and the infliction of cruel and unusual punishment. 8. Counts 2 to 238, inclusive, should be stricken for the reason that they show on their face that they are a repetition of the alleged acts in count 1, and show no new or separate ground for contempt." The respondent also filed a motion to quash the citation "for the reason that the said citation or information seeks to carve out of one alleged offense two hundred and thirty-eight offenses, which is contrary to law." The court on October 21, 1949, overruled the demurrers and the motion to quash, to which judgments no exceptions were taken. After hearing evidence the court adjudged the respondent in contempt for each of the two hundred and thirty-eight days and ordered that he be punished by imprisonment in jail for five days on each count and pay a fine of $ 50 on each count. Respondent [***13] filed a motion in arrest of judgment, as follows: "1. That the evidence adduced in the trial of said contempt proceeding, taken as a whole and construed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, establishes at most but a single offense of contempt as charged in the first count of said citation. 2. That all of the sentence imposed by the court in excess of a single term of imprisonment of twenty (20) days and a fine of two hundred dollars ($ 200) is null and void, and each and every day of imprisonment, and each and every dollar of fine imposed upon any count or counts of said citation numbered from two (2) to two hundred thirty-eight (238), inclusive, are null and void, contrary to law, and in contravention of the rights of this defendant under the Constitution and laws of the State of Georgia and of the United States of America." The motion in arrest was overruled on November 15, 1949, to which judgment exceptions pendente lite were filed. The respondent filed a motion for a new trial and an amendment thereto containing eleven grounds. The motion for a new trial as amended was overruled. The exceptions in this court are to all of the foregoing judgments of the judge except [***14] the judgments overruling the respondent's demurrers and motion to quash. The specific exceptions to the judgment imposing the fines and imprisonment are as follows: "(a) The judgment was in excess of the limits imposed by the Constitution and laws of Georgia for punishments for contempt; (b) the judgment was not supported by the evidence in that the evidence established at most but a single contempt terminated and not repeated, and the evidence did not therefore support the sentence imposed; (c) the judgment was so excessive as to be unreasonable and an abuse of judicial discretion; (d) said judgment imposes cruel and unusual punishment upon the defendant contrary to the Constitution and laws of the United States and of the State of Georgia."



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part, and reversed in part with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed exceptions to his convictions by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) for his convictions for 238 counts of contempt and his sentence of fines and imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of 238 counts of contempt for his actions in a child custody proceeding. The trial court sentenced defendant for each count of contempt, and defendant sought review by filing exceptions to the judgment. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for contempt, holding that the demurrers and the motion to quash raised the question of whether there was 1 count of contempt or 238; therefore, the ruling on that issue became the law of the case. Also, the court had jurisdiction over the parties and the subject matter. The court, however, reversed defendant's sentence, holding that the trial court's sentence of defendant on each count amounted to an aggregate sentence that constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. IX. The sentence included multiple and cumulative punishment for the same design.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for 238 counts of contempt but reversed his sentence. The court remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1986 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Boyett v. State


No. 32641


Court of Appeals of Georgia


81 Ga. App. 49; 57 S.E.2d 831; 1950 Ga. App. LEXIS 817



February 23, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Larceny; motion to withdraw plea of guilty; from Pierce Superior Court -- Judge Thomas. March 7, 1949.

J. R. Boyett and Eugene Moody filed, in the Superior Court of Pierce County, their motion to withdraw pleas of guilty entered for them to an accusation charging them with the offense of simple larceny (hog stealing), and to vacate and set aside the sentence and judgment of the court entered thereon for the reason that they were deprived of due process of law, and the benefit and right of counsel to represent them in entering the pleas of guilty. A rule nisi was issued setting the motion for hearing at a designated time and place. Upon the hearing, and after the introduction of evidence by both the applicants and the State, the prayers of the motion were overruled and the applicants appealed to the Supreme Court, which transferred the case to this court for determination since the writ of error presented no question requiring a construction of a constitutional provision nor attacked any statute as being unconstitutional. Boyett v. State, 205 Ga. 370 (53 S. E. 2d, 919).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court for Pierce County (Georgia), defendants were convicted of larceny for stealing a hog. Defendants filed a motion to withdraw their pleas of guilty and to vacate and set aside the sentence and judgment of the superior court. The superior court overruled the motion, and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon a call from a sheriff, a solicitor general went to the courthouse and told defendants that they were being charged with stealing a hog. The solicitor general asked defendants if they wished to enter a plea of guilty, and defendants indicated that they did. At a hearing on their motion to withdraw their guilty pleas and set aside the judgment of conviction, defendants adduced evidence related to the events that occurred prior to the killing of the hog, such as their arrests and their alleged confessions. Defendants contended that they never intended to enter pleas of guilty and that they did not steal the hog in question. Defendants alleged that they simply wished to resolve the matter and dispose of the case and that they did not realize what was occurring at the time they entered their pleas even though their appointed counsel was with them. On appeal, the court held that the superior court did not abuse its discretion in overruling defendants' motion; the superior court was the judge of defendants' credibility upon their motion, and it found that no officer of the superior court held out any representations or inducements to defendants at the time of their pleas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1987 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Nobles v. State


No. 32724


Court of Appeals of Georgia


81 Ga. App. 229; 58 S.E.2d 496; 1950 Ga. App. LEXIS 869



January 28, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Violating liquor law; from Early Superior Court -- Judge P. Z. Geer. August 20, 1949. (Application to Supreme Court for certiorari.)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an indictment, defendant was charged with possession of three pints of non-tax-paid whisky. Defendant filed a plea to the jurisdiction of the Superior Court of Early County (Georgia). The superior court struck the plea to the jurisdiction. After trial, the superior court entered judgment convicting defendant as charged. Following sentencing, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his plea to the jurisdiction of the superior court, defendant asserted there was an accusation for the same offense pending in the city court, and because the city court had first obtained jurisdiction over defendant and had concurrent jurisdiction of the offense with the superior court, the superior court should have taken no further cognizance of the indictment. On appeal, defendant contended the superior court erred in striking the plea to the jurisdiction. The court affirmed the judgment of convictions because the superior court had jurisdiction over both the subject matter and defendant's person, and thus, his plea to the jurisdiction was properly stricken.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of possession of three pints of non-tax-paid whisky.

 

1988 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Clayton


No. 32597


Court of Appeals of Georgia


80 Ga. App. 21; 55 S.E.2d 171; 1949 Ga. App. LEXIS 761



September 10, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint; from Floyd City Court -- Judge Kelly. April 29, 1949.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error winning gambler appealed a judgment of the Floyd City Court (Georgia) in favor of defendant in error losing gambler in the losing gambler's action to recover money lost in gambling transactions, and the losing gambler, citing 1949 Ga. Laws 1827, filed a motion to dismiss the writ of error.


OVERVIEW: The losing gambler argued that after the passage and approval of 1949 Ga. Laws 1827, providing for a trial by a jury of six in the trial court that tried the case, the trial court ceased to be a constitutional city court and a writ of error did not lie directly from that court to the court. The winning gambler contended on appeal that the verdict was not authorized by the evidence. The court denied the motion and affirmed the judgment. The court stated that under the constitutional provisions concerning the enactment of local laws and precedent applying them, the act providing for a trial by six jurors in the trial court was not in fact law at all and had never been so and the court had to deal with it accordingly, even though the court was powerless to declare the law unconstitutional. The court determined that the motion to dismiss the writ of error had to be denied. The court observed that it was within the province of the jury to resolve the conflicts in the evidence and that by the verdict those conflicts were resolved in favor of the losing gambler. The court stated that the verdict was authorized by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied the losing gambler's motion to dismiss the writ of error and affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the losing gambler in his action against the winning gambler to recover money lost in gambling transactions.

 

1989 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Findley v. Vidalia


No. 32243


Court of Appeals of Georgia


78 Ga. App. 581; 51 S.E.2d 542; 1949 Ga. App. LEXIS 933



January 8, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 11, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment; from Toombs Superior Court -- Judge Humphrey. May 3, 1948. (Application to Supreme Court for certiorari.)

C. W. Findley and others, citizens and taxpayers of the City of Vidalia, filed a petition in Toombs Superior Court in behalf of themselves and other citizens and taxpayers of said city, against the City of Vidalia and J. B. McCrary Company Inc., for a declaratory judgment and other relief.
